It emphasizes using AsyncPipe for templates, flattening streams with operators, ensuring proper cleanup with takeUntil and DestroyRef, implementing error handling, and combining RxJS with Angular signals for efficient state management, ultimately leading to future-proof and maintainable code in Angular 17/18.</p> <i>By Shrinivass Arunachalam Balasubramanian</i>

Title: "I'm Always In Pain": Dilbert Creator Scott Adams Announces He Has 'Same Cancer As Biden' And Has Months To Live
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">"I'm Always In Pain": Dilbert Creator Scott Adams Announces He Has 'Same Cancer As Biden' And Has Months To Live</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Scott Adams, the prolific cartoonist behind the 'Dilbert' comic who was canceled from newspapers nationwide for expressing conservative opinions, says <strong>he has the same type of aggressive cancer as former President Joe Biden and has just months to live.</strong></p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/image_92%2864%29_0.jpg?itok=Hu5cBTDK" data-link-option="0" href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/image_92%2864%29_0.jpg?itok=Hu5cBTDK"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="7e7d45f4-8ada-48bf-b412-203126345d94" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2864%29_0.jpg?itok=Hu5cBTDK" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Scott Adams, creator of the comic strip “Dilbert,” talks about his work at his studio in Dublin, Calif., on Oct. 26, 2006. AP Photo/Marcio Jose Sanchez</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>"I have the same cancer that Joe Biden has. I also have prostate cancer that has also spread to my bones," said the 67-year-old Adams during his May 19 "Coffee with Scott Adams" show on Rumble.</p>

<p>"My life expectancy is maybe this summer. I expect to be checking out from this domain sometime this summer."</p>

<p>Adams said that the cancer "is already intolerable."</p>

<p>"I can tell you that I don’t have good days. So if you are wondering, ‘Hey Scott, do you have any good days’? Nope. Nope. Every day is a nightmare and evening is even worse."</p>

<p>"<strong>I do have the ability to kind of get up for this part of the day, but I am in pain, and I’m always in pain</strong>. And the pain moves around to different parts of my body,” he said during the show. “I’ve been using a walker to walk for months now."</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Scott Adams gives solid words of wisdom after revealing his cancer diagnosis.<br /><br />
"I realize that for some of you, this is hitting you hard because you're hearing it for the first time."<br /><br />
"I have to say that everybody has to die, as far as I know. And it's kind of civilized that you… <a href="https://t.co/g5eRulqKH8">pic.twitter.com/g5eRulqKH8</a></p>
— Collin Rugg (@CollinRugg) <a href="https://twitter.com/CollinRugg/status/1924525515433800161?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 19, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>As the <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/dilbert-creator-scott-adams-says-he-has-same-cancer-as-biden-months-to-live-5860025?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge&src_src=partner&src_cmp=ZeroHedge"><em>Epoch Times</em></a> notes further, Adams said he wouldn’t go into the details about treatments he'd undergone. However, he did mention that<strong> he attempted to use medications such as ivermectin and fenbendazole to no effect.</strong></p>

<p>Adams had words of support for Biden and his family.</p>

<p>“I’d like to extend my respect and compassion and sympathy for the ex-president and his family, because <strong>they’re going to be going through an especially tough time</strong>,” he said.</p>

<div class="my-5">On Sunday, a Biden spokesperson confirmed that an aggressive form of prostate cancer had spread to the former president’s bones, meaning that it has metastasized. The American Cancer Society <a class="article-hover-class" href="https://www.cancer.org/cancer/types/prostate-cancer/detection-diagnosis-staging/survival-rates.html" target="_blank">says</a> that when a cancer metastasizes, the survival rate drops significantly.</div>

<p>“While this represents a more aggressive form of the disease, the cancer appears to be hormone-sensitive, which allows for effective management,” Biden’s office told media outlets. “<strong>The President and his family are reviewing treatment options with his physicians.</strong>”</p>

<p>In a post on X on Monday morning, Biden included a photo of himself and his wife Jill Biden, and wrote: “Cancer touches us all. Like so many of you, Jill and I have learned that we are strongest in the broken places. Thank you for lifting us up with love and support.”</p>

<p>Prostate cancers are graded for aggressiveness using what’s known as a Gleason score. The scores range from 6 to 10, with 8, 9, and 10 prostate cancers behaving more aggressively. Biden’s office said his score was 9, suggesting his cancer is among the most aggressive.</p>

<p><strong>A number of political leaders on both sides of the political aisle sent words of support to Biden after the announcement.</strong></p>

<p>Trump, a longtime political opponent, wrote on social media that he was saddened by the news and “we wish Joe a fast and successful recovery.”</p>

<p>Biden’s vice president, Kamala Harris, said on social media that she was keeping him in her family’s “hearts and prayers during this time.”</p>

<p>Adams launched “Dilbert” in 1989. Known for its satirical office humor, the comic at one point appeared in thousands of newspapers across multiple languages.</p>

<p>In 2023, the strip was dropped by many publications after Adams made controversial comments on race.</p>

<div class="my-5"><em>The Associated Press contributed to this report.</em></div>

      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-21T03:00:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 23:00</span>


Title: The 'Big, Beautiful Bill' Will "Massively" Increase Near-Term Deficits, Add $5 Trillilon In Debt
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">The 'Big, Beautiful Bill' Will "Massively" Increase Near-Term Deficits, Add $5 Trillilon In Debt</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Late last week, the <em><strong>Joint Committee on Taxation (JCT) </strong></em>released its preliminary score of the House Ways and Means Committee mark-up of the large budget reconciliation bill working its way through Congress, also known as Trump's "<strong><em>Big, Beautiful Bill</em></strong>" (<em><strong>BBB</strong></em>). And while the BBB is inching to passing through Congress - despite holdouts still remaining <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/im-still-no-battle-over-salt-holding-big-beautiful-bill-trump-demands-progress">especially over the size of the SALT deduction </a>- here is a snapshot of what is in the Bill, and how it will affect the US in the coming decade.</p>

<p>We start with a look at the fiscal policy focus of the BBB: Republicans' slim majority and their use of the budget reconciliation process are key influences on the composition of the fiscal policy-related legislation. That said, <strong>extending the expiring provisions of the TCJA should have sufficient support </strong>within the party for enactment. Additional tax cuts, such as a domestic manufacturing credit and not taxing tips, will be facilitated by the political viability of sufficient “pay-fors”. This will likely include watered-down versions of proposed IRA tax credit phase-outs and cuts to social spending programs.</p>

<p>So how does one quantify the impact of the BBB: as a reminder, the <strong><em>Ways and Means Committee </em></strong>is responsible for writing the main tax code portion of the bill. Relative to the CBO’s January 2025 baseline, the JCT estimated the mark up to <strong>increase deficits by $3.8trn over the next 10 years, </strong>with most of the deficit increase ($2.2trn) occurring over the next five years. Indeed, breaking the bill down even further, of the $1.9trn of total savings identified in the mark up, the majority ($1.2trn) is realized over the back half of the 10-year budget window.</p>

<p>It is also notable that <strong>$915bn of savings stem from capping individual deductions for state and local taxes </strong>– a figure that will come down in the final legislation given the pushback from many Republicans in high tax states. As a reminder, under current law, <strong>upon expiry of the Tax Cuts and Jobs Act, the cap on state on local deductions would go away leading to lower tax revenues </strong>(all else equal).</p>

<p>In addition, <strong>~$560bn of savings are generated through terminations or earlier phasing out of clean energy-related tax credits and another $116bn from “remedies against unfair foreign taxes”</strong> – both measures highly dependent on projections with very wide error bands and/or yet to be defined enforcement mechanisms.</p>

<p>As DB's Brett Ryan - who previously had made his own deficit claculations as a result of the "Big, Beautiful Bill"- writes, while the specific components of the additional tax cuts on top of the TCJA extension differed from what he had previously outlined, the JCT score of the Ways and Means mark-up was largely in line with the top-line deficit assumptions provided by Deutsche Bank. However, one key difference was 2025, where Ryan had assumed more of the additional tax cuts on top of the TCJA extension would be made retroactive to 2025. The first table below shows DB's prior estimates for deficit increases from tax and spending measures – excluding tariff revenue assumptions – compared to the latest JCT score of the Ways and Means mark up.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/ways%20and%20means.jpg?itok=ifIeJqtR" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/ways%20and%20means.jpg?itok=ifIeJqtR"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="e00b32f6-6a28-4978-8566-55f633426300" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="219" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/ways%20and%20means.jpg?itok=ifIeJqtR" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>To be sure, the JCT scoring of the Ways and Means Committee mark-up does not capture key elements of the fiscal outlook – namely, <strong>estimates of tariff revenues and potential spending increases. </strong>Recall that the Ways and Means Committee is responsible for the tax writing portion of the bill and JCT only scores revenue-related measures. Indeed, CBO scoring will likely provide a more complete picture on tariff revenue and spending as the legislative process moves forward. DB anticipates $300bn of increased spending on border and defense to be front loaded over the next couple of years as well as tariff revenues of around ~250bn per year.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/JCT%20score%201.jpg?itok=U2GpuZjN" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/JCT%20score%201.jpg?itok=U2GpuZjN"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="092cdc85-1305-425b-b95d-56cc3ba76c9a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="184" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/JCT%20score%201.jpg?itok=U2GpuZjN" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Risks are two-sided at this point. On the one hand, tariff revenues could be higher than currently penciled in, which assumes a ~15% tariff rate and only 2% import growth on average going forward. Conversely, the JCT score of the Ways and Means mark-up can be best thought of as a floor in terms of deficit increases over the 10-year budget window. The final legislative product is likely to show even less savings once the House and Senate “reconcile” their differences. </p>

<p>In short, as DB concludes, "<strong>there appears to be no serious effort at reining in historically-elevated deficits which remain on track to exceed over 6% of GDP in the coming years."</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/us%20deficit.jpg?itok=JyVUexAd" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/us%20deficit.jpg?itok=JyVUexAd"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="18c8d6cc-da53-4576-b8fd-1551730b11a0" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="313" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/us%20deficit.jpg?itok=JyVUexAd" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Extending on this, Morgan Stanley writes that the bank's base case is that a politically viable fiscal package will be composed of tax cut extensions with incremental tax cuts mostly offset by <em><strong>“pay-fors”. </strong></em>As such, the key driver of projected deficit expansion in 2026 is slowing economic growth and cost growth embedded in current policy, and this fiscal package would add modestly to that baseline. Accounting for potential tariff revenue as a mitigant, the bank expects a 2026 deficit of 7.1% of GDP (vs. 6.7% in 2025), an increase of ~$310 billion year on year...</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2026%20budget%20deficit.jpg?itok=42ow3gSL" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2026%20budget%20deficit.jpg?itok=42ow3gSL"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0a77161c-954b-4e60-aa33-fc0531b7516a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="277" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2026%20budget%20deficit.jpg?itok=42ow3gSL" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>... however, the bank also lays out a low and high deficit case, where the former leads to a $400BN increase in the deficit, while the latter "only" $200BN.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/MS%20alternate%20scenarios.jpg?itok=Pd_CInN0" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/MS%20alternate%20scenarios.jpg?itok=Pd_CInN0"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a33525ca-becd-440f-be53-a14b3c143bc5" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="279" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/MS%20alternate%20scenarios.jpg?itok=Pd_CInN0" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Taking a look at the bigger picture, keep in mind that the bulk of the BBB is just extending on the tax cuts from Trump 1.0, which is why if the bill does not pass, it would be equivalent to a huge tax hike, one which would lead to a lower budget deficit, but lead to an immediate recession as it would translate into a massive fiscal headwind. As such, while the BBB does lead to higher deficits, if largely due to secondary drivers such as the record $1.2 trillion in gross interest expense and economic slowdown, the <em><strong>Big Beautiful Bill </strong></em>will not result in much policy stimulus in 2026. Meanwhile, as Morgan Stanley notes, <strong>even assuming continuation of current policy, deficits should increase as the economy slows. </strong>And speaking of growth slowing down, MS expects this to happen due to a rise in uncertainty, trade policy, and restrictive immigration, but really it is a modest normalization of the runaway spending of the last two years of the Biden admin. In any case, softer economic growth means lower revenues and a higher deficit. In fact, <strong>only a third of the deficit increase for 2026 is due to discretionary fiscal policy in excess of TCJA extension.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/higher%20deficit%20but%20not%20much%20policy%20stimulus.jpg?itok=tR3oB2Ux" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/higher%20deficit%20but%20not%20much%20policy%20stimulus.jpg?itok=tR3oB2Ux"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a0eab03c-1982-43b5-ad9b-da4ac4a6b10b" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="272" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/higher%20deficit%20but%20not%20much%20policy%20stimulus.jpg?itok=tR3oB2Ux" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Finally, we look at the latest in-depth analysis from the Committee for a Responsible Federal Budget, which estimates the <em><strong>BBB </strong></em>would <strong>add $3.3 trillion to the debt including interest or $5.2 trillion if its temporary provisions are made permanent</strong>. In part because new borrowing is front-loaded and offsets are back-loaded, the bill would add massively to near-term deficits.</p>

<p>Unlike Morgan Stanley, the CRFB estimates the House bill would boost the FY 2027 deficit – the deficit in the first year the policies would be fully in effect – substantially more, <strong>by nearly $600 billion</strong>, or 1.8% of GDP. That’s the net effect of roughly $770 billion of new borrowing and only $180 billion of offsets.</p>

<p>The deficits boost represents a one-third increase in total projected deficits from $1.7 to $2.3 trillion – <strong>and a near doubling of the primary (non-interest) deficit. </strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/CRFB%201.jpg?itok=V35Am4dO" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/CRFB%201.jpg?itok=V35Am4dO"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="04a994e2-3652-42a9-b1d2-5826dd0a254a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="375" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/CRFB%201.jpg?itok=V35Am4dO" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>What is (perhaps not so) unique about the bill is that <strong>spending and tax cuts are front-loaded, </strong>while <strong>offsets are back-loaded, </strong>which means about 55% of the gross deficit increases – $2.8 trillion – would take place in the first half of the budget window. Meanwhile only 40% of the offsets – $970 billion – would accumulate over that period. As a result, <strong>70% </strong>of the non-interest borrowing would occur in the first five years.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/front%20loaded%20spending.jpg?itok=tGy7sl0Y" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/front%20loaded%20spending.jpg?itok=tGy7sl0Y"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="fd1a385e-8340-4e7a-be7d-128b3485c9fa" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="375" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/front%20loaded%20spending.jpg?itok=tGy7sl0Y" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The tax cut and spending increase provisions are front-loaded due to the use of “<a href="https://www.crfb.org/papers/playing-budget-rules-understanding-and-preventing-budget-gimmicks#gimmick10">arbitrary expirations”</a> designed to <a data-entity-substitution="canonical" data-entity-type="node" data-entity-uuid="d543f109-1f88-4f4f-9381-6466c6186311" href="https://www.crfb.org/blogs/permanent-ways-means-bill-could-add-53-trillion-deficits" title="Permanent Ways & Means Bill Could Add $5.3 Trillion to Deficits">limit reported costs</a>. A number of provisions – including the enhanced Child Tax Credit and standard deduction, no tax on tips and overtime, 100 percent bonus depreciation for equipment, and new ‘MAGA accounts’ – are scheduled to expire in 2028 or 2029. The bill also relies on one-time appropriations for defense and immigration, which must be obligated by 2029. And finally, the bill includes a large number of retroactive provisions that provide a one-time windfall for activities already undertaken.</p>

<p>Meanwhile, <strong>many of the offsets don’t begin or ramp up until late in the budget window. </strong>Medicaid work requirements, for example, save $300 billion through 2034 but do not take effect until 2028. In addition, while some of the Inflation Reduction Act (IRA) energy credits are repealed at the end of 2025, the most expensive ones only begin phasing out in a few years with some restrictions taking effect sooner.<strong> </strong>And the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (SNAP) state matching fund requirements do not start until 2028. </p>

<p>As a result of this mismatch and the sheer size of the bill’s deficit increases, the House bill would add to the deficit in every single year – with the possible exception of 2025 – even after the temporary provisions expire. <strong>But the largest deficit increases will take place very early in the budget window. </strong></p>

<p>The impact of tariffs aside, this additional acceleration in near-term borrowing could stoke inflation and push up interest rates well above current levels. And it may continue in the future if Congress extends expiring provisions and perhaps cancel some of the offsets.</p>

<p>But what is most amazing, is that even this massive increase in the US deficit in the coming years is <strong>still a remarkable slowdown to the debt and deficit avalanche observed during the Biden administration, </strong>where like the president himself the economy was kept on life support thanks to a cocktail of <em><u><strong>debt, debt and more debt</strong></u></em>, as we <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/economics/here-1-trillion-stealth-stimulus-behind-bidenomics">first explained in the summer of 2023</a>.</p>

<p>This is how Bank of America's <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/scl/fi/b8uy29f3wb4k8xvtz2gxo/BofA-Hartnett-The-Flow-Show-More-Jaw-Jaw-less-War-War-20250516.pdf?rlkey=epcv8zpugp76d7j8ip36ookkr&dl=0">Michael Hartnett explained </a>the "policy math" as one where <em>monetary and fiscal policy stimulus in 2024 was best in USA, but in 2025 it’s better in the Rest-of-World:</em></p>

<ul><li><strong>US Fed funds rate: </strong>2024 = down 100bps, 2025 = unchanged.</li>
	<li><strong>US government spending: </strong>past 12 months spending up huge $750bn (to $7.1tn), <strong>next 12 months spend down $50bn according to FY26 budget proposal.</strong></li>
	<li><strong>US tariffs: </strong>past 12 months import duties raised $85bn, next 12 months = $400-600bn (assuming 10-15% tariff rate), <strong>tariff taxation that falls on either foreign exporters, domestic importers, or domestic consumers.</strong></li>
	<li><strong>US tax cuts: </strong>next 12 months potentially start delivering $90bn per year in new tax cuts (rather than tax cut extensions); per CRFB current cost of “big, beautiful bill” next 10 years sees $0.2tn TCJA expansion of tax cuts + $0.7tn new tax cuts.</li>
	<li><strong>US policy stimulus crudely flipping from meaty 100bps cuts & $750bn fiscal stimulus to >$250bn fiscal contraction </strong>(spending cuts & tariff hikes before tax cuts) & zero rate cuts…big reason why US economy slows in 2025</li>
	<li>Meanwhile, <strong>China is in big fiscal stimulus mood, and NATO military expenditures: </strong>defense spending in Europe set to rise $100bn per annum; per US proposal all other 31 NATO countries to raise military spend to 5% of GDP by 2032= $700bn extra defense spending by NATO ex. US (currently US accounts for $0.9tn or 69% of the NATO military budget covering 32 members</li>
</ul><p>The final straw, of course, was last Friday's Moody's downgrade of the US Aaa rating - the final one - which took place on purpose just as the debate over the BBB hit a fever pitch. And speaking of Moody's, <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/markets/hell-pay-what-americas-debt-doomsday-looks">earlier today we explained </a>that the rating agency assumes the 2017 tax cuts are extended (unlike the last CBO semi-annual estimates), pushing debt and deficits much higher. The key Moody’s projections are:</p>

<ul><li><strong>Interest + mandatory spending will hit 78% of total federal outlays by 2035 </strong>(from 73% in 2024)</li>
	<li>Deficits will rise from 6.4% to <strong>9% of GDP by 2035</strong></li>
	<li><strong>Debt/GDP will hit 134% by 2035 (vs. 98% today)</strong></li>
</ul><p>And, as we also discussed earlier today in what America's Debt Doomsday looks like, both U.S. debt and deficits are about to truly take off. As shown in the chart below, while the baseline CBO projections don’t include the tax cut extension, one of their alternative scenarios of including it <strong>pushes debt/GDP above 200% of GDP over the decades ahead. </strong>The chart hardly needs any further commentary.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/debt%20to%20gdp_0.png?itok=z1KVk7ay" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/debt%20to%20gdp_0.png?itok=z1KVk7ay"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="38a443af-0af7-4738-9409-cf18632b21f3" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="177" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/debt%20to%20gdp_0.png?itok=z1KVk7ay" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>For anyone "shocked" by this development, don't be: back in February we warned readers, while praising the efforts of Elon Musk and DOGE, that while superficially cutting and streamlining government spending here and there will help, <strong>it will do nothing at all in the grand scheme of things to truly slash unsustainable government spending</strong>, which is dictated by Congress...</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">

— zerohedge (@zerohedge) <a href="https://twitter.com/zerohedge/status/1888351368785604870?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">February 8, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>... and when it comes to the debt trajectory set there, <strong>nothing will ever stop this train</strong>, or <a href="https://x.com/zerohedge/status/1888351368785604870">as we put it</a> in February:</p>

<blockquote>
<p>What Musk is doing in trying to streamline the govt is admirable but ultimately it will be Congress that decides the endgame.</p>

<p>And there things are as status quo as always.</p>
</blockquote>

<p>Three months later, a rather dejected Elon Musk observed the same thing when he said <strong>that the $2 trillion DOGE savings goal relies on the government</strong>, and that the "<em>Doge team has done incredible work, but the magnitude of the savings is proportionate to the support we get from Congress and from the executive branch of the government in general."</em></p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-partner="tweetdeck">

We are the advisors, and so we can, we can advise, and the progress we've… <a href="https://t.co/9RrK2rCxK2">pic.twitter.com/9RrK2rCxK2</a></p>

Title: Watch: Inside The Secret Illegal Antifa Headquarters
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Watch: Inside The Secret Illegal Antifa Headquarters</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>From Portland to Washington, D.C., and across Europe, the far-left extremist movement known as Antifa has unleashed years of orchestrated chaos driven by a radical, anti-capitalist agenda aimed at destabilizing the West. Now, for the first time, explosive undercover footage reveals life inside an illegal Antifa headquarters. </p>

<p><em><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PK4M2UOnN1M">YouTuber The Urban Legend</a></em> has released 30 minutes of explosive footage captured inside a secret and illegal Antifa headquarters in Manchester, United Kingdom.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-19_14-42-36.png?itok=TNVwg2Pp" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-19_14-42-36.png?itok=TNVwg2Pp"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="df37bb13-5678-4946-9cad-5650d315526b" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="284" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-19_14-42-36.png?itok=TNVwg2Pp" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The video reveals what appears to be a fully operational base—complete with stockpiles of food, racks of clothing, a sleeping area, and what looks like a makeshift revolutionary workshop for rioters. The footage offers a rare and disturbing glimpse into the behind-the-scenes of the revolutionary movement that has fueled unrest across the West. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-19_14-24-58.png?itok=eSFTGCHJ" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-19_14-24-58.png?itok=eSFTGCHJ"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="fe4c4aaa-e0d1-4bbc-b2f7-0d9a7c8eed51" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="230" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-19_14-24-58.png?itok=eSFTGCHJ" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

Title: Tulsi On Fauci's Role In Funding COVID Pandemic: "Is It Any Wonder He Sought A Preemptive Pardon?"
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Tulsi On Fauci's Role In Funding COVID Pandemic: "Is It Any Wonder He Sought A Preemptive Pardon?"</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://amgreatness.com/2025/05/14/tulsi-on-faucis-role-in-funding-covid-pandemic-is-it-any-wonder-he-sought-a-preemptive-pardon/"><em>Via American Greatness,</em></a></p>

<p><strong>Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard told Megyn Kelly that one reason Dr. Anthony Fauci sought a preemptive pardon before Joe Biden left the White House is because he lied under oath about helping fund the Covid-19 pandemic.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-22-18.jpg?itok=nzXylTlJ" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-22-18.jpg?itok=nzXylTlJ"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="178ac2ba-6149-469d-99b8-c8af289c8d95" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-22-18.jpg?itok=nzXylTlJ" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Gabbard recounted the numerous times that Fauci denied providing funding for gain-of-function research at the Wuhan Institute of Virology (WIV) while being questioned under oath by Sen. Rand Paul (R-KY).</p>

<p><em><strong>“So is it any wonder that he sought a preemptive pardon for anything during a certain period of time by President Biden before he left office,”</strong></em> Gabbard asked.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard CONFIRMS Anthony Fauci sought a preemptive pardon because he lied under oath about funding the Covid Pandemic<br /><br />
“Anthony Fauci helped fund the pandemic, things that he denied over and over and over to Senator Rand Paul's questioning”… <a href="https://t.co/hX5w82rLFs">pic.twitter.com/hX5w82rLFs</a></p>
— Wall Street Apes (@WallStreetApes) <a href="https://twitter.com/WallStreetApes/status/1922467544126079025?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>In the five years since the pandemic first began, the official story that the SARS-CoV-2 virus originated in a Wuhan wet market has been gradually walked back by members of the media, the intelligence community and the government.</p>

<p>The <a href="https://www.megynkelly.com/2025/03/17/megyn-kelly-slams-new-york-times-for-column-about-covid-lab-leak-theory/">most likely origin of the virus</a>, according to Kelly, is from a lab leak at the WIV where research was being performed on bat coronaviruses.</p>

<p>Earlier this month, the State Council Information Office of the People’s Republic of China <a href="http://english.scio.gov.cn/whitepapers/2025-04/30/content_117854036_3.html">released a white paper</a> claiming that the U.S. was trying to “shift the blame” for the virus to China, even as Chinese officials accused the U.S. of potentially being the origin point of the virus.</p>

<p>Gabbard said she has not yet read the white paper but maintains that the postmortem on the Covid-19 pandemic is far from over.</p>

<p>Gabbard explained,<em><strong> “I created… the Directors Initiative Group that is focused on investigating a number of the president’s top priorities and the things that the American people really deserve and want to know the truth about. The origins of COVID-19 is one of them… [and] a lot of the work that has been done is on covid.gov.”</strong></em></p>

<p>Gabbard has also teamed up with Director of the National Institutes of Health (NIH) Jay Bhattacharya to find the specific link between gain-of-function research being done by the Wuhan Lab and its partnership with U.S. nonprofit Ecohealth Alliance.</p>

<p><strong>If that link can be established, it would directly link Fauci, through Ecohealth Alliance, to funding the research that gave us Covid-19.</strong></p>

<p>This could open up new possibilities of criminal prosecution of Fauci at the state level as well as the possibility of Biden’s autopen-signed pardon being revoked.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-21T01:45:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 21:45</span>


Title: GOP Zeroes In On $40,000 SALT Cap
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">GOP Zeroes In On $40,000 SALT Cap</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong><em>Update (2135ET): </em></strong>Speaker Mike Johnson (R-LA) and moderate Republicans have tentatively agreed on a state and local tax (SALT) cap increase to <strong>$40,000 for individuals making $500,000 or less in income </strong>(no word on married couples) - with a 1% increase per year over 10 years, one source told <a href="https://thehill.com/homenews/house/5310851-republicans-salt-deal-trump-bill/?email=d2413eca022878438abcfb7cdd1787062bcf57ea&emaila=d6a773502826d0d710f0a2acdbd8d913&emailb=9cdd3d4e02ca37e04fbc498480a72da2eb4960dceaad0557609f9a2dfc0a1dde&utm_source=Sailthru&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=05.20.25%20CD%20Johnson"><em>The Hill</em></a> Tuesday night.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>That marks an increase from the $30,000 cap with a $400,000 income cap currently in the bill — a provision that SALT Caucus members vehemently rejected. The House Rules Committee is scheduled to convene at 1 a.m. Wednesday, during which the panel will consider changes to the bill.</em></p>

<p><em>While several members of the SALT Caucus are supportive of the plan, according to sources, Johnson will need to sell the proposal to hardline conservatives — including many in the House Freedom Caucus — who have been resistant to a significant hike to the deduction cap.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Members of the SALT Caucus met with Johnson into the evening - but upon leaving said that they did not yet have a 'firm' deal - though 'significant progress' had been made.</p>

<p>"We weren’t even in the same universe a couple of days ago. We’re on the same ballfield now," said Rep. Nick LaLota (R-NY).</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">THE SALT DEAL is coming together.<br /><br />
$40,000 deduction with a $500,000 cap. both the income and deduction limits escalate every year for a decade.<br /><br />
JOHNSON needs to sell this. but he will make the case that this is a better deal than what the SALTers were seeking. and, with rules…</p>
— Jake Sherman (@JakeSherman) <a href="https://twitter.com/JakeSherman/status/1925001999063318994?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 21, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>*  *  *</p>

<p>While Republicans hash out the details on the path to passing President Trump's 1,116-page 'Big, Beautiful Bill' - <strong>a key sticking point has emerged in regards to the state and local tax (SALT) deduction, </strong>which allows taxpayers who itemize to deduct state and local taxes (such as income and property taxes) from their federal taxable income. <strong>This primarily benefits rich taxpayers in high-tax states such as California, New York and New Jersey. </strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/trump_098e78_jpg_92.jpg?itok=-tattu1D" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/trump_098e78_jpg_92.jpg?itok=-tattu1D"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ca9451f7-f9b3-48d1-a369-f579c785a874" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/trump_098e78_jpg_92.jpg?itok=-tattu1D" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Tax writers on the House Ways and Means Committee have offered to raise the cap from its current $10,000 to $30,000 for joint filers making up to $400,000 per year - while Speaker Mike Johnson's most recent offer was a $40,000 cap for indivuduals / $80,000 for couples for four years at a $751,600 income limit.</p>

<p>The 'SALT Caucus,' meanwhile, are holding out for at least a $62,000 cap for individual filers, and $120,000 for couples before they'll vote 'yes' on the bill.</p>

<p>"I’m still a no on the Jason Smith number," said SALT Caucus member Rep. Nick LaLota (R-NY), referring to the $30,000 cap floated by House Ways and Means Chair Jason Smith (R-MO). "I hope that the president’s presence here today motivates everybody, especially my leadership, to give the SALT Caucus a number to which we could actually say yes."</p>

<p>The SALT cap is worth thousands of dollars in savings to millions of typically higher-income taxpayers who itemize vs. take the standard deduction. <strong>The cost to the rest of America for this would be around $1 trillion over the next decade, </strong>according to the Joint Committee on Taxation.</p>

<p>Before 2017, the average SALT deduction was approximately $13,000, before it was capped at $10,000. In 2022, nearly 10% of all taxpayers used a SALT deduction.</p>

<p><strong>Trump Drops F-Bomb</strong></p>

<p>During a Tuesday meeting with House Republicans, President Donald Trump pressured Republicans to fall in line behind the bill and get it done - asking moderate Republicans from blue states to give up their SALT battle, while warning members <strong>not to "fuck with Medicaid,"</strong> which some lawmakers have eyed for cuts.</p>

<p>"It’s not a question of holdouts. We have a tremendously unified party," Trump told reporters before the meeting. "There are some people who want a couple of things that maybe I don’t like or that they’re not going to get."</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>A White House official said <strong>Trump made clear in the meeting that he’s losing patience with all holdout factions of the conference, including the SALT Caucus and the House Freedom Caucus</strong>, and he insisted every Republican should vote “yes.”</em></p>

<p><em><strong>His main requests to the conference were not to let SALT impede the bill, a</strong>rguing Republicans can fight for SALT later on; not to touch Medicaid except for eliminating waste, fraud and abuse such as booting off those who entered the country illegally and instituting commonsense work requirements; and to stick together and get the bill done, a White House official told The Hill.</em></p>

<p><em>The president told lawmakers in the closed-door meeting to “let SALT go,” arguing concerns over the provision can’t get in the way of passing the bill. <strong>He signaled he was supportive of raising the SALT deduction from $10,000 to $30,000 for anyone making $400,000 or less</strong> — the proposal currently in the bill that members of the SALT Caucus have vocally rejected. -The Hill</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Trump's appearance at the nearly two-hour meeting didn't move the needle much, however.</p>

<p>"The president I don’t think convinced enough people that the bill is adequate the way it is," said Rep. Andy Harris (R-MD), chair of the House Freedom Caucus, whose members are among the loudest critics of the massive spending package. "I can’t support it the way it is right now," Harris added.</p>

<p><strong>Meanwhile, </strong>Rep. Mike Lawler (R-NY), a prominent SALT Caucus member, said "While I respect the president, I’m not budging on it."</p>

<p>So, it all comes down to SALT.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-21T01:34:55+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 21:34</span>


Title: Short Seller Challenges Jimmy Fallon To $1M Air Taxi Bet Before 2028 LA Olympics
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Short Seller Challenges Jimmy Fallon To $1M Air Taxi Bet Before 2028 LA Olympics</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Archer Aviation is set to serve as the <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/technology/los-angeles-announces-flying-taxis-visitors-no-car-olympics">official air taxi provider</a> for the 2028 Olympic and Paralympic Games in Los Angeles—a high-profile partnership that has boosted the startup's public visibility. However, skepticism mounts over whether Archer can deliver a fully operational flying taxi aircraft ahead of the Games.</p>

<p>Short seller Culper Research has released a scathing report on Archer Aviation, alleging that the startup has "systematically misled, deceived, or outright lied" investors about nearly every significant milestone tied to developing and testing its eVTOL aircraft, Midnight.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_14-18-20.png?itok=Pvdvw4gF" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_14-18-20.png?itok=Pvdvw4gF"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="1ac67824-afa4-431d-9455-8491e392db3b" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="347" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-20_14-18-20.png?itok=Pvdvw4gF" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>"Archer's misrepresentations have grown increasingly brazen as it attempts to conceal a far more deep-seated, and – in the Company's very own words – "potentially catastrophic" problem: Midnight's sham transition flight and underlying instability. In our view, Archer's continued promotion of near-term commercialization is not only premature, but reckless," Culper wrote in the report.</p>

<p>Culper claimed Midnight was "nowhere close to flying," and pointed out that Archer CEO Adam Goldstein has been more focused on running promotions, such as appearing on Jimmy Fallon's Tonight Show last Thursday. </p>

<p>"Our sources suggest, however, Archer paid millions for the airtime, in addition to Fallon's recent appearance at an Archer promotional event in NYC," the short seller wrote, adding, "We reached out to Fallon's agent who told us that we, too, could have Jimmy show up at our party (to say nothing of his appearance in a promotional video) for about $600,000, plus transportation."</p>

<p>On Tuesday morning, Culper wrote on X, "We are short Archer Aviation - and we're extending a $1 million wager to Jimmy Fallon, who has earned millions to promote Archer. Jimmy - if you truly believe in Archer, prove it."</p>

Title: How Hackers Can Control Your Phone With "Zero-Click" Attack
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">How Hackers Can Control Your Phone With "Zero-Click" Attack</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/article/how-hackers-can-control-your-phone-without-you-clicking-on-a-link-5853147?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge&src_src=partner&src_cmp=ZeroHedge">Authored by Chris Summers via The Epoch Times</a> (emphasis ours),</em></p>

<p>In 2025, most people are inseparable from their laptops and smartphones. With that familiarity has come a wariness of the dangers of clicking on unsolicited emails, SMS, or WhatsApp messages.</p>

<p><strong>But there is a growing menace called zero-click attacks, which have previously targeted only VIPs or the very wealthy because of their cost and sophistication.</strong></p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2860%29_0.jpg?itok=WwC7_dhw" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2860%29_0.jpg?itok=WwC7_dhw"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ecec102a-9eb3-4ef4-a95b-2072ddc174d0" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2860%29_0.jpg?itok=WwC7_dhw" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Illustration by The Epoch Times, Shutterstock</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p><strong>A zero-click attack is a cyberattack that hacks a device without the user clicking anything.</strong> It can happen just by receiving a message, call, or file. The attacker uses hidden flaws in apps or systems to take control of the device, with no action needed from the user and the user remains unaware of the attack.</p>

<p>“Although public awareness has increased recently, these attacks have steadily evolved over many years, becoming more frequent as smartphones and connected devices proliferated,” Nathan House, CEO of StationX, a UK-based cybersecurity training platform, told The Epoch Times.</p>

<p>“<strong>The key vulnerability is in the software, rather than the type of device, meaning any connected device with exploitable weaknesses could potentially be targeted,</strong>” he said.</p>

<p>Aras Nazarovas, an information security researcher at Cybernews, told The Epoch Times why <strong>zero-click attacks usually target VIPs,</strong> rather than ordinary individuals.</p>

<p>“S<strong>ince finding such zero-click exploits is difficult and expensive</strong>, most of the time such exploits are used to gain access to information from key figures, such as politicians or journalists in authoritarian regimes,” he said.</p>

<p>“They are often used in targeted campaigns. Using such exploits to steal money is rare.”</p>

<p>In June 2024, the BBC <a href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/articles/cl770d121gro">reported</a> that social media platform TikTok had admitted that a “very limited” number of accounts, including those of media outlet CNN, had been compromised.</p>

<p>While ByteDance, the owner of TikTok, did not confirm the nature of the hack, cybersecurity companies such as Kaspersky and Assured Intelligence <a href="https://www.kaspersky.co.uk/blog/tik-tok-vulnerability-zero-click/27685/">suggested</a> it stemmed from a zero-click exploit.</p>

<p>“<strong>The part that requires high levels of sophistication is finding bugs that allow such attacks and writing exploits for these bugs,</strong>” Nazarovas said.</p>

<p>“It has been a billion-dollar market for years, selling zero-click exploits and exploit chains. Some gray/dark market exploit brokers often offer $500,000 to $1 million for such exploit chains for popular devices and apps.”</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2861%29.jpg?itok=C3aGFy_P" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2861%29.jpg?itok=C3aGFy_P"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a2eb83ac-bb63-4271-b1ea-7ae61df51415" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2861%29.jpg?itok=C3aGFy_P" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>An attendee inspects the new iPhone 16 Pro Max during event at the Apple headquarters in Cupertino, Calif., on Sept. 9, 2024. Experts warn of a rise in zero-click attacks—cyberattacks that compromise devices without any user interaction. Justin Sullivan/Getty Images</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>Nazarovas added that while ordinary users have been hit in the past by zero-click ‘drive-by’ attacks. These are <a href="https://www.kaspersky.com/resource-center/definitions/drive-by-download#:~:text=A%20drive%2Dby%20download%20attack,to%20actively%20enable%20the%20attack.">attacks</a> that emerge after the unintentional installation of malicious software onto a device, often without the user even realizing it. They have become more infrequent with the growing gray market for such exploits.</p>

<p>House said zero-click exploits often seek out vulnerabilities in software and apps that are expensive to discover, which means the perpetrators are usually “nation-state actors or highly-funded groups.”</p>

<h2>Expanded Spyware Markets</h2>

<p>Although there have been recent innovations in AI that have made certain cyber crimes, such as voice-cloning or <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/article/the-terrifying-way-scammers-clone-your-voice-to-defraud-your-family-5849310">vishing</a>, more prevalent, Nazarovas says there is no evidence yet that it has increased the risk from zero-click attacks.</p>

<p><strong>House said people could use AI to “write zero-click exploit chains for people who would have otherwise lacked the time, experience, or knowledge to be able to discover and write such exploits.”</strong></p>

<p>But, he said, the increase in zero-click attacks in recent years, “stems mainly from expanded spyware markets and greater availability of sophisticated exploits, rather than directly from AI-driven techniques.”</p>

<p>He said <strong>zero-click attacks have existed for more than a decade</strong>, the most infamous of which was the Pegasus <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/world/the-international-spyware-scandal-runs-deeper-than-pegasus-3915927">spyware</a> affair.</p>

<p>In July 2021, The Guardian and 16 other media outlets published a series of articles, alleging that foreign governments used the Israeli-based NSO Group’s Pegasus software to surveil at least 180 journalists and numerous other targets around the world.</p>

<p>Alleged targets of Pegasus surveillance included French President Emmanuel Macron, Indian opposition leader Rahul Gandhi, and Washington Post writer Jamal Khashoggi, who was slain in Istanbul on Oct. 2, 2018.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2862%29_0.jpg?itok=Qh56tFMX" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2862%29_0.jpg?itok=Qh56tFMX"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="169b3954-f967-4bc0-ae3b-4d519aeca10b" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2862%29_0.jpg?itok=Qh56tFMX" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>A woman checks the website of Israel-made Pegasus spyware at an office in Nicosia, Cyprus, on July 21, 2021. Pegasus has been tied to several high-profile international zero-click attacks in recent years. Mario Goldman/AFP via Getty Images</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>In a <a href="https://www.nsogroup.com/Newses/following-the-publication-of-the-recent-article-by-forbidden-stories-we-wanted-to-directly-address-the-false-accusations-and-misleading-allegations-presented-there/">statement</a> at the time, NSO Group said, “As NSO has previously stated, our technology was not associated in any way with the heinous murder of Jamal Khashoggi.”</p>

<p>On May 6, a California jury <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/jury-awards-meta-168-million-in-whatsapp-spyware-case-5853795">awarded</a> WhatsApp’s parent company, Meta, $444,719 in compensatory damages and $167.3 million in punitive damages, in a privacy case against NSO Group.</p>

<p>The WhatsApp complaint was focused on the Pegasus spyware, which, according to the lawsuit, was developed “to be remotely installed and enable the remote access and control of information—including calls, messages, and location—on mobile devices using the Android, iOS, and BlackBerry operating systems.”</p>

<p>“<strong>While ordinary users can occasionally become collateral targets, attackers generally reserve these costly exploits for individuals whose information is especially valuable or sensitive,</strong>” Nazarovas said.</p>

<p>According to Nazarovas, corporations offer hackers ‘bug bounties’ to incentivize them to find these exploits and report them to the company, rather than selling them to a broker who then sells them on to parties who use them illegally.</p>

<p><em>Read the rest <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/article/how-hackers-can-control-your-phone-without-you-clicking-on-a-link-5853147?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge&src_src=partner&src_cmp=ZeroHedge"><strong>here...</strong></a></em></p>
</div>

Title: David Sacks' Lieutenant Explains The Real Reason Why Trump's AI Deal With UAE Is A Yuge Win For America
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">David Sacks' Lieutenant Explains The Real Reason Why Trump's AI Deal With UAE Is A Yuge Win For America</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p dir="ltr"><strong>Sriram Krishna</strong>n, Senior White House Policy Advisor on Artificial Intelligence, joined the Monday edition of TBPN to explain <strong>why the U.S.-UAE AI Partnership is a strategic victory for the United States in its race to lead AI development against China,</strong> a perspective largely (and unsurprisingly) overlooked by mainstream media.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">EXCLUSIVE: we asked <a href="https://twitter.com/sriramk?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@sriramk</a> to break down the $600B deal announced last week by <a href="https://twitter.com/WhiteHouse?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@WhiteHouse</a>.<br /><br />
"We signed the first AI acceleration partnership. There are 3 critical components to this deal."<br /><br />
"First, this represents a large investment in US data centers and US AI infrastructure.… <a href="https://t.co/cL4RUfgTRV">https://t.co/cL4RUfgTRV</a> <a href="https://t.co/8MRimP0rMg">pic.twitter.com/8MRimP0rMg</a></p>
— TBPN (@tbpn) <a href="https://twitter.com/tbpn/status/1924579955545088302?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 19, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>SRIRAM KRISHAN: We signed the first AI acceleration partnership. You guys probably read about in the press, but there are probably three important components that just, I wanted to have the technology brothers have the alpha and the have the first group on that. <strong>The most important part, the first part, is that this represents a large investment in U.S. data centers and U.S. AI infrastructure</strong>. So these countries will be investing in U.S. AI infrastructure. To make them as equal, if not larger, than the data centers and infrastructure they're building back home. So this means, obviously a large infusion of capital revenue to data centers here in America. </p>

<p>JORDI HAYS: <strong>That story was kind of lost. Right? I feel like a lot of the focus was on localized investment and infrastructure. </strong></p>

<p>JOHN COOGAN: To break it down in language that a venture capitalist could understand. This is something like what we're seeing with Stargate where <strong>there's a ton of capital forming and that's coming from SoftBank, but it's also coming from Middle Eastern investment funds and sovereign nations investing in American infrastructure.</strong> And then there's a whole host of companies that might come in the stack to actually build a new data center. Is that right?</p>

<p>SRIRAM KRISHAN: Exactly. You should be doing our talking points. I would say, look, <strong>these countries have AI ambitions, right? They want to buy American AI. They wanna buy our semiconductors.</strong> They want to buy our large language model. They want to use us. And so as a part of this deal, they're agreeing to a few things. The most important thing they're gonna agree to is that capital, like you mentioned, right? Like, and, and this is, by the way, net new. This is not part of any existing project. Sure. These net new deals will mean infrastructure being built out physically in the US.</p>

<p><strong>So for example, if they build out X megawatts of gigawatts of capacity, yep. This will mean the same X megawatts of gigawatts of capacity in the US, and this is an important point.</strong> Because some of the chatter has been, Hey, how does America maintain its lead? Well, one of the ways we maintain our lead is everything that is being built up by our allies. We get a matching deal back home. So that's probably the number one headline.</p>

<p>The second headline would be that <strong>the vast majority of the GPUs that are as a part of this deal, which is gonna be, say, hosted in the UAE, will be hosted, run, operated by American hyperscaler companies, right? </strong>And so, you probably know them all, right? These would be large American companies who. <strong>They will be running it, hosting it, maintaining, and this is actually important because this represents an expansion opportunity for all of our companies</strong>. This means they would get to win market share away from competition from other countries. And obviously there's a whole huge amount of revenue and ecosystem coming in. <strong>And so that's the second key point, the vast majority of the GPUs are going to be run by American companies, often by a lot of our friends in these large, uh, you know, hyperscaler companies.</strong></p>

<p>And the third point, and this is, again, something just lost in the chatter, is I'm sure you've heard questions about, <strong>Hey, how do we make sure these GPUs, you know, don't get to somebody they don't need to be</strong>. So there are rigorous security protocols in place, so every GPU gets shipped over. We are gonna make sure that, a., they can't be physically diverted. These are really large boxes. You can't hide them under your t-shirt or your tux and kind of stick them out the door<strong>. You can't really go George Clooney Oceans 11 on them. So one is there's going to be a large amount of physical verification and physical security protocols.</strong></p>

<p>The second is remote access. We are gonna make sure through these deals, through the framework that nobody who's not supposed to have access, especially from countries of concern, can get access.</p>

<p><strong>And so these three kinds of the core pillars, and here's why this event, right?</strong> And I think everybody in your audience who's like a technology person, a technology brother, or in the software world, here's why they'll understand it. What has history taught as a software industry? The company with the biggest network effect, the biggest ecosystem wins, right? <strong>We've all grown up with Microsoft. How did Microsoft win with the Windows and Office ecosystem? Think about this as the American AI ecosystem.</strong></p>

<p>We are getting these resource-rich countries who are critical allies in very interesting geopolitical places to basically adopt the American AI stack, right? Up and down. This means <strong>they are going to be part of our ecosystem for years and decades to come</strong>, and it essentially forms a shield from them ever adopting or using technology or working closely with some people that we don't want them to work with. In a way, I kind of think of this like a software ecosystem play, where we now have them tied to the American AI ecosystem.</p>

<p> </p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-21T00:30:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 20:30</span>


Title: Trump Unveils $175 Billion Plan For "Golden Dome" Missile Defense System
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Trump Unveils $175 Billion Plan For "Golden Dome" Missile Defense System</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em>By Ryan Morgan of <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/design-selected-for-golden-dome-missile-defense-plan-trump-announces-5860756?utm_source=Goodevening&src_src=Goodevening&utm_campaign=gv-2025-05-20&src_cmp=gv-2025-05-20&utm_medium=email&est=qST%2FIH4DR4fqwQ25iG0z%2FpHk7eNTzES3en88GqT0I3FBNW68Oe0qK3q%2BBDkd34k%2F3Q%3D%3D">Epoch Times</a></em></p>

<p>The Department of Defense has selected a design for President Donald Trump’s “Golden Dome” missile defense initiative, Trump announced on May 20.</p>

<p>“I’m pleased to announce that we have officially selected an architecture for this state-of-the-art system that will deploy next-generation technologies across the land, sea, and space, including space-based sensors and interceptors,” Trump told reporters at the White House.</p>

<p>In his first week in office, Trump signed an executive order directing the Department of Defense to devise a plan to implement his missile defense proposal.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/trump%20golden%20dome.jpg?itok=AjqGMpp6" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/trump%20golden%20dome.jpg?itok=AjqGMpp6"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="cecb6896-71b9-4bb6-b21d-b698946dea0e" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="331" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/trump%20golden%20dome.jpg?itok=AjqGMpp6" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>“It should be fully operational before the end of my term. So we'll have it done in about three years,” the president said.</p>

<p>Trump said the plan the Department of Defense has selected should cost about $175 billion to complete.</p>

<p>The plan will meld new technologies with existing U.S. missile defense systems.</p>

<p>Canada may also partner with the United States to help develop the improved missile defense shield, the president said. “Canada wants to be a part of it, which would be a fairly small expansion, but we'll work with them on pricing.”</p>

<p>In addition to new and improved space-based sensors and interceptors, Trump’s January executive order called for the Department of Defense to consider non-kinetic missile interception technologies such as lasers.</p>

<p>The order also tasked the department with examining methods and technologies for intercepting missile threats before they can launch, or in their initial boost phase.</p>

<p>Standing beside Trump during the Oval Office announcement, Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth noted the parallels between Trump’s missile defense proposal and the Strategic Defense Initiative put forth by President Ronald Reagan in the 1980s.</p>

<p>Reagan’s Strategic Defense Initiative included a number of aspirational missile defense concepts, and some critics referred to it as Reagan’s “Star Wars” proposal.</p>

<p>“President Reagan, 40 years ago, cast the vision for it. The technology wasn’t there. Now it is, and you’re following through,” Hegseth told the president.</p>

<p>Congressional Republicans have put forth a $150 billion supplemental military spending package, with about $25 billion set aside to kickstart the Golden Dome project. The $150 billion defense spending plan is one piece of a larger bill that Trump and his allies are hoping to pass through the reconciliation process, avoiding a potential Senate filibuster.</p>

<p>Trump expressed confidence that the reconciliation bill will pass.</p>

<p>“We’ve already spoken to everybody that we have to speak to,” he said.</p>

<p>“Everybody’s in line.”</p>

<p>Adding to his Golden Dome announcement on Tuesday, Trump named Gen. Michael Guetlein, vice chief of space operations for the U.S. Space Force, as the program manager for the project.</p>

<p>Trump said Guetlein is “one of the most respected people in the world, having to do with defense.”</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-21T00:05:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 20:05</span>


Title: US Veteran Freed From Venezuelan Prison After Latest Trump Diplomacy With Maduro
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">US Veteran Freed From Venezuelan Prison After Latest Trump Diplomacy With Maduro</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>In another diplomatic win for the Trump administration, a US Air Force veteran unlawfully imprisoned in Venezuela has been released on Tuesday, following secret talks with President Nicolás Maduro's representatives and Trump's special envoy Ric Grenell.</p>

<p>Joseph St. Clair, a 33-year-old combat-disabled veteran, had been <strong>detained in Venezuela since November</strong>, and was <strong>one of nine Americans declared by Washington as 'wrongfully detained'</strong>.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/stclair.jpg?itok=aqTlsnkE" data-link-option="0" href="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/inline-images/stclair.jpg?itok=aqTlsnkE"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="b9ba02c2-f8c4-4ddc-9a20-16f634782c69" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/stclair.jpg?itok=aqTlsnkE" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Images source: the St Clair family/770 KTTH Conservative Talk Radio</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p data-analytics-observe="off" data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmawu5flf00043b6mzbrw763r@published">"This news came suddenly, and we are still processing it — but we are overwhelmed with joy and gratitude," parents Scott and Patti St. Clair said.</p>

<p>Few initial details of his release or the terms of any possible deal or incentives offered Maduro have not been forthcoming. However, Grenell's talks with Venezuelan officials, reportedly in Antigua, <strong>likely focused on both oil and the migrant crisis</strong>.</p>

<p>Conservative news outlet <a href="https://www.newsmax.com/us/venezuela-ric-grenell-joseph-st-clair/2025/05/20/id/1211648/"><em>Newsmax</em></a> says it "learned that Grenell and Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent on Tuesday <strong>extended the waivers for U.S. companies' oil licenses in Venezuela by 60 days</strong>."</p>

<p>Clearly the Maduro government is ready to engage in top-level negotiations with Washington, in hopes for sanctions relief, and in return it is likely also willing to take back migrants.</p>

<p>According to background on St. Clair's arrest <a href="https://www.stripes.com/theaters/us/2025-05-06/veteran-service-member-venezuela-prison-detained-17704313.html">last year</a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Air Force veteran Joe St. Clair, their 33-year-old son, was <strong>traveling as a tourist near the Venezuelan border in October 2024 when he and a friend from Colombia were arrested by Venezuelan authorities, who transported them across the border to a Venezuelan prison,</strong> his family said. “We learned that Joe decided to take a trip near the border with one of his friends to visit [the friend’s] family member and got too close to the border and got abducted by the Venezuelan police,” Scott St. Clair explained. </em></p>

<p><em>“They were shaken down, questioned and searched. All their possessions were taken.” St. Clair said he was told the border is “fluid,” and that Venezuelan authorities detain Americans as bargaining chips to gain leverage against the U.S. to ease restrictions placed on the country. Joe is a linguist who served as a tech sergeant in the Air Force until 2019. He was honorably discharged after nine years of service, his family said.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>He had actually been deployed on four combat tours in Afghanistan. It's unclear whether the two travelers were inside Venezuelan territory or not.</p>

<p><em>This follows an initial big release of six Americans from Venezuela back in late January...</em></p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Venezuela frees 6 Americans after meeting between President Maduro and Trump’s envoy <a href="https://t.co/ZUdtlS1M20">https://t.co/ZUdtlS1M20</a> <a href="https://t.co/cc8nqhnc7O">pic.twitter.com/cc8nqhnc7O</a></p>
— New York Post (@nypost) <a href="https://twitter.com/nypost/status/1885496892391366905?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">February 1, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>St. Clair's parents had been very active in public lobbying for his freedom, calling on President Trump to <strong>"act now to save Joe and his fellow captives"</strong> at various events and rallies, including in D.C.</p>

<p>Trump has of late been emphasizing a foreign policy message of peace through strength and dealmaking and diplomacy, as opposed to the chaos of proxy wars and conflict.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-20T23:40:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 19:40</span>


Title: Australia's Unrealized Gains Tax Will Be A Lesson In Economic Suicide
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Australia's Unrealized Gains Tax Will Be A Lesson In Economic Suicide</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em>Submitted by <a href="https://quoththeraven.substack.com/p/australias-unrealized-gain-tax-plan">QTR's Fringe Finance</a></em></p>

<p>I’ve spent <a href="https://quoththeraven.substack.com/p/taxing-unrealized-gains-would-obliterate?utm_source=publication-search" rel="">years warning about the economic dangers</a> of policies that attempt to tax wealth before it’s realized, and now, like a slow-motion train wreck, we’re about to witness exactly why those warnings matter.</p>

<p>Australia’s <a href="https://www.skynews.com.au/business/financial-commentators-lash-labor-for-targeting-unrealised-capital-gains-in-super-warn-of-potential-extensions-to-other-assets/news-story/05ef5fc57f5c5f8e75ff405023693591" rel="">new move to tax unrealized capital gains</a> is one of the most reckless policy decisions I’ve ever seen — and keep in mind, I had front row seats to an “Inflation Reduction Act” that added more than $1 trillion in spending.</p>

<p>Taxing unrealized gains is equal parts <em>outright f*cking mathematically insane </em>and <em>cut-and-dry </em>authoritarian. And while I’m appalled by the policy itself, there’s a perverse part of me that’s almost glad it’s happening in Australia first—because the disastrous results will be on full display for the world to see.</p>

<p>Starting in July 2025, the Albanese government is set to debut its latest economic masterstroke: taxing imaginary money. That’s right—if you’ve got more than $3 million sitting in your superannuation, not only will you get slapped with a 30% tax, but it doesn’t even matter if you actually <em>made</em> any money.</p>

<p>Didn’t sell anything? Didn’t cash out? Never saw a cent? Tough luck—Big Brother took a peek at your account, saw some numbers went up, and decided you owe them a slice of your hypothetical success.</p>

<p>This isn’t just bending the rules of how taxation and private property works—it’s snapping them clean in half and using the pieces to beat your rights to death. For as long as economies have existed, the deal was simple: you sell an asset, you make a profit, and then you pay tax. You know, <em>after</em> you’ve actually made money. Because taxing cash that doesn’t exist yet is the kind of thing you expect from crackheads playing Monopoly, not national policy.</p>

<p>But here we are. Australia is now sprinting headfirst toward a future where you get billed for wealth that isn’t liquid, isn’t realized, and, if the market tanks tomorrow, might never even <em>exist</em>. It’s like being forced to pay income tax on the raise your boss <em>almost</em> gave you but didn’t, or footing the bill for the lottery jackpot on the billboard on the side of I-95 that you didn’t win.</p>

<p><a data-component-name="Image2ToDOM" href="https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F6f068c91-6664-46bd-b18c-40142e37a55b_1140x740.jpeg"
