fetchpriority="high" height="370" sizes="100vw" src="https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F6f068c91-6664-46bd-b18c-40142e37a55b_1140x740.jpeg" srcset="https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_424, c_limit, f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F6f068c91-6664-46bd-b18c-40142e37a55b_1140x740.jpeg 424w, https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_848, c_limit, f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F6f068c91-6664-46bd-b18c-40142e37a55b_1140x740.jpeg 848w, https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_1272, c_limit, f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F6f068c91-6664-46bd-b18c-40142e37a55b_1140x740.jpeg 1272w, https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_1456, c_limit, f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F6f068c91-6664-46bd-b18c-40142e37a55b_1140x740.jpeg 1456w" width="570" /></a></p>

<p>The fallout is not rocket science. People will be forced to liquidate assets—probably the wrong ones, at the worst possible time—just to scrape together enough <em>real</em> money to cover taxes on their <em>fake</em> money. Don’t have the cash lying around to pay that bill? Sounds like a <em>you</em> problem. Better start liquidating. And this isn’t just stocks we’re talking about. Real estate? Private businesses? Long-term investments you hold precisely because they’re supposed to be safe and stable? All fair game in a fire sale.</p>

<p>But wait, it gets even better. That $3 million threshold? It’s not even indexed to inflation. So as the value of money inevitably erodes, more and more regular people will find themselves dragged into this mess. It’s like the $1,200 handpay rule in Atlantic City and Las Vegas: it was created in the 1800s when $1,200 was enough to buy a private island, but as the purchasing power of the dollar has eroded, the rule has been kept in place, with the recalibration serving as way to monitor more and more transactions.</p>

<hr /><p>🔥 <strong>50% OFF FOR LIFE:</strong> Using this coupon entitles you to 50% off an annual subscription to <em>Fringe Finance </em>for life: <strong><a href="https://quoththeraven.substack.com/subscribe?coupon=d8097c43" rel="">Get 50% off forever</a></strong></p>

<hr /><p>With these unrealized gains, today it’s “only the rich,” but tomorrow it’s anyone who happened to save diligently or saw their house value rise because some genius decided to inflate the housing market even more.</p>

<p>So, if you’re sitting there thinking, “Well, that won’t affect me,” just wait. You might not be rich enough for the government’s shakedown <em>yet</em>, but thanks to inflation and asset bubbles, they’ll be at your door before you can say “unrealized gains.”</p>

<p>Back in 2024, I wrote <a href="https://quoththeraven.substack.com/p/taxing-unrealized-gains-would-obliterate?utm_source=publication-search" rel="">about why taxing unrealized gains</a> in the U.S. would be a catastrophic policy error. I warned that it would lead to forced sales, create liquidity crises, and punish anyone who dares to invest in volatile or long-term assets. Investors will avoid riskier assets that fluctuate in value because even a temporary increase could trigger a tax liability before they’ve seen any real return. This creates a chilling effect on investment in startups, innovation, and anything with a long payoff horizon.</p>

<p>It would also cause monstrous capital flight out of the U.S., as I’m guessing we’ll soon see in Australia.</p>

<p><a data-component-name="Image2ToDOM" href="https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fbf79d23e-83ff-46af-a5db-b0a6c44fc695_1146x728.jpeg" rel="" target="_blank"><img alt="" data-attrs="{"src":"https://substack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com/public/images/bf79d23e-83ff-46af-a5db-b0a6c44fc695_1146x728.jpeg","srcNoWatermark":null,"fullscreen":null,"imageSize":null,"height":728,"width":1146,"resizeWidth":null,"bytes":118658,"alt":null,"title":null,"type":"image/jpeg","href":null,"belowTheFold":true,"topImage":false,"internalRedirect":"https://quoththeraven.substack.com/i/163970180?img=https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fbf79d23e-83ff-46af-a5db-b0a6c44fc695_1146x728.jpeg","isProcessing":false,"align":null}" height="364" loading="lazy" sizes="100vw" f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fbf79d23e-83ff-46af-a5db-b0a6c44fc695_1146x728.jpeg 848w, https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_1272, c_limit, f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fbf79d23e-83ff-46af-a5db-b0a6c44fc695_1146x728.jpeg 1272w, https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/w_1456, c_limit, f_auto, q_auto:good, fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fbf79d23e-83ff-46af-a5db-b0a6c44fc695_1146x728.jpeg 1456w" width="570" /></a></p>

<p>Then there’s the bureaucratic nightmare of it all. Valuing assets for tax purposes every single year is an administrative quagmire. How do you accurately value a private business annually? How do you value collectibles, real estate, or other non-liquid assets in a way that’s fair and consistent? The government doesn’t have that kind of precision, and neither do most investors. What you end up with is a system riddled with errors, disputes, and compliance headaches for both taxpayers and the government.</p>

<p>Yet despite all these glaring problems, Australia is going through with it. And while I genuinely feel for the Australians who are about to suffer the consequences of this insanity, there’s also a silver lining. The rest of the world is watching. This is about to become the textbook case study in how not to run an economy. If you want to see what happens when a government taxes phantom wealth and forces people to pay cash they don’t have, just keep your eyes on Australia over the next few years.</p>

<p>My prediction? You’ll see a mass exodus of capital. People will restructure their investments, move funds offshore, and pull money out of productive sectors of the economy. You’ll see market volatility as investors dump assets to avoid future tax liabilities. You’ll watch the property market distort as people chase after tax shelters. And ultimately, you’ll see economic growth grind down under the weight of a policy that punishes investment and rewards government overreach.</p>

<p>In a strange way, I’m thankful this is happening—not because I support it, but because it will stand as a stark, irrefutable warning to every other country foolish enough to consider the same policy. The Australian government is about to run a live experiment in economic self-sabotage, and the results will be undeniable. In my opinion, after this plays out, no serious policymaker with a shred of economic literacy will be able to look at the forthcoming outcomes and still argue that taxing unrealized gains is anything but a disastrously stupid idea.</p>

Title: Experts Warn Trump's "Big Beautiful Bill" Could Codify Big Land Grabs 
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Experts Warn Trump's "Big Beautiful Bill" Could Codify Big Land Grabs </span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Agricultural advocates and lawmakers are <strong>sounding the alarm this week</strong>, as section <a href="https://docs.house.gov/meetings/IF/IF00/20250513/118261/BILLS-119CommitteePrintSubtitleApp-U1.pdf">41001 of the proposed Budget Reconciliation Act</a> (the Big Beautiful Bill) <strong>contains language</strong> that would centralize local authority to the federal government regarding <strong>land use and land expropriation</strong>.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Property rights are under attack again.<br /><br />
A House Energy and Commerce proposal for the budget reconciliation bill would override state laws that protect landowners’ private property rights from being taken by Green New Deal carbon sequestration pipeline companies.<br /><br />
The proposal… <a href="https://t.co/FWKqiaVwbe">https://t.co/FWKqiaVwbe</a> <a href="https://t.co/wakjgv3d4D">pic.twitter.com/wakjgv3d4D</a></p>
— Speaker Jon Hansen (@SpeakerHansen) <a href="https://twitter.com/SpeakerHansen/status/1922622938538541395?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 14, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Beginning under the Biden administration's Federal Plan for Equitable Long-Term Recovery and Resilience (ELTRR), funding from the Inflation Reduction Act (IRA) and the USDA credit line, known as the Commodities Credit Corporation (CCC), were allocated to ideologically aligned Non-Governmental Organizations (NGOs). </p>

<p>Using contract law, NGOs were <a href="https://emeraldcities.org/j40playbook/">then tasked with</a> creating a <a href="https://www.csis.org/analysis/voluntary-carbon-markets-review-global-initiatives-and-evolving-models">carbon market</a> and <a href="https://www.moreheadcitync.org/AgendaCenter/ViewFile/Item/2102?fileID=9002">strategic buyout programs</a> for federally funded public-private land acquisitions—entered into as an agreement structure with local municipalities—to <a href="https://brownstone.org/articles/america-the-titanic-policy-recommendations/">facilitate the Green New Deal.</a>  </p>

<p><strong>Carbon capture has captured Farm Credit</strong>, and could soon <strong>capture lands across America's Heartland</strong>.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/unnamed-2_31.png?itok=bxFtzAEN" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/unnamed-2_31.png?itok=bxFtzAEN"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="840737a0-8a9b-4e7a-8dcf-b755f664d3e4" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="288" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/unnamed-2_31.png?itok=bxFtzAEN" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Amid a flurry of administrative rule changes, the Biden administration <a href="https://www.usda.gov/about-usda/news/press-releases/2023/05/16/biden-harris-administration-makes-historic-11-billion-investment-advance-clean-energy-across-rural">prioritized government-backed Farm Credit</a> lending for <a href="https://farmcredit.com/stories/pedernales-electric-cooperative/">rural utilities</a>. Reallocating parts of the USDA's Rural Development budget, the Biden administration attracted "eligible organizations" to "invest in renewable energy infrastructure and zero-emission systems," to "significantly reduce greenhouse gas emissions."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-10-42.png?itok=CmJBs4dF" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-10-42.png?itok=CmJBs4dF"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="4ee8562b-7ad5-4457-877b-b39cb19f069e" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="739" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-10-42.png?itok=CmJBs4dF" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Simultaneously, as part of the ELTRR's "<a href="https://bidenwhitehouse.archives.gov/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/Full-PREPARE-Plan.pdf">whole-of-government</a>" approach; the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) <a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2024/05/09/2024-09233/new-source-performance-standards-for-greenhouse-gas-emissions-from-new-modified-and-reconstructed">exempted</a> certain "Green Energy" infrastructure projects, such as solar and carbon capture from Environmental Impact Studies, while 45Q tax credits promised billions in government subsidies, and agencies <a href="https://www.federalregister.gov/d/2024-08736/page-36910">eased land acquisition</a> regulations for "Federally Assisted Programs."</p>

<p>This coalescence created a proverbial gold rush. Suddenly, private equity firms like <strong>Blackrock and Vanguard</strong> quickly began backing projects for <a href="https://www.desmog.com/2023/05/31/princeton-maps-ccs-us-plans-co2-pipeline-buildout/">Carbon Sequestration infrastructure</a>, such as the 2,500-mile C02 pipeline project spanning five states. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-11-09.png?itok=oF_FactX" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-11-09.png?itok=oF_FactX"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="302145e8-9bf6-4ec7-8c37-92df74920890" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="604" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-11-09.png?itok=oF_FactX" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Now, as Congress works to immediately halt IRA funding and reign-in the <strong>"whole-of-government," state lawmakers and agricultural advocates warn the cure could exacerbate the disease.</strong></p>

<p><strong>According to Amanda Radke</strong>, a fifth-generation cattle rancher who has fought against giving private corporations eminent domain power in South Dakota, "this proposal would open the door for federal overreach and eminent domain abuse, especially with the $10 million price tag to fast-track these projects."</p>

<p>"<strong>I'm deeply concerned that the current proposal for the budget reconciliation bill will grant centralized federal authority over the permitting of carbon dioxide pipelines</strong>," Radke said. "<strong>This Green New Deal has held America hostage for far too long, and it's time for Congress to cut ties with this boondoggle once and for all. Landowners across the nation are calling for Congress to cut wasteful spending, halt the subsidies of the IRA like the 45Q tax credit, and protect our private property rights</strong>." </p>

<p>S.D. landowners have also found a fierce advocate in <a href="https://www.thedakotascout.com/p/carbon-pipeline-opponents-win-key">Speaker of the House, Rep. Jon Hansen</a>. Hansen, who is now running for Governor,  and running-mate Rep. Karla Lems, have <a href="https://southdakotasearchlight.com/2025/03/03/carbon-pipeline-eminent-domain-ban-advances-sd-legislature-compromise-bill-gutted/">led the charge to protect private property rights</a> in the State of South Dakota. </p>

<p>However, according to Hansen, these hard-won efforts could now be a moot point. </p>

<p>"<strong>President Trump has made it very clear that he wants to end the Green New Deal scam</strong>. In spite of that, politicians in Washington are trying to sneak a provision deep in the budget bill that would override the hard-fought protections that we have put into place for farmers, ranchers, and land owners in South Dakota," Hansen told ZeroHedge.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-11-34.png?itok=i3wZbEs4" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-11-34.png?itok=i3wZbEs4"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="41e8bd20-fb1d-4de3-9eae-7e67752c82c0" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="629" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-20_13-11-34.png?itok=i3wZbEs4" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>While GOP leadership has made quiet promises that the bill will be amended, an updated draft has yet to materialize prior to Wednesday's vote. A fact that isn't sitting well with Radke or Hansen.</p>

<p>"<strong>While we've been told this language would be cut on Wednesday morning</strong>, farmers and ranchers are waiting for reassurance from Congressional leaders that our land is, in fact, not for sale to the highest bidder," Radke said. </p>

<p>For Hansen, however, anything short of killing this section, <strong>will be considered an absolute failure</strong>.</p>

<p>"<u><strong>All members of Congress must reject this proposal</strong></u>," Hansen said. "Anything short of killing the land grab proposal and totally defunding the 45Q tax credit is an absolute failure to deliver on ending the green new deal scam and a failure to defend our peoples' constitutional rights."</p>
</div>

Title: Israel Preparing Possible Preemptive Attack On Iranian Nuclear Facilities: US Intelligence
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Israel Preparing Possible Preemptive Attack On Iranian Nuclear Facilities: US Intelligence</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong><u>Update(1830ET)</u>: </strong>At a moment it has become very clear that Netanyahu could care less about 'pressure' from Western allies the US, UK, and Canada, there are breaking reports Tuesday evening that a preemptive Israeli attack on Iran's nuclear sites could be imminent. According to <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2025/05/20/politics/intelligence-israel-possible-strike-iran-nuclear-facilities">CNN</a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>The US has obtained new intelligence suggesting that Israel is making preparations to strike Iranian nuclear facilities</strong>, even as the Trump administration has been <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2025/05/17/middleeast/iran-trump-nuclear-talks-intl">pursuing a diplomatic deal</a> with Tehran, multiple US officials familiar with the latest intelligence told CNN.</em></p>

<p data-analytics-observe="off" data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmawxynpd00033b6m09g5pqdd@published"><em>Such a strike would be a brazen break with President Donald Trump, US officials said. It could also risk tipping off a broader regional conflict in the Middle East — something the US has sought to avoid since the war in Gaza inflamed tensions beginning in 2023.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p data-analytics-observe="off" data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmawxynpd00033b6m09g5pqdd@published">The same report underscores that no 'final decision' has been made yet, and this is perhaps another ploy by the Israelis to show the West and the Mideast region that it means business, in the wake of "Israel's 9/11" - the Oct.7, 2023 Hamas terror attacks. </p>

<p data-analytics-observe="off" data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmawxynpd00033b6m09g5pqdd@published">The late in the day headline resulted in an immediate spike in oil prices... </p>

<p data-analytics-observe="off" data-article-gutter="true" data-component-name="paragraph" data-editable="text" data-uri="cms.cnn.com/_components/paragraph/instances/cmawxynpd00033b6m09g5pqdd@published"><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/oiliranstrike.png?itok=4embFJtY" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/oiliranstrike.png?itok=4embFJtY"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="50af9475-71ec-41eb-ba1e-4e973318a03c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="306" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/oiliranstrike.png?itok=4embFJtY" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>* * *</p>

<p>The United Kingdom on Tuesday suspended its free-trade agreement negotiations with Israel over the growing Gaza crisis, and after British Prime Minister Keir Starmer expressed disgust at newly expanded Israeli military operations in the Gaza Strip, also as famine threats at least 500,000 Palestinians.</p>

<p>Starmer described that he and his French and Canadian counterparts are "horrified" by the Netanyahu government's escalation in Gaza. This also comes as international headlines and warnings grow more dire. For example Al Jazeera has the following new <a href="https://www.aljazeera.com/news/liveblog/2025/5/20/live-israeli-allies-say-they-will-take-concrete-actions-over-gaza-siege">headline</a>: <strong>"Starving Palestinians resort to eating animal feed, flour mixed with sand"</strong>.</p>

<p>"<strong>We repeat our demand for a ceasefire as the only way to free the hostages</strong>, we repeat our opposition to settlements in the West Bank, and we repeat our demand to massively scale up humanitarian assistance into Gaza," Starmer told parliament.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/lammyisrael.jpg?itok=QTrmQPpd" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/lammyisrael.jpg?itok=QTrmQPpd"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="63af1bf0-9307-4309-bd42-783b7566f911" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/lammyisrael.jpg?itok=QTrmQPpd" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>David Lammy with Israeli President Isaac Herzog, via GPO</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>A Monday <a href="https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2025/5/20/uk-france-and-canada-threaten-concrete-actions-against-israel">joint statement</a> by the UK, France and Canada had threatened sanctions on Israel. Britain further did slap <strong>targeted sanctions on Israeli settler groups</strong> and individuals. </p>

<p>Later on Tuesday, Foreign Secretary David Lammy voiced agreement with Starmer, saying that Israel’s actions are "morally wrong" and "unjustifiable." He also said of the fresh sanctions, "I have seen for myself the consequences of settler violence. The fear of its victims. The impunity of its perpetrators."</p>

<p>In announcing the pause in free-trade agreement negotiations, Lammy further revealed that the <strong>Israeli ambassador had been summoned</strong>. Britain is reportedly demanding the full resumption of humanitarian aid deliveries to the Gaza Strip.</p>

<p>Responding to shadow foreign secretary Priti Patel, Lammy <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/politics/live/2025/may/20/uk-eu-deal-keir-starmer-rachel-reeves-gulf-nations-politic-live-news-updates?filterKeyEvents=false&page=with%3Ablock-682c85998f08a5e9325ebad3">told parliament</a>:</p>

<blockquote data-spacefinder-role="inline">
<p><em>I think the whole house should be able to utterly condemn the Israeli government’s denial of food to hungry children. It is wrong. It’s appalling.</em></p>

<p><em>Opposing the expansion of a war that has killed thousands of children is not rewarding Hamas. Opposing the displacement of 100,000s of civilians is not rewarding Hamas. On this side of the house, we are crystal clear that what is happening is morally wrong, unjustifiable, and it needs to stop.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Starting Friday the Israel Defense Forces (IDF) announced an expanded mobilization of troops for operation 'Gideon's Chariots'. Some two million Palestinians are <strong>expected to be forced into a "humanitarian zone" </strong>while most of the enclave is destroyed and flattened.</p>

<p>The policy somewhat contradicts Trump's main messaging during last week's Gulf tour, wherein he emphasized peace through deal-making, and not 'chaos' in the war-torn Middle East. </p>

<p>This is probably <strong>the most pressure Israel has come under from its Western allies since Oct.7, 2023</strong>. As we previously reported, even Vice President JD Vance <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/vance-abruptly-cancels-israel-visit-idf-expands-gaza-operations">abruptly canceled</a> a planned trip to Israel following the Netanyahu government's declaration that it would ramp up operations to conquer all of Gaza.</p>

<p><i>Meanwhile the domestic policy fight within Israel has been ramping up too...</i></p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Yair Golan, an IDF major general and leader of Israel’s Democrats Party, said Monday that Israel is killing babies as a hobby:<br /><br />
“A sane country does not wage war against civilians, does not kill babies for a hobby, and does not set goals involving the expulsion of populations.” <a href="https://t.co/NofvIAdNW9">pic.twitter.com/NofvIAdNW9</a></p>
— Dave DeCamp (@DecampDave) <a href="https://twitter.com/DecampDave/status/1924797801650688141?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 20, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Axios had <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/vance-skip-israel-visit-gaza-operation">written</a> that "The US official said Vance made the decision because <strong>he didn't want his trip to suggest the Trump administration endorsed the Israeli decision to launch a massive operation</strong> at a time when the U.S. is pushing for a ceasefire and hostage deal." </p>

<p>Neither the US nor UK have every fully cut funding or arms transfers to Israel for any reason, and are unlikely to ever escalate to that point, no matter how tense relations become.</p>

Title: After Credit Downgrade, Maryland's Leftist Governor Torpedoes Reparations Bill To Avoid Political Blowback
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">After Credit Downgrade, Maryland's Leftist Governor Torpedoes Reparations Bill To Avoid Political Blowback</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>The optics are grim for far-left Maryland Governor Wes Moore. As the state grapples with a fiscal crisis (deficit explosion), a credit downgrade, illegal alien invasion, violent crime, the looming threat of resident and business flight, a potential tsunami of new taxes, and a worsening power crisis, Moore is facing a growing backlash from all Marylanders. His ability to lead is increasingly being questioned—and it's becoming clear he's far from presidential material.</p>

<p>Moore has managed to anger both sides of the political aisle. The latest outrage comes from within his own party after he vetoed a bill that would have established a state commission to study and recommend reparations for African Americans affected by slavery.</p>

<p>In a letter explaining his decision, Moore said it's not the time for another study, emphasizing the need for direct action to address racial disparities such as the wealth gap, homeownership, education, and food insecurity.</p>

<p>"I will always protect and defend the full history of African Americans in our state and country," Moore wrote in his letter, adding, "But in light of the many important studies that have taken place on this issue over nearly three decades, now is the time to focus on the work itself: Narrowing the racial wealth gap, expanding homeownership, uplifting entrepreneurs of color, and closing the foundational disparities that lead to inequality — from food insecurity to education."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/fa2f702e-7d36-4dbd-9acd-ba4806045c51-jumbo3x1_Gov.WesMooresatdownwithpoliticalcommentatorArmstrongWilliamsinAnnapolisonAug.22.png?itok=wTSoaAh1" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/fa2f702e-7d36-4dbd-9acd-ba4806045c51-jumbo3x1_Gov.WesMooresatdownwithpoliticalcommentatorArmstrongWilliamsinAnnapolisonAug.22.png?itok=wTSoaAh1"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="dfc791d0-3709-411e-ad98-3a032e477097" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="269" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/fa2f702e-7d36-4dbd-9acd-ba4806045c51-jumbo3x1_Gov.WesMooresatdownwithpoliticalcommentatorArmstrongWilliamsinAnnapolisonAug.22.png?itok=wTSoaAh1" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>He continued: "We have moved in partnership with leaders across the state to uplift Black families and address racial disparities in our communities. That is the context in which I've made this difficult decision. Because while I appreciate the work that went into this legislation, <strong>I strongly believe now is not the time for another study. </strong>Now is the time for continued action that delivers results for the people we serve."</p>

<p>Moore's rationale—more likely crafted by his advisors—appears rooted in political optics. These far-left redistribution programs are so detached from capitalist principles and Western values that they risk being deeply unpopular, especially at a time when Maryland's finances are unraveling after decades of Democratic overspending and an economy overly dependent on government funding.</p>

<p>We suspect Moore's veto has also angered hardline Marxist Democrats in the state, who continue to push for socialist systems that redistribute wealth from the productive to the less productive. Under the current leadership of activist progressives, Maryland is on a death spiral—and it's not us saying this—but some leaders of some of the largest companies that operate in the Baltimore area have told us this.</p>

<p>With Democrats furious over Moore's veto of the reparations bill, the governor has now managed to infuriate both sides of the political aisle.</p>

<p>The Maryland Legislative Black Caucus was not pleased with Moore: </p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>"The state's first black governor chose to block this historic legislation that would have moved the state toward directly repairing the harm of enslavement."</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Meanwhile, Maryland's financial outlook continues to deteriorate, with a $3 billion budget shortfall looming—likely paving the way for new taxes and triggering yet another wave of resident flight.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">It just keeps getting WORSE<br /><br />
Maryland has now LOST its prized AAA bond rating from Moody's. Add that to the growing list of what Maryland has recently lost.<br /><br />
- FBI Headquarters<br />
- Washington Commanders<br />
- IonQ’s quantum computing hub<br />
- Six Flags America<br /><br />
What will be next?</p>
— Chris Papst (@chrispapst) <a href="https://twitter.com/chrispapst/status/1922977765046841577?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 15, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>A large asset manager based in Baltimore told us earlier this year that they had advised clients to leave the state before the impending tax tsunami and to avoid purchasing Maryland municipal bonds due to the high risk of a credit downgrade.</p>

<p>And last week, <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/paying-price-failed-leadership-maryland-hit-first-credit-downgrade-50-years">Maryland's financial credit profile deteriorated</a>, for the first time in decades—after Moody's downgraded the state's creditworthiness to Aa1 from AAA.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Snag_91efc59f.png?itok=cQxjZIOt" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Snag_91efc59f.png?itok=cQxjZIOt"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="9b61827a-ae3a-4444-b830-0300e56cb048" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="216" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Snag_91efc59f.png?itok=cQxjZIOt" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Since 1973, Maryland has maintained a top-tier credit rating, long seen as a reflection of fiscal discipline and responsible governance. However, far-left Democrats in Annapolis have chosen to run deficits to fund their progressive pet projects. This credit downgrade puts Maryland on the disastrous pathway toward becoming "<strong>Illinois 2.0."</strong></p>

<p>“I think it’s disgraceful that we’re going to set up a reparations tax that might tax one race and give to another race all in the name of equity,” Matthew Morgan, a Republican delegate, said in April before voting against the bill.</p>

<p><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/maryland-governor-vetoes-reparations-bill-says-its-not-time-for-another-study-5860075?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge">Epoch Times</a> noted, "Some lawmakers also took issue with the bill's broad language, which gave the proposed commission wide discretion in defining eligibility. They warned that, in theory, this could extend benefits to millions of people across the United States or even the world, costing billions of dollars."</p>

<p>Perhaps Moore should take some personal time—maybe at the upscale Caves Valley Golf Club, where sources say he is a member—and reflect on his state strategy while paying a round of golf. With crises piling up well before Trump's second term began, Moore has yet to demonstrate strong leadership Maryland needs.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-20T22:00:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 18:00</span>


Title: Working Out Is Right Wing, And That's A Good Thing
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Working Out Is Right Wing, And That's A Good Thing</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://amgreatness.com/2025/05/20/working-out-is-right-wing-and-thats-a-good-thing/"><em>Authored by Braeden Sorbo via American Greatness,</em></a></p>

<p><em><strong>The media has a new villain: fitness...</strong></em></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_11-34-09.jpg?itok=tWmOud4M" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-20_11-34-09.jpg?itok=tWmOud4M"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="8c857915-8485-4f03-80e8-8408780fcd56" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="287" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-20_11-34-09.jpg?itok=tWmOud4M" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>According to recent articles, engaging in physical exercise is now linked to right-wing extremism. </strong></p>

<p>The narrative suggests that lifting weights, building discipline, and taking responsibility for your body are somehow dangerous acts. <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/article/2024/jun/03/getting-fit-could-turn-you-into-a-rightwing-jerk"><em>The Guardian</em></a> claims that getting in shape could turn you into a “right-wing jerk,” while <a href="https://time.com/6242949/exercise-industry-white-supremacy/"><em>TIME</em> </a>runs pieces on “the white supremacist origins of exercise.” <a href="https://www.msnbc.com/opinion/msnbc-opinion/pandemic-fitness-trends-have-gone-extreme-literally-n1292463">MSNBC </a>warns that during the pandemic, workout trends ended up leading to “extreme” ideologies.</p>

<p><strong>Seriously? Can we just stop with the nonsense?</strong></p>

<p>I’ll tell you the real reason fitness is under attack. It breeds autonomy. And autonomous men are a threat to systems built on dependence and compliance.</p>

<p><strong>Allow me to be controversial: physical strength and mental resilience are connected. </strong>According to a 2022 study published in <a href="https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fpsyg.2022.859117/full"><em>Frontiers in Psychology</em></a>, individuals who maintain regular physical activity demonstrate significantly higher psychological resilience and lower levels of anxiety and depression. When you commit to training your body, you’re also training your mind. You’re learning delayed gratification. You’re becoming comfortable with discomfort. You’re developing the backbone to say no—to weak ideas, to bad leadership, to mob thinking. In other words, weak people are agreeable, which is exactly what the government wants.</p>

<p>Testosterone plays a central role in this. Individuals with higher levels of testosterone flowing through their bodies are more likely to question authority and even think for themselves. A 2015 review in <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4330791/"><em>Biological Psychiatry</em></a> explained that testosterone influences areas of the brain involved in motivation, emotional regulation, and social behavior, helping men navigate challenges with clarity and confidence.</p>

<p>But wait, there’s more! Another study in <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6742992/"><em>PNAS</em> </a>(2019) directly debunked the myth that testosterone reduces empathy, showing no evidence that it impairs cognitive empathy at all. Translation: Higher testosterone doesn’t make you a bad person. It makes you sharper, more focused, and more prepared to lead.</p>

<p><strong>So why the war on fitness? Because fit, strong, disciplined men are harder to control.</strong></p>

<p>They don’t break down from online shaming. They don’t beg bureaucracies for handouts. They know how to fight—metaphorically and literally—and that makes them dangerous to anyone trying to neuter society. As <a href="https://youtu.be/sP37wxRUJVk?si=wtcgn3Y5zA85eNwk">Jordan Peterson</a> once said, “A harmless man is <em>not</em> a good man. A good man is a very, very dangerous man who has it under voluntary control.”</p>

<p>When you’re physically able to defend yourself, you become dangerous—in the best way. The world thrives on intimidation. That’s why so many people—especially young women—go along with destructive ideas like abortion or men in women’s sports. Deep down, they know something’s off. But fear keeps them quiet. Now take a man who’s strong, capable, and confident—traits often earned through training—and you have someone who can’t be bullied into submission. He doesn’t fold under pressure. He doesn’t need the world’s approval because he knows he can stand on his own.</p>

<p><strong>Without the ability to defend yourself, you stop forming your own opinions. </strong>You become agreeable out of survival instincts. Weakness breeds obedience. What’s been labeled as <em>toxic</em> is actually <em>essential</em>. Without strength, there is no freedom. And without testosterone, there is no original thought—just borrowed scripts and empty slogans. The <a href="https://bmcpublichealth.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s12889-022-13070-7">stronger </a>the body, the more stable the mind. The more you train your limits, the less likely you are to break under pressure.</p>

<p><strong>Socially, the story is the same.</strong> Parenthood and family responsibility—things once considered pillars of adulthood—are now “conservative red flags.” But the data says otherwise. A 2022 study published in the <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC9449478/">National Library of Medicine</a> found that becoming a parent consistently predicts a shift toward more conservative values across different cultures. Why? Because raising a child forces you to care about things that extend beyond yourself.</p>

<p>So yes—men who lift, who lead, who protect—are more likely to value tradition, reject chaos, and push back against cultural decay, and that’s a good thing.</p>

<p><strong>If being <a href="https://youtu.be/sP37wxRUJVk?si=wtcgn3Y5zA85eNwk">physically fit</a>, masculine, and protective lands you on a government watchlist, maybe it’s the government that should be watched. </strong>If being strong, loyal, and self-reliant makes you “right-wing,” maybe being right-wing just means you haven’t lost your mind.</p>

<p>The gym isn’t just about vanity and lifting big things. It’s about whether you can defend your home when the need arises. It’s about your son learning to lead, not obey. It’s about your daughter growing up knowing someone strong has her back.</p>

<p><strong>So if working out makes you a right-wing extremist, then we need more gyms.</strong></p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-20T21:40:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 17:40</span>


Title: NH's First Black Sheriff Jailed For Blowing Public Money On Travel With Women
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">NH's First Black Sheriff Jailed For Blowing Public Money On Travel With Women</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>A New Hampshire man who was heralded as <strong>the first black sheriff in the state's history was sentenced on Monday to 3 1/2 years in prison for squandering $19,000 of taxpayers' money on expensive getaways with multiple love interests </strong>-- and then lying to investigators about what he'd done. Tightly following the script we've seen so many times before, <strong>the disgraced "barrier-breaker" had previously said fellow Democrats who investigated his crimes were racists, </strong>and that his term in office was "rife with inequities." Despite repeatedly lying to the court and violating his bail conditions, his sentence was a fraction of what prosecutors sought. </p>

<p>At 35 years old, Democrat Mark Brave was <strong>also the youngest-ever sheriff i</strong>n New Hampshire history when he was elected in November 2020 -- following the summer of George Floyd and amid the Black Lives Matter mania that swept the country and helped usher under-qualified blacks into many top roles in and out of law enforcement. "<a href="https://apnews.com/general-news-e25df8ff28c8bdf1f8b2fa71c5985001">It’s something I feel should have happened a long time ago</a>, but I’m honored that I will be the person to pave the way,” said Brave at the time. (Alas, some barriers proved insurmountable that year, as a self-described <a href="https://apnews.com/article/e1580367018108b09755dfb994395c0a">transgender Satanist</a> lost the Cheshire County New Hampshire sheriff race.) </p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="zxx" xml:lang="zxx" xml:lang="zxx"><a href="https://t.co/2cDFI1Tid9">pic.twitter.com/2cDFI1Tid9</a></p>
— Daniel Concannon (@TooWhiteToTweet) <a href="https://twitter.com/TooWhiteToTweet/status/1924490821350339067?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 19, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>“<a href="https://www.timesunion.com/news/article/former-new-hampshire-sheriff-sentenced-to-prison-20335111.php">His repeated lies, misuse of taxpayer funds, and abuse of office</a> were not just criminal — they were a profound betrayal of the public trust and the oath he took to serve with integrity,” said New Hampshire Attorney General John Formella in a statement. That said, <strong>the sentence handed down by lily-white Judge Dan St. Hilaire was far lighter than the seven- to 14-year confinement that prosecutors had requested</strong>. Brave will technically be eligible for parole in 3 1/2 years, but the reality is that <strong>he'll walk even sooner</strong> if he participates in certain prison programs. He must pay $18,969 in restitution to Strafford County. </p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/brave-cuffed-682b4bdebdf54.jpeg?itok=GyeKPatk" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/brave-cuffed-682b4bdebdf54.jpeg?itok=GyeKPatk"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="d9e6fb30-7fca-4e5b-af6c-20ab463056d2" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="306" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/brave-cuffed-682b4bdebdf54.jpeg?itok=GyeKPatk" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><strong>Mark Brave was led out of the courtroom in handcuffs</strong> (WMUR)</figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p><strong>The judge's leniency was at odds with his characterization of Brave's conduct.</strong> “The court has reviewed a record that has been unlike any other case that has come before it, mainly because of <a href="https://www.unionleader.com/news/courts/ex-sheriff-mark-brave-sentenced-to-minimum-of-3-years-in-prison-for-perjury/article_e796a635-cf80-43bc-acb8-c62115585286.html">the continuation of the crimes that were being committed while the case was proceeding</a>." The judge was apparently referring to Brave's: </p>

<ul><li>Lying to the grand jury</li>
	<li>Lying on his application for public defense by <a href="https://nhjournal.com/court-brave-tried-to-hide-1-5-million-to-score-free-lawyer/">failing to disclose $1.5 million</a> received on the sale of his home</li>
	<li>Violating his bail conditions by paying $52,000 to lease an apartment in Boston, when he was mandated to remain in New Hampshire; he also traveled to Florida and Puerto Rico</li>
	<li>Lying to the judge, saying he was living in Dover with his ex-wife and that he was out of money</li>
	<li>Failing to disclose his purchase of a 1968 Porsche, though he posted videos and photos of the vehicle to social media</li>
</ul><p>Brave went wild with his county credit card, using it to fund <strong>multiple trips to destinations in Florida, Baltimore and Maryland for getaways with various women </strong>-- with at least some of the trysts happening <a href="https://www.unionleader.com/news/courts/ex-sheriff-mark-brave-sentenced-to-minimum-of-3-years-in-prison-for-perjury/article_e796a635-cf80-43bc-acb8-c62115585286.html">while Brave was married</a>. He attempted to conceal his misuse of funds by attributing the travel to <strong>fictional business meetings</strong> and training sessions. He also lied to investigators and a grand jury. Some of his lies were exposed by <a href="https://www.nhpr.org/nh-news/2025-05-19/former-strafford-county-sheriff-to-serve-jail-time-for-theft-perjury">hotel lobby security cameras that captured him in the company of women</a> on trips where he claimed to have been traveling alone.      </p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/freezenia.jpg?itok=zY4FuX5C" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/freezenia.jpg?itok=zY4FuX5C"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="effbe633-4dd9-4d2b-8334-8981d0829a89" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="483" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/freezenia.jpg?itok=zY4FuX5C" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><strong>Brave created an entirely-new job in his department for longtime "friend" Freezenia Veras -- then jetted off to Florida with her using a county credit card </strong>(<a href="https://nhjournal.com/mark-braves-taxpayer-funded-love-life/"><em>NH Journal</em></a>)</figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>Brave's misconduct started to unravel when an audit prompted an inquiry into JetBlue tickets purchased for a 2022 trip to Fort Lauderdale. <strong>Not content to merely steal public money, Brave opted for JetBlue's pricey "EvenMore" package</strong>, with the pair of tickets costing $1,615. Defending the expenditure, Brave said he needed the extra room because he's 6' 2" tall, and <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/news/lies-mark-brave-told-got-035900280.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAE_BmpwckAYhvrEBzBv8I3ybPZbOKcwlbb0oCDA__EDiLYBlReIDyqnECDRL4CwzNm9dGHUKIo11mu6XE-AGFN5XATPMgCFNFjKVwOw5np1UuGSP9y1lFHGpd_PYfY60lDVxicpHerNwroL8u9RISTJJjgZMt0uadmimF0hM6Wpb">claimed he'd traveled with a "well-built, muscular" deputy</a>. Investigators found, however, that he was traveling with female employee.</p>

<p>In <strong>another comical instance</strong> in which he was caught in a lie about a supposed business trip with a colleague, County Administrator Raymond Bower asked Brave why the hotel room only had a single king-bed. "There was a slight pause, and he said, <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/news/lies-mark-brave-told-got-035900280.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAE_BmpwckAYhvrEBzBv8I3ybPZbOKcwlbb0oCDA__EDiLYBlReIDyqnECDRL4CwzNm9dGHUKIo11mu6XE-AGFN5XATPMgCFNFjKVwOw5np1UuGSP9y1lFHGpd_PYfY60lDVxicpHerNwroL8u9RISTJJjgZMt0uadmimF0hM6Wpb">“Oh, aw, the other person slept on the couch,” </a>Bower said in an affidavit.  He also lied about spending money on business meals associated with meetings with the completely fictional "New England Sheriff's Association." </p>

<p>He also <strong>installed a friend, Freezenia Veras, in a newly-created $80,000 job</strong>, and <a href="https://nhjournal.com/braves-love-life-got-him-in-trouble-but-his-lies-put-him-in-jail/">jetted off to Florida </a>with her for a non-existent consultation with a law enforcement agency. In one of his many lies to a grand jury, Brave denied that he took another woman on a dinner cruise using his county credit card. <strong>When prosecutors whipped out a photo of Brave and the woman,</strong> <strong>he hilariously couldn't come up with her name:</strong> "Her name, her name is … um … let me see, I forget which one this is. I’ve been dating a lot of people,” he told the grand jury, according to <a href="https://nhjournal.com/braves-love-life-got-him-in-trouble-but-his-lies-put-him-in-jail/"><em>NH Journal</em></a>. </p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/epp-schmidt-1-768x1023%202.jpg?itok=iViCd-oQ" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/epp-schmidt-1-768x1023%202.jpg?itok=iViCd-oQ"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="7f0b51b3-eb9c-4801-8a99-393c5a4364c8" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="472" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/epp-schmidt-1-768x1023%202.jpg?itok=iViCd-oQ" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><strong>Brave used public money for his trip to visit Kenisha Epps-Schmidt -- then talked her into giving him $2,300 for a used-car purchase he never made</strong> (<a href="https://nhjournal.com/mark-braves-taxpayer-funded-love-life/"><em>NH Journal</em></a>)</figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>Brave also traveled to Maryland to spend time with Kenisha Epps-Schmidt, whom he'd met online. He tried papering over that embezzlement by attributing the trip to a Washington DC meeting with Rep. Chris Pappas that never happened. <strong>Brave proceeded to cheat Epps-Schmidt out of $2,300 she gave him to buy a car </strong>-- <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/news/lies-mark-brave-told-got-035900280.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAE_BmpwckAYhvrEBzBv8I3ybPZbOKcwlbb0oCDA__EDiLYBlReIDyqnECDRL4CwzNm9dGHUKIo11mu6XE-AGFN5XATPMgCFNFjKVwOw5np1UuGSP9y1lFHGpd_PYfY60lDVxicpHerNwroL8u9RISTJJjgZMt0uadmimF0hM6Wpb">which he never did</a>.   </p>

<p>Add it all up, and <strong>we have another low-IQ miscreant advanced to a position of authority because he had the right skin color.</strong> That's bad enough, but the black-catering madness carried over over to his sentencing, as a white Republican judge ensured a short stay in prison despite the black defendant's profound and repeated contempt for the criminal justice system all throughout the adjudication of his crime.   </p>

<p>As part of his plea deal, Brave is barred from seeking a law enforcement job during his post-confinement probation. That still leaves him in prime position to become the boyfriend of a leftist congresswoman or a progressive NGO executive and take a salary for providing "security consultant" services. <strong><em><a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/cori-bush-private-security">Just axe former Rep. Cori Bush</a> or Black Lives Matters Global Network Foundation co-founder <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/whats-more-tragic-capitalism-blm-faces-bankruptcy-founder-cullors-cut-warner-bros">Patrissee Cullors</a> how it works. </em></strong> </p>

Title: Boomers, Let's Face It: The Math Doesn't Work
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Boomers, Let's Face It: The Math Doesn't Work</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://charleshughsmith.substack.com/p/boomers-lets-face-it-the-math-doesnt"><em>Authored by Charles Hugh Smith via OfTwoMinds blog,</em></a></p>

<p><strong>There are many consequential things we can't discuss factually because the topic upsets everyone.</strong> And since getting upset shuts down any direct discussion of difficult issues, these issues metastasize into problems that end up sinking the ship.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/150501160534-rough-economic-seas.jpg?itok=LzGxwzSn" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/150501160534-rough-economic-seas.jpg?itok=LzGxwzSn"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="2f0e5fb8-c2b6-4958-a56d-cc13d0338366" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/150501160534-rough-economic-seas.jpg?itok=LzGxwzSn" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>The </strong><em><strong>Titanic</strong></em><strong> has already struck the iceberg and is doomed, but since this upsets the passengers, we dance around the facts rather than take immediate action.</strong> Everything about the situation is upsetting, and so emotions dominate the zeitgeist: resentments, blame-game, accusations, the whole self-reinforcing dynamic leads to people shouting at others as they drown. The last word, indeed.</p>

<p><strong>Federal deficit spending and the overweighting of entitlement spending on retirees is too upsetting to discuss factually, so we don't. But the math doesn't work, and so the ship will sink.</strong> This was obvious 20 years ago, when I posted this: <a href="https://www.oftwominds.com/blogs/boomers.html">Boomers, Prepare to Fall on Your Swords</a> (June 2005), in which I suggested that well-off Boomers address the problem by gracefully making the necessary sacrifices rather than heap them on the younger generations.</p>

<p><strong>It was even more obvious by 2013, when I posted this:</strong> <a href="https://www.oftwominds.com/blogmay13/genX5-13.html">Generation X: An Inconvenient Era</a> (May 23, 2013), in which correspondent Eric A. explains how <em>the math doesn't work</em>.</p>

<p><strong>Let's start with some necessary stipulations.</strong> When I suggest well-off Boomers accept the need to make sacrifices to save the ship from sinking, I suggest this as someone in this cohort.</p>

<p>I am a Boomer, drawing my Social Security benefit, which like my lifetime income, is close to the national median SSA benefit. I'm solidly in the middle of the pack. Being over the age of 65, I also have Medicare benefits. Like many others of my generation, I've lived frugally, saved money, worked hard, etc. Since I'm still working, I pay Social Security and Medicare taxes--15.3% of all earned income as I am self-employed.</p>

<p>Unlike others in my generation, I attribute only a modest percentage of my net worth to frugality and working hard, as the majority of whatever "wealth" I own is the direct result of the hyper-financialization credit-asset bubble that's been inflated since 2007.</p>

<p><strong>Those who were able to buy assets such as houses and stocks decades ago saw their net worth rise to extraordinary heights in the bubble.</strong> Those who didn't or couldn't buy assets before the bubble did not see their net worth rise to extraordinary heights.</p>

<p><strong>Let's go over how we got here.</strong> The current federal tax system and retiree benefits evolved in the 1930s to the mid-1960s. In the 1930s, retirement meant poverty for many workers who were unable to save a nestegg large enough to fund their no-earnings years. Social Security was enacted as a way of using the SSA taxes paid by current workers (1% of wages in those days) to fund a modest retirement income for retirees.</p>

<p><strong>Social Security was always a </strong><em><strong>pay as you go</strong></em><strong> system.</strong> Whatever SSA tax revenues that weren't distributed piled up in a Trust Fund. This Trust Fund was eliminated in the mid-1960s, and excess SSA taxes went into the federal general fund. The current Trust Fund is a useful fiction. When SSA runs a deficit, the Treasury funds the deficit by selling Treasury bonds, just as it does with all other deficit spending.</p>

<p><strong>Political realities demanded that the program be universal to attract widespread support.</strong> So millionaires collect Social Security and Medicare benefits, too. As SSA's financial foundations erode, a modest reform was enacted: above a modest income, 50% of SSA benefits are taxed as regular income.</p>

<p><strong>Back when the program was enacted, there were around 10 workers for every retiree.</strong> The demographics and economy were different then. The economy was mostly domestic, and the bubble of the 1920s had popped. Financialization and globalization were at low ebb. Everyone assumed there would always be 10 workers for every retiree.</p>

<p><strong>But people started living longer, the disabled were added to Social Security, and Medicare ballooned from a modest program to an open-ended spending juggernaut.</strong> In other words, the economy changed, demographics changed, but the system has not been changed to reflect these realities. SSA and Medicare taxes have increased dramatically, but these programs are still funded by payroll taxes paid by employees and employers.</p>

<p>Capital (assets, income from capital gains, speculation and investments) only pays a thin slice of Medicare via the Net Investment Income Tax (NIIT) on capital gains incomes above $200,000 for single taxpayers and above $250,000 for couples filing jointly.</p>

<p><strong>What we're actually discussing isn't just generational; it's 1) the open-ended nature of the Medicare and Medicaid programs</strong>, 2) the impossibility of relying on two workers to pay all the benefits for each retiree as the number of retirees and beneficiaries exceeds 69 million people while the full-time workforce is 135 million, and 3) the extraordinary wealth divide in the U.S. where the majority of the wealth is held by the top few percent and the retiree generation (Boomers) for the reasons stated above.</p>

<p><strong>The solutions are as obvious as plugging a hole in the ship's hull.</strong></p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>1) The tax burden has to be shifted from labor to capital via financial transaction taxes and ending the multi-trillion dollar exclusions on capital gains.</em></p>

<p><em>2) Social Security and Medicare benefits must be means tested; those collecting $10,000 a month in other pensions and investment income don't need Social Security benefits, which should be reserved for those with no other substantive source of steady income in their retirement years.</em></p>

<p><em>3) The open-ended entitlement programs must be limited in some fashion, and there is no way to do this that will not upset everyone. Hard choices--triage--must be made, as doing nothing is choosing to let the ship sink.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p><strong>Let's feast on the facts of the matter.</strong> Those who need a calming agent, please do so now.</p>

<p><strong>Here's household/non-profit net worth.</strong> The household sector has a net worth of $160 trillion. Notice that the total is far above the inflation rate. This is a credit-asset bubble on steroids.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2813%29_7.jpg?itok=-vuWcHQw" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2813%29_7.jpg?itok=-vuWcHQw"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="577c034a-ef3c-468e-8215-7ba86d134b58" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="423" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2813%29_7.jpg?itok=-vuWcHQw" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Here is total debt.</strong> Borrow a bunch of money into existence and dump it into financial speculation, and voila, a debt-fueled asset bubble for the ages.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2814%29_7.jpg?itok=XxT2uVi2" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2814%29_7.jpg?itok=XxT2uVi2"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="74091f7e-8806-424e-9801-4600cbf38c3c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="417" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2814%29_7.jpg?itok=XxT2uVi2" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Here is total public debt.</strong> Is a parabolic rise really sustainable? No, the math doesn't work, especially as interest rates rise: the debt costs nothing to service at 0%, but the interest payments are huge at 4%.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2815%29_8.jpg?itok=vBbuxe-_" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2815%29_8.jpg?itok=vBbuxe-_"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="854fe1c8-7b67-4381-883e-1c8a83f684d3" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="416" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2815%29_8.jpg?itok=vBbuxe-_" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Apologists love to attribute the debt to inflation or "growth," but that's misdirection.</strong> As a percentage of the nation's GDP (gross domestic product), the debt has risen 4-fold since president Reagan shepherded Social Security reforms in the early 1980s, and doubled as a percentage of GDP since 2007, before the Federal Reserve bailed out the status quo with hyper-financialization.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2816%29_6.jpg?itok=Vo6fZPPj" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2816%29_6.jpg?itok=Vo6fZPPj"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="259b05a6-8fd4-4613-a556-793a341279d2" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="415" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2816%29_6.jpg?itok=Vo6fZPPj" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Here is a pie chart of federal spending.</strong> Social Security, Medicare and Medicaid are 44%. Toss in the other mandatory spending--a big chunk of which is interest paid on federal debt--and there's not much left to cut. The reality is there is no way to slow the runaway debt train without tackling open-ended retirement / healthcare programs.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2817%29_7.jpg?itok=vyRO9vFW" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2817%29_7.jpg?itok=vyRO9vFW"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="38d2bfd4-5d4f-4745-baf8-1d7c09a2431c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="351" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2817%29_7.jpg?itok=vyRO9vFW" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>The vast majority of projected growth in federal spending stems from these programs and the interest paid on funds borrowed to fund them.</strong> Unfortunately, these facts don't disappear because we don't like them.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2818%29_7.jpg?itok=yd97UcYD" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2818%29_7.jpg?itok=yd97UcYD"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="8fa2544d-df9c-4333-9c41-d24c7c5d82b8" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="375" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2818%29_7.jpg?itok=yd97UcYD" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Boomers hold the majority of net worth.</strong> So it follows that increasing taxes on capital will impact the Boomers who are wealthy--and younger folks who are wealthy, too, of course.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2819%29_7.jpg?itok=1BbviyzM" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2819%29_7.jpg?itok=1BbviyzM"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="55dc2351-99fc-4c0f-b862-4bb394261125" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2819%29_7.jpg?itok=1BbviyzM" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>It's interesting how debt and the net worth of the top 1% have soared in tandem.</strong> Could it be that soaring debt-asset bubbles have benefited the top 1% far more than the debt bubble has benefited the bottom 50%? And if that's the case, then what does this suggest in terms of saving the ship from sinking?</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2820%29_7.jpg?itok=ID1Lkq5C" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2820%29_7.jpg?itok=ID1Lkq5C"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="5b99954b-2257-48eb-80a0-e500fb8cd58c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="313" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/httpssubstack-post-media.s3.amaz%20%2820%29_7.jpg?itok=ID1Lkq5C" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>The passengers on the </strong><em><strong>Titanic</strong></em><strong> arguing with each other can't stop the ship from sinking by "winning the argument."</strong> Silencing those willing to discuss the issues factually doesn't actually make the factual realities go away.</p>

<p><strong>Those of us who run businesses / are self-employed don't have the luxury of not dealing with financial realities. Triage comes with every enterprise.</strong> We need a national discussion of triage that doesn't immediately degrade into denial or histrionics. And no, AI and stablecoins aren't going to make all this go away, any more than hoping the Central Bank of Mars will emerge to give us a 36 trillion-quatloo bailout.</p>

<p><strong>Boomers--and Gen X, Millennials, Gen Z--let's face it: the math doesn't work.</strong> Triage means sacrifices will have to be made and distributed to those most able to afford them to spare those least able to afford them. The ship is not just taking on water; it's loaded with <em>third rails</em> and sacred cows that can't be touched, and so it's doomed to sink if we do nothing.</p>
</div>

Title: No Trial Data, No Vax: FDA Demands Gold Standard Testing For Any New COVID-19 Vaccines
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">No Trial Data, No Vax: FDA Demands Gold Standard Testing For Any New COVID-19 Vaccines</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/health/fda-says-no-licenses-for-covid-19-vaccines-for-many-americans-without-trial-data-5860572?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge&src_src=partner&src_cmp=ZeroHedge">Authored by Zachary Stieber via The Epoch Times</a> (emphasis ours),</em></p>

<p><strong>The Food and Drug Administration (FDA) will not approve COVID-19 vaccines for many Americans absent trial data showing that the benefits outweigh the risks</strong>, top agency officials said on May 20.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2863%29_0.jpg?itok=HeKo-I7i" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2863%29_0.jpg?itok=HeKo-I7i"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="5ed7d47b-29f1-4f74-8eae-9536b7555750" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2863%29_0.jpg?itok=HeKo-I7i" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Dr. Marty Makary, commissioner of the Food and Drug Administration, in Washington on May 5, 2025. Anna Moneymaker/Getty Images</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>“Moving forward, <strong>the FDA will adopt the following Covid-19 vaccination regulatory framework: On the basis of immunogenicity—proof that a vaccine can generate antibody titers in people</strong>—the FDA anticipates that it will be able to make favorable benefit–risk findings for adults over the age of 65 years and for all persons above the age of 6 months with one or more risk factors that put them at high risk for severe Covid-19 outcomes,” such as asthma or cancer, FDA Commissioner Dr. Marty Makary and Dr. Vinay Prasad, head of the FDA’s Center for Biologics Evaluation and Research, <a href="https://www.nejm.org/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMsb2506929">wrote</a> in a New England Journal of Medicine article.</p>

<p>“For all healthy persons—those with no risk factors for severe Covid-19—between the ages of 6 months and 64 years<strong>, the FDA anticipates the need for randomized, controlled trial data evaluating clinical outcomes before Biologics License Applications can be granted.</strong>”</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/jbRGlEsbKQ4?si=5lUDYXbm_3hpZyMc" title="YouTube video player" width="560"></iframe></p>

<p>Pfizer, Moderna, and Novavax, which have received licenses for their COVID-19 vaccines, did not immediately respond to requests for comment.</p>

<p>Several medical groups that have commented on FDA steps concerning COVID-19 vaccines, such as the American Academy of Family Physicians, did not return inquiries.</p>

<p>The FDA in 2024, in its most recent action concerning the Pfizer and Moderna vaccines, <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/health/fda-approves-new-covid-19-vaccines-5710997">approved</a> updated versions for most Americans and extended emergency authorization for others, despite there being no trial data available for those formulations.</p>

<p><strong>The regulatory agency on May 16<a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/health/fda-approves-new-covid-19-vaccine-with-restrictions-5859587"> approved</a> Novavax’s COVID-19 vaccine for the first time</strong>. The approval was for adults aged 65 and up. The agency said that people aged 12 to 64 could receive a Novavax shot, but only if they have one of the conditions that puts them at higher risk for severe COVID-19 outcomes.</p>

<p>An earlier version of Novavax’s shot was tested in a randomized, controlled trial in 2021.</p>

<p>The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention currently recommends that people aged 6 months and older receive one of the latest COVID-19 vaccines, but just 13 percent of children and 23 percent of adults have followed that recommendation.</p>

<p><strong>Makary and Prasad noted that a number of other countries, such as Australia and Germany, only recommend COVID-19 vaccines to certain populations.</strong></p>

<p>“While all other high-income nations confine vaccine recommendations to older adults (typically those older than 65 years of age), or those at high risk for severe Covid-19, the United States has adopted a one-size-fits-all regulatory framework and has granted broad marketing authorization to all Americans over the age of 6 months,” they wrote on Tuesday. “The U.S. policy has sometimes been justified by arguing that the American people are not sophisticated enough to understand age- and risk-based recommendations. We reject this view.”</p>

<p><strong>The officials said that while the quick development of COVID-19 vaccines was a scientific and medical achievement, the benefit of repeated dosing—some people have received at least six doses—is unclear.</strong></p>

<p>The trials of the vaccines should measure prevention of symptomatic COVID-19, with secondary endpoints including severe COVID-19, hospitalization, and death, according to Makary and Prasad, who said that the trials should include participants who contracted COVID-19 within the past year, and they should follow participants for at least six months “to ensure that early booster gains persist.” The control group could receive a saline placebo, the officials said.</p>

<p>“<strong>Ultimately, these studies alone can provide reassurance that the American repeat-boosters in-perpetuity strategy is evidence-based</strong>,” they wrote.</p>

<p>Health Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. recently <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/article/hhs-to-require-placebo-controlled-trials-for-new-vaccines-5850077">pledged</a> to require placebo-controlled trials for new vaccines.</p>

<p>Makary and Prasad planned to talk about the policy update<a href="https://www.youtube.com/live/jbRGlEsbKQ4"> at 1 p.m.</a> on Tuesday.</p>

<p><em>This is a developing story that will be updated.</em></p>
</div>
