Title: "Today I Will Show My Naked Body": Rep. Nancy Mace Combats Voyeurism During Oversight Hearing
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">"Today I Will Show My Naked Body": Rep. Nancy Mace Combats Voyeurism During Oversight Hearing</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Rep. Nancy Mace (R-SC) <strong>showed 'photos of her naked body' during a House Oversight meeting on Tuesday </strong>as the latest twist in her crusade against voyeurism.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/6f483ee9_jpg_92.jpg?itok=vhcIH-Pi" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/6f483ee9_jpg_92.jpg?itok=vhcIH-Pi"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="44ff159b-6377-496c-b718-aeb398aa2ade" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/6f483ee9_jpg_92.jpg?itok=vhcIH-Pi" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Mace was engaged to Charleston-based software entrepreneur, Patrick Bryant. After purchasing two properties together, their relationship ended abruptly in 2021 after Mace reportedly discovered Bryant on a dating app.</p>

<p><strong>Mace would later claim</strong> in a <a href="https://scdailygazette.com/2025/02/28/attorneys-for-1-of-the-men-accused-by-mace-demand-evidence-or-an-apology/">February speech</a> on the House floor that in November 2023, she discovered a digital cache of <a href="https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/patrick-bryant-nancy-mace-accusations-b2696289.html">over 10,000 videos and photos</a> on Bryant’s phone, depicting rape, nonconsensual photos, and videos of women and underage girls, including herself. </p>

<p>She recounted finding a video of herself naked, unaware she was being filmed, and alleged that Bryant recorded her without consent - and claims that Bryant and several other men conspired to commit <strong>sexual exploitation, voyeurism, and assault </strong>targeting multiple women, including minors, for over two decades.</p>

<p>She also says she found evidence of an app storing files from <strong>a hidden camera - </strong>with one alone containing <a href="https://www.postandcourier.com/politics/congresswoman-nancy-mace-house-speech-south-carolina/article_4b162376-e7c7-11ef-8169-2799c722a7b6.html">10,633 videos</a>.</p>

<h2>Rape, Drugging and Sex Trafficking</h2>

<p>Mace alleged that in 2022, while at a property co-owned by Bryant and another accused man, she consumed two vodka sodas, blacked out, and was raped, though she could not confirm if Bryant was the perpetrator - but that Bryant and his associates drugged her and other women, suggesting the incidents might have been filmed or sold on the dark web.</p>

<p>She also accused the men of <a href="https://people.com/nancy-mace-accuses-ex-fiance-patrick-bryant-others-rape-8789748">sex trafficking</a>, alleging they paid each other to abuse women, which she described as a “premeditated, calculated exploitation.”</p>

<p>Bryant, a co-founder of the software firm Code/+/Trust and former chairman of the Charleston Metro Chamber of Commerce, categorically denied all allegations.</p>

<p>"I categorically deny these allegations. I take this matter seriously and will cooperate fully with any necessary legal processes to clear my name," he told the <em>Associated Press</em>, calling Mace's accusations "devastatingly harmful" and an attempt to further her political career.</p>

<h2>'Today I will show my naked body'</h2>

<p>Which brings us to today - when Mace <a href="https://x.com/RepNancyMace/status/1924825678479798513">posted</a> on X; "<span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><strong>Today I will show my naked body on one of the videos predator and rapist Patrick Bryant took of me and many other women.</strong> Mace made the statement one hour after she posted: </span>"<span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">In my Oversight hearing today I’m going to expose predator and rapist Patrick Bryant for the monster he is. With evidence. Naked bodies. Legs spread apart. Upskirt photos. The kinds of things he would film and photograph women without their knowledge, permission or consent."</span></p>

<p>People waited with anticipation...</p>

Title: US Attorney's New Program Sidesteps California's Sanctuary Laws Shielding Illegals From ICE
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">US Attorney's New Program Sidesteps California's Sanctuary Laws Shielding Illegals From ICE</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/us-attorneys-new-program-gets-around-californias-sanctuary-laws-shielding-illegal-immigrants-from-ice-5860259?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge"><em>Authored by Darlene McCormick Sanchez via The Epoch Times,</em></a></p>

<p>In what could be a game changer for the Trump administration’s deportation efforts, the U.S. Attorney’s Office for California’s Central District and federal partners launched a program to “neutralize California’s sanctuary state policy.”</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image%20%2819%29_8.jpg?itok=TwR0bKt7" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image%20%2819%29_8.jpg?itok=TwR0bKt7"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="54eb1a7d-3d94-40bd-aa39-476ceb81051c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image%20%2819%29_8.jpg?itok=TwR0bKt7" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Operation Guardian Angel, announced by federal officials on May 19, will file complaints and arrest warrants to allow federal authorities to take as many defendants as possible into custody from county jails, according to a Department of Justice <a href="https://www.justice.gov/usao-cdca/pr/operation-guardian-angel-launched-neutralize-californias-sanctuary-state-policies">press release</a>.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>“Under the Trump administration, we will not allow sanctuary jurisdictions to stand in the way of keeping the American People safe,”</strong> U.S. Attorney Bill Essayli, who launched the test program, <a href="https://x.com/USAttyEssayli/status/1924550658369438170">posted</a> on X.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>One of President Donald Trump’s main campaign promises for a second term was the mass deportation of millions who came into the country illegally during the Biden administration.</p>

<p><strong>If a person who has been deported reenters the country illegally, that’s a felony under Title 8 law, said Ciaran McEvoy, a spokesman for the U.S. Attorney’s Office in Los Angeles.</strong></p>

<p>California’s state law—<a href="https://leginfo.legislature.ca.gov/faces/billTextClient.xhtml?bill_id=201720180SB54">Senate Bill 54</a>—prevents county sheriff’s departments and local law enforcement from honoring an Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) detainer.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>“Even if they want to turn them over, they can’t,” McEvoy told The Epoch Times.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p><strong>Operation Guardian Angel gets around the law through federal arrest warrants, which McEvoy said leave the counties no choice but to hand the targeted illegal immigrants over.</strong></p>

<p>Essayli stated in the press release that “the worst criminal aliens in state custody are frequently released into the community” because California’s sanctuary state policies block cooperation with federal law enforcement.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>“These laws effectively render federal immigration detainers meaningless. The days of giving criminal illegal aliens a free pass are over,”</strong></em> he stated.</p>

<p><em><strong>“While California may be presently disregarding detainers, it cannot ignore federal arrest warrants.”</strong></em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>The program, which began May 10, has resulted in the arrest of 13 defendants as of May 15 in California. The Operation Guardian Angel task force is made up of ICE, the FBI, the Drug Enforcement Administration, Homeland Security Investigations, and the Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives.</p>

<p>The California federal district is home to the counties of Riverside, San Bernardino, San Luis Obispo, Santa Barbara, Ventura, and Los Angeles County. An estimated 1.5 million illegal immigrants reside in the district, including gang members, the press release said, adding that California’s protection of criminal illegal aliens makes residents less safe.</p>

<p>The release noted that in February 2025, José Cristian Saravia-Sánchez, 30, of Mexico, shot and killed an Inglewood man who tried to stop him from stealing a catalytic converter, which garnered national attention.</p>

<p>He was an illegal immigrant who had been convicted of vehicle theft, removed from the United States in 2013, and arrested 11 times between June 2022 and August 2024, according to the release. However, local law enforcement was prevented by state law from complying with an immigration detainer request, the release stated.</p>

<p>The office of California Gov. Gavin Newsom did not immediately respond to a request for comment from The Epoch Times by publication time.</p>
</div>

<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-20T19:00:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 15:00</span>


Title: Rubio Says Syria Could Be 'Weeks Away' From Civil War, State Collapse (Again)
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Rubio Says Syria Could Be 'Weeks Away' From Civil War, State Collapse (Again)</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>US Secretary of State Marco Rubio last Thursday met with Syrian Foreign Minister Asaad al-Shaibani and other ruling Hayat Tahrir al-Sham (HTS) officials in Antalya, Turkey - just as President Trump controversially greeted Syria's new ruler Ahmed al-Sharaa (Jolani) in Riyadh. Rubio's was the first such US meeting with a Syrian foreign minister in fifteen years, the State Department later said.</p>

<p>Following this, Rubio on Tuesday went before the Senate Foreign Relations Committee to defend the administration's dropping of all Syria sanctions, in order to "give them a chance" - as Trump said of Syria while on his Gulf visit. Rubio sounded an alarm, warning that the already war-torn country <strong>could be weeks away from civil war </strong>and <strong>collapse</strong> of the HTS government. Watch:</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="560">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Syria is likely on the verge of 'full scale civil war' — Marco Rubio<br /><br />
The US state secretary laments the country's current rulers 'didn't pass their background check with the FBI' <a href="https://t.co/gBUH1gCYwa">https://t.co/gBUH1gCYwa</a> <a href="https://t.co/g2mY1UMcZC">pic.twitter.com/g2mY1UMcZC</a></p>
— RT (@RT_com) <a href="https://twitter.com/RT_com/status/1924851512376734033?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 20, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>"It is our assessment that, frankly, the transitional authority, given the challenges they’re facing, <strong>are maybe weeks — not many months — away from potential collapse </strong>and a full-scale civil war of epic proportions, basically the country splitting up," Rubio told the Senate hearing. There have for weeks been running street battles between HTS and Druze factions in the south and in suburbs of Damascus.</p>

<p>Describing the rationale behind dropping the years-long brutal US sanctions, Rubio said: "We want to help that government succeed, because the alternative is full-scale civil war and chaos, <strong>which would, of course, destabilize the entire region</strong>."</p>

<p>Of course, the supreme and dark irony here is that it was Washington which led destabilization efforts in Syria over the last decade in the first place, with the CIA's <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/08/02/world/middleeast/cia-syria-rebel-arm-train-trump.html">Operation Timber Sycamore</a>. Assad fled the country on December 8, and since then the brutal Islamist group HTS and US-designated terrorist Sharaa/Jolani has ruled from Damascus.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">🔥everything is fine🔥 <a href="https://t.co/RIrzRbjLn3">pic.twitter.com/RIrzRbjLn3</a></p>
— Hassan Ridha (@sayed_ridha) <a href="https://twitter.com/sayed_ridha/status/1924844684595364136?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 20, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p><strong>To state the obvious, <em>just maybe</em> the US should <em>not </em>have sought to overthrow the largely secular government of Bashar al-Assad</strong>, which protected the minority religious communities now being massacred by HTS? Christians, Alawites, Druze, and secularists of all strips in Syria are now living in a new dark ages.</p>

<p>Rubio actually said before the senators that <strong>"When Syria is unstable, the region becomes unstable."</strong></p>

<p>But, he continued, "If we engage them, it may work out, it may not work out. If we did not engage them, it was guaranteed to not work out."</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Important “Islamic State Leader Omar al-Shishani Fought Under U.S. Umbrella as Late as 2013” by <a href="https://twitter.com/BradRHoff?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@BradRHoff</a> <a href="https://t.co/JQg5TwcLDp">https://t.co/JQg5TwcLDp</a></p>
— Joshua Landis (@joshua_landis) <a href="https://twitter.com/joshua_landis/status/707938546737262592?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">March 10, 2016</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>It should be recalled that over the past decades Rubio himself as a senator had <strong>called for regime change in Damascus</strong> on many occasions.</p>

<p>For example, in 2015 - at a moment the Islamic State was making gains in eastern Syria and across the region, Rubio <a href="https://www.presidency.ucsb.edu/documents/rubio-campaign-press-release-we-need-plan-stop-the-islamic-state-and-end-assads-regime-now">said</a> "Ending Assad's reign of terror once and for all will be, too. And both will be much more difficult than if we had acted at the outset of the civil war in Syria, <strong>as some of us urged President Obama and then-Secretary of State Hillary Clinton</strong>. But it is still not impossible."</p>

Title: US Shale Output Nearing Peak As Oil Prices Stagnate
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">US Shale Output Nearing Peak As Oil Prices Stagnate</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://oilprice.com/Energy/Energy-General/US-Shale-Output-Nearing-Peak-as-Oil-Prices-Stagnate.html"><em>Authored by Tsvetana Paraskova via OilPrice.com,</em></a></p>

<ul><li>
	<p>Low oil prices and economic uncertainty are causing U.S. oil production, particularly in shale basins, to plateau or decline earlier than anticipated.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Major oil companies acknowledge the accelerated peak in U.S. oil output, with the Permian Basin being the last major area still showing growth potential.</p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p>Forecasts for U.S. crude supply are being revised downward as the profitability of shale production is challenged by current oil prices.</p>
	</li>
</ul><p>The decline in oil prices and the prevailing uncertainty about the economy, trade, and supply chains are accelerating the peak in U.S. oil production despite President Donald Trump’s<strong> ‘drill, baby, drill’ </strong>slogan.  </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-16_dqnyjhsqgw.jpg?itok=p4Fi5xzK" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-16_dqnyjhsqgw.jpg?itok=p4Fi5xzK"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a714c979-5485-48c2-a4e0-322bee471c0a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="209" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-16_dqnyjhsqgw.jpg?itok=p4Fi5xzK" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>With the U.S. benchmark <a href="https://oilprice.com/oil-price-charts/#WTI-Crude">WTI crude prices</a> at $60 per barrel, it’s mostly “hold, baby, hold” in the American shale patch, where output in the major basins except the Permian has already started to level off or drop. </strong></p>

<p>The U.S.-China 90-day tariff pause and the start of trade talks did little to erase the crash in oil prices from April, and even less to restore confidence or wipe out the high uncertainty regarding the economy and the cost of supply with unknown levels of tariffs. The shale patch has historically been immediately responsive to changing market conditions, but living in 90-day cycles of tariffs, no-tariffs, reduced tariffs, or surprise U.S. geopolitical moves could be too much for the oil industry, especially the smaller companies. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/bfm7C56_0.jpg?itok=1A3bmswv" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/bfm7C56_0.jpg?itok=1A3bmswv"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="b0799e29-e924-4061-9735-f89ba2629b85" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="256" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/bfm7C56_0.jpg?itok=1A3bmswv" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The big ones, including ExxonMobil, Chevron, Occidental, and ConocoPhillips, aren’t voicing publicly concerns about doing business and doing it as usual at $60 oil. But some of them have already said that the peak in U.S. oil production is being accelerated and could be sooner than previously expected. </p>

<p>The peak, whenever it occurs, does not mean a steep decline afterwards—it would rather be a long plateau of leveling off of U.S. crude oil production in which the slowdown in shale would be partly offset by rising output from the U.S. Gulf of Mexico, executives and analysts say.  </p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>“As you know that most of the shale basins now have either plateaued or starting to decline, except for the Permian,” </strong></em>Vicki Hollub, President and CEO of Occidental Petroleum, <a href="https://www.oxy.com/siteassets/documents/investors/quarterly-earnings/oxy1q25transcript.pdf">said</a> on the Q1 earnings call. </p>

<p><em>“If companies continue to talk about dropping activity levels, I think the Permian could plateau sooner than we expected - and we had expected the Permian to continue growth through 2027,” Hollub added. </em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>Oxy had expected that U.S. production overall would peak between 2027 and 2030. </p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>“It's looking like with the current headwinds or at least volatility and uncertainty around pricing and the economy and recessions and all of that - it's looking like that peak could come sooner,”</strong></em> Hollub said, adding that the Permian would grow very little this year, if at all.  </p>
</blockquote>

<p>Ryan Lance, the chief executive of ConocoPhillips, <a href="https://static.conocophillips.com/files/resources/cop-usq_transcript_2025-05-08.pdf">said</a> on the company’s earnings call that at $60 oil, “the folks that don't have the kind of cost of supply sitting in their portfolio are going to find themselves cash-strapped and returns-strapped.”</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em><strong>“Obviously, the balance sheets are in pretty good shape across the industry, better than we were in the last downturn, but you'll see a lot of activity cut back,”</strong></em> Lance added. </p>
</blockquote>

<p>At current prices, ConocoPhillips doesn’t expect a lot of things to change for the company, although there would be changes if WTI sinks to $50 per barrel. However, “that's not our view today and doesn't represent where we think the market is going to be for the next few years,” Lance noted. </p>

<p>The current mantra at ConocoPhillips is “don't whipsaw this thing too hard right now…so don't overreact, but don't put your head in the sand either.” </p>

<p><strong>Earlier this month, Diamondback Energy said onshore oil production in the U.S. <a href="https://oilprice.com/Latest-Energy-News/World-News/Shale-Major-Sees-US-Oil-Production-Peaking.html">has already peaked</a>. </strong></p>

<p>“We currently estimate that the U.S. frac crew count is already down ~15% this year, with the Permian Basin crew count down ~20% from its January peak, and both are expected to decline further,” Diamondback said in a <a href="https://www.diamondbackenergy.com/news-releases/news-release-details/letter-stockholders-issued-diamondback-energy-inc-7">letter</a> to investors. </p>

<p>Liberty Energy, the fracking company founded by now-Energy Secretary Chris Wright, is also prepping for a <a href="https://oilprice.com/Latest-Energy-News/World-News/US-Fracking-Company-Forecasts-Major-Shale-Slowdown.html">slowdown in shale drilling</a>.  </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/bfm78B9_0.jpg?itok=ZCfsg-WY" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/bfm78B9_0.jpg?itok=ZCfsg-WY"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="51b8a987-801d-45be-a180-71fdbe82d17f" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="256" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/bfm78B9_0.jpg?itok=ZCfsg-WY" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>U.S. crude oil supply will rise more slowly than expected for the rest of 2025 and in 2026 and <a href="https://oilprice.com/Energy/Energy-General/US-Crude-Oil-Output-to-Peak-Sooner-Than-Expected.html">peak as early as this year</a>, as WTI prices at $60 per barrel are testing the breakeven point of shale production, energy flows intelligence firm Kpler said last week. </p>

<p><strong>With the low oil prices, Kpler <a href="https://x.com/Kpler/status/1919355178756559254">has now cut</a> its U.S. crude supply forecast by 120,000 barrels per day (bpd) to 170,000 bpd for the rest of 2025 and into 2026, “as weaker prices threaten to slow shale production.”  </strong></p>

<p>Despite steady near-term activity, growth is slowing in the U.S. shale patch, and U.S. crude output is set to peak this year, Kpler noted. </p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-20T18:20:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 14:20</span>


Title: The Red Line: Democratic Officials Claim A Dangerous License For Illegality
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">The Red Line: Democratic Officials Claim A Dangerous License For Illegality</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://jonathanturley.org/2025/05/20/the-red-line-democratic-officials-claim-a-license-for-illegality/"><em>Authored by Jonathan Turley,</em></a></p>

<p><strong>Across the country, a new defense is being heard in state and federal courtrooms. </strong>From Democratic members of Congress to judges to city council members, officials claim that their official duties include obstructing the official functions of the federal government. </p>

<p>It is <strong>a type of liberal license that excuses most any crime in the name of combating what Minn. Gov. Tim Walz called the “<a href="https://thehill.com/homenews/state-watch/5307956-minnesota-gov-tim-walz-gestapo-trump/">modern-day Gestapo</a>”</strong> of the Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE).</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/images%20%283%29_15.jpg?itok=dH3leeO6" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/images%20%283%29_15.jpg?itok=dH3leeO6"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="79547ee7-7211-46de-adda-0dfb3c7b7164" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="335" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/images%20%283%29_15.jpg?itok=dH3leeO6" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The latest claimant of this license is Rep. LaMonica McIver (D-NJ), who was charged with assaulting, resisting, and impeding law enforcement officers during a protest at Delaney Hall ICE detention facility in Newark, New Jersey. McIver is shown on <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kqIDzHUixco">video</a> forcing her way into an ICE facility and striking and shoving agents in her path.</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/kqIDzHUixco" title="DHS Releases Video Of Rep. McIver At Delaney Hall Detention Center—Now She Is Being Charged By DOJ" width="560"></iframe></p>

<p><strong>This was not a major incursion, but these state and federal officials joined a mob in briefly overwhelming security and breaching the fence barrier after a bus was allowed through the entrance. </strong>Federal officials were able to quickly force back the incursion.</p>

<p>McIver and House Democrats insisted that McIver’s forcing her way into the facility might be trespass and assault for other citizens, but she was merely exercising “legislative oversight.” Rep. Alexandria Ocacio-Cortez (D., N.Y.) <a href="https://www.aol.com/border-czar-homan-shrugs-off-230503183.html">declared</a> “You lay a finger on someone – on Bonnie Watson Coleman or any of the representatives that were there – you lay a finger on them, we’re going to have a problem.”</p>

<p><strong>Minority Leader Hakeem Jeffries (D., N.Y.) even ominously warned the federal government that Democrats would bring down the house if it tried to charge McIver: “It’s a red line. They know better than to go down that road.”</strong></p>

<p>Well, the red line was crossed in a big way after Acting U.S. Attorney for the District of New Jersey Alina Habba charged McIver with a felony under Title 18, United States Code, Section 111(a)(1).</p>

<p><strong>The ACLU <a href="https://www.aclu.org/press-releases/aclu-and-aclu-of-new-jersey-react-to-trump-administrations-charges-against-congresswoman-mciver">called</a> the charged “authoritarianism” and insisted that these state and federal politicians “have every right to exercise their legally authorized oversight responsibilities for expanded immigration detention in New Jersey.”</strong></p>

<p>The problem with the oversight claim is that McIver’s status as a member of Congress does not allow her access into closed federal facilities. Congress can subpoena the Executive Branch or secure court orders for access. However, member do not have immunity from criminal laws in unilaterally forcing their way into any federal office or agency.</p>

<p>If that were the case, Rep. Alexandria Ocacio-Cortez would not have posted images of herself <a href="https://thehill.com/homenews/house/450315-photographer-shares-photos-of-ocasio-cortez-at-border-after-concentration-camp/">crying at the fence</a> of an immigrant facility, she could have climbed over the fence in the name of oversight.</p>

<p>Conversely, Republicans in the Biden Administration could have simply pushed their way into the Justice Department to seek the files on the influence-peddling scandal.</p>

<p><strong>Yet, the point of the claim is less of a real criminal defense and more of a political excuse.</strong></p>

<p>It is the same claim being heard this week from Worcester City Councilor Etel Haxhiaj who was shown in a <a href="https://whdh.com/news/worcester-police-release-bodycam-footage-of-ice-arrest/">video shoving</a> and obstructing ICE officers attempting to arrest a woman on immigration charges. Two other individuals (including a Democratic candidate for a school board) were arrested, but not Haxhiaj who claimed that she was merely protecting “a constituent.” After the melee, the city manager issued an order preventing city police from assisting in any way in the carrying out of such civil immigration enforcement efforts by the federal government.</p>

<p><strong>Even judges are claiming the same license.</strong> </p>

<p>In Wisconsin, Judge Hannah Dugan has been charged with obstructing a federal arrest of an illegal immigrant who appeared in her courtroom. Dugan heard about agents waiting outside in the hallway to arrest the man and went outside to confront the agents. She told them to speak to the Chief Judge and that they needed a different warrant.</p>

<p><strong>The agents complied and the Chief Judge confirmed that they could conduct the arrest. In the interim, however, Dugan led the man out a non-public door and facilitated his escape (he was arrested after a chase down a public street).</strong></p>

<p>Judge Duggan also claimed that she was carrying out her duties even though her hearing was over, the charges were not part of state matter, and the arrest was being carried out outside of her courtroom.</p>

<p>As Democratic leaders like Walz engage in rage rhetoric and paint Republicans (and federal law enforcement) as Nazis, political violence across the country. Many of the people burning Teslas and engaging in such crimes claim the same type of license that the ends justify the means. That includes affluent professionals who are now <a href="https://jonathanturley.org/2025/04/07/the-american-jacobin-how-some-on-the-left-have-found-release-in-an-age-of-rage/">shoplifting from Whole Foods</a> as a “protest” against Jeff Bezos meeting with Trump.</p>

<p>When the Administration sought to investigate those burning Teslas and dealerships, Rep. Dan Goldman (D., N.Y.) <a href="https://jonathanturley.org/2025/03/27/rep-goldman-the-fbi-investigation-of-tesla-attacks-is-political-weaponization/">denounced</a> it as a “political weaponization” of the legal system. The comments suggest that such arson is somehow a form of political expression on the left.</p>

<p><strong>House Minority Leader Jeffries was correct that a “red line” was crossed but not the one that he was thinking of in threatening consequences for any charges. The red line is the one separating political expression and criminal conduct.</strong></p>

<p>Border Czar stressed repeatedly to political leaders that they can protest and refuse to help but “you can‘t cross the line” into obstruction and interference with their operations.</p>

<p>If oversight means that members can force their way into any federal facilities, we would have 535 roaming inspectors general who could wander at will through the executive branch.</p>

<p><strong>Rep. McIver would be better to claim a different type of oversight, in allowing her passion to briefly overwhelm her judgment in rushing into the facility.</strong></p>

<p>In the end, however, McIver and Duggan may have a license of a different kind.</p>

<p><strong>Both have an advantage of being charged in liberal districts where they would appear before sympathetic jurors.</strong>  They need to just convince a single jury to engage in “jury nullification,” to vote based on the cause, not the crime, in the case.</p>

<p><em>Jonathan Turley is the Shapiro professor of public interest law at George Washington University and the author of “</em><a href="https://nam11.safelinks.protection.outlook.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2Fexec%2Fobidos%2FASIN%2F1668047047%3Ftag%3Dsimonsayscom&data=05%7C02%7CDFreddoso%40thehill.com%7Cce3c9dc02c24470c534008dd12d814f1%7C9e5488e2e83844f6886cc7608242767e%7C1%7C0%7C638687441535176515%7CUnknown%7CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJFbXB0eU1hcGkiOnRydWUsIlYiOiIwLjAuMDAwMCIsIlAiOiJXaW4zMiIsIkFOIjoiTWFpbCIsIldUIjoyfQ%3D%3D%7C0%7C%7C%7C&sdata=k5fEv5U%2FfqcDIOipOj6kSiPbIfFkv2RL3ryF6pALU%2BE%3D&reserved=0"><em>The Indispensable Right: Free Speech in an Age of Rage</em></a><em>.”</em></p>
</div>

<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-20T17:40:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Tue, 05/20/2025 - 13:40</span>


Title: US Should Never Have Gotten 'Entangled' In Ukraine 'Death Trap': Trump
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">US Should Never Have Gotten 'Entangled' In Ukraine 'Death Trap': Trump</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>President Trump following Monday's <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/trump-speak-putin-zelensky-monday-toward-ending-ukraine-bloodbath">phone calls</a> with Russia's Vladimir Putin and Ukraine's Volodymyr Zelensky said that the United States <strong>should have never intervened in Ukraine</strong> in the first place.</p>

<p>He blasted his predecessor Joe Biden for sinking boundless billions in arms and aid into Kiev's coffers and yet it has only been a "death trap" and "real mess" which US decision-makers should have avoided altogether. "<strong>This is not my war. We got ourselves entangled in something we shouldn't have been involved in, and we would have been a lot better off. It's a real mess. It's a death trap</strong>," he said before reporters Monday afternoon.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/ukrwrfile.jpg?itok=Qq6aO_Lo" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/ukrwrfile.jpg?itok=Qq6aO_Lo"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0f4a4c9d-dbfe-4c06-b24d-c7564e6d41ed" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/ukrwrfile.jpg?itok=Qq6aO_Lo" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Via Reuters</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p><strong>"I do have a certain line, but I don't want to say what that line is because I think it makes the negotiation even more difficult than it is</strong>," Trump asserted. When pressed, he refrained from divulging what precisely that red line is in the press briefing.</p>

<p>Trump also addressed the ever-present potential for the US to get drawn in deeper, which is why he said this should be Europe's mess and responsibility, and not the United States'.</p>

<p>"We don’t have boots on the ground, we wouldn’t have boots on the ground. But we do have a big stake. The financial amount that was put up is just crazy," he added.</p>

<p>"Again,<strong> this was a European situation</strong>. It should have remained a European situation. But we got involved – much more than Europe did – because the past administration felt very strongly that we should," he said. <strong>"We gave massive amounts, I think record-setting amounts, both weaponry and money."</strong></p>

<p>Watch a key segment of the Trump presser:</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Reporter: “Do you have a red line of what would cause you to back away?”<br /><br />
Trump: “Yeah, in my head, but not something I'm going to announce…This isn't our war…We got ourselves entangled in something that we shouldn't have been involved in.” <a href="https://t.co/tVCZcyfLhj">pic.twitter.com/tVCZcyfLhj</a></p>
— The Bulwark (@BulwarkOnline) <a href="https://twitter.com/BulwarkOnline/status/1924579231465357662?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 19, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Meanwhile, in the wake of the Trump-Putin call, which lasted over two hours, <strong>the mainstream media has been slamming the US president as essentially giving Putin a free hand</strong>. President Trump had said it went "very well" and that he seems "an imminent end to the war".</p>

<p>For example, below is The Washington Post's perspective in a fresh <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2025/05/20/trump-putin-call-ukraine-europe/">Tuesday report</a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p data-apitype="text" data-contentid="KDZF2G6ZQFE6HEQVYIGOGUT3FQ" data-el="text" dir="null"><em>A phone call between President Donald Trump and Russian President Vladimir Putin <strong>shut down an effort to pressure Russia into an immediate ceasefire</strong> and instead opened the way for continued fighting while lengthy negotiations take place — much to the consternation of Ukraine and its European allies Tuesday.</em></p>

<p data-apitype="text" data-contentid="63JY6EMDWRFXLHNIBNIM5D4OAE" data-el="text" dir="null"><em><strong>Trump’s abandonment of new sanctions on Russian indicated that he may be stepping away from involvement in the talks</strong>, something that his team has been flagging for weeks. Trump said Monday that the conditions for a ceasefire could only be agreed by the warring parties “because they know details of a negotiation that nobody else would be aware of.”</em></p>

<p data-apitype="text" data-contentid="2XNNLWU3Y5E5VMRELINVXN4PWY" data-el="text" dir="null"><em><strong>European leaders say they had originally been planning with U.S. officials to levy new sanctions on Russia if it did not declare an immediate ceasefire in Ukraine</strong>.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>And yet the reality is that the sanctions themselves would certainly escalate the conflict and proxy war further, providing even less of an opportunity for a diplomatic off-ramp, and Trump knows this.</p>

<p>Trump had written just after the call: "Russia and Ukraine will immediately start negotiations toward a Ceasefire and, more importantly, an END to the War.</p>

<p><em>Growing impatience on all sides, even among Trump supporters and conservatives, amid fears that the proxy war could just continue endlessly...</em></p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Trump continues to pose as a mediator while simultaneously supplying weapons and intelligence to Ukraine. <a href="https://t.co/Q8vzJr7Bbz">pic.twitter.com/Q8vzJr7Bbz</a></p>
— Thomas Fazi (@battleforeurope) <a href="https://twitter.com/battleforeurope/status/1924754411756118124?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 20, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>He wrote on Truth Social, "The conditions for that will be negotiated between the two parties, as it can only be, because they know details of a negotiation that nobody else would be aware of. </p>

<p>He then emphasized, <strong>"The tone and spirit of the conversation were excellent. If it wasn’t, I would say so now, rather than later</strong>."</p>

Title: Coinbase Data Leak Could Put Users In Physical Danger; TechCrunch Founder
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Coinbase Data Leak Could Put Users In Physical Danger; TechCrunch Founder</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://cointelegraph.com/news/coinbase-breach-physical-crime-techcrunch-founder"><em>Authored by Zoltan Vardai via CoinTelegraph.com,</em></a></p>

<p>A recent data breach at crypto exchange Coinbase has raised concerns about user safety after hackers gained access to sensitive information, including home addresses.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/0193d4f8-f1c9-7318-8ce2-28cfe013.jpg?itok=pVVCEec_" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/0193d4f8-f1c9-7318-8ce2-28cfe013.jpg?itok=pVVCEec_"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="80fc3cd2-3a6c-477a-9ced-d1d36c14b354" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/0193d4f8-f1c9-7318-8ce2-28cfe013.jpg?itok=pVVCEec_" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Coinbase, the world’s third-largest cryptocurrency exchange, confirmed that less than 1% of its transacting monthly users were affected in an attack that may cost the <a href="https://cointelegraph.com/news/cyber-criminals-steal-coinbase-customer-data-20-m-ransom">exchange up to $400 million</a> in reimbursement expenses, Cointelegraph reported on May 15.</p>

<p>However, the “human cost” of this data breach may be much higher for users, according to Michael Arrington, the founder of TechCrunch and Arrington Capital.</p>

<p><strong>“Very disappointed in Coinbase right now.</strong> Using the cheapest option for customer service has its price,” Arrington said in a May 20 X <a href="https://x.com/arrington/status/1924587249674412266">post</a>, adding:</p>

<blockquote><strong>“Something that has to be said though - this hack - which includes home addresses and account balances - will lead to people dying. It probably has already.</strong>”</blockquote>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/0196ed07-ec36-7bf7-b81a-6df082e9.jpg?itok=Izc9-4k9" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/0196ed07-ec36-7bf7-b81a-6df082e9.jpg?itok=Izc9-4k9"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="837bf29d-9501-4807-b6ca-62903fb6d34a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/0196ed07-ec36-7bf7-b81a-6df082e9.jpg?itok=Izc9-4k9" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><em>Source: Michael </em><a href="https://x.com/arrington/status/1924587249674412266"><em>Arrington</em></a></p>

<p>While no passwords, private keys or account funds were exposed, cybercriminals reportedly bribed overseas customer service contractors to access internal systems. This allowed them to steal personal data that could be used in social engineering scams or even physical extortion attempts.</p>

<p><strong>With Bitcoin trading above $100,000, crypto wealth has <a href="https://cointelegraph.com/news/100k-bitcoin-impacts-wealth-gap-digital-age">become a growing target for criminals</a>.</strong> Experts warn that leaked address data could expose high-net-worth individuals to real-world risks.</p>

<p>On May 16, Cointelegraph reported on <a href="https://cointelegraph.com/news/violent-crypto-robberies-rise-six-attacks-investors">six violent robberies</a> that targeted cryptocurrency investors, aiming to extort digital assets via kidnapping or torture.</p>

<p>In a ruthless attack on May 4, the father of a French crypto entrepreneur was <a href="https://edition.cnn.com/2025/05/04/europe/crypto-entrepreneur-finger-severed-intl-latam">abducted</a> in Paris, France. The kidnappers cut the victim’s finger and sent a video to his son, demanding 5 million euros in crypto.</p>

<p>The victim was held for two days before French police were able to find and rescue him. According to CNN, five people were <a href="https://edition.cnn.com/2025/05/04/europe/crypto-entrepreneur-finger-severed-intl-latam">arrested</a> in connection with the kidnapping.</p>

<h2>Crypto exchanges need “layered” cybersecurity</h2>

<p>To prevent similar user data breaches, crypto exchanges need to adopt a “layered defense strategy,” according to Ronghui Gu, the co-founder of CertiK Web3 security firm.</p>

<p>“This can include privileged access management, zero trust architecture, multifactor authentication across internal systems, and continuous monitoring with behavioral analytics,” Gu told Cointelegraph, adding: </p>

<blockquote><em><strong>“Preventive measures such as regular phishing simulations, tailored security training, and restricting third-party access to sensitive systems may help reduce these risks.”</strong></em></blockquote>

<p>However, crypto platforms will need to “rethink their security posture” as attackers “increasingly target human vulnerabilities rather than technical ones,” added Gu, warning of the rising threat of social engineering schemes.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/01942bf5-7206-76b5-abfe-161a827b.jpg?itok=TTvUbCYr" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/01942bf5-7206-76b5-abfe-161a827b.jpg?itok=TTvUbCYr"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="2c257832-ec0c-4ded-b2e3-2b1a70bea8e4" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="239" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/01942bf5-7206-76b5-abfe-161a827b.jpg?itok=TTvUbCYr" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><em>Incidents and losses in 2024 by month. Source: CertiK</em></p>

<p><strong>Social engineering schemes, such as <a href="https://cointelegraph.com/news/phishing-scams-top-crypto-threat-2024-certik">phishing scams, were</a> the most significant security threat of 2024, costing the industry over $1 billion across 296 incidents, </strong>according to CertiK.</p>

Title:  “就像船即将触礁，但掌舵人却在争论该往哪个方向转弯”，投资者质疑特朗普减税法案加剧债务 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">美债市场正处于暴风雨前夜，特朗普政府推进的巨额减税法案恐将成为压垮骆驼的最后一根稻草。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">美国国会委员会在周日通过的预算法案将预计将在未来十年增加数万亿美元的联邦赤字。这项法案和信用评级下调加剧了人们对美国公共财政可持续性的担忧，而许多投资者和分析师表示，美国的债务和赤字已经处于令人不安的高水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">在接受媒体采访时，桥水基金亿万富翁创始人达利欧（Ray Dalio）对此表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>“这就像一艘船即将触礁，而掌舵人却在争论该往哪个方向转弯。我不太关心他们是向左转还是向右转，我更关心的是他们能否让船回到正确的航道上。”</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">税改法案引爆恐慌，“债市义警”准备就绪</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">据悉，这项税改方案将延长特朗普在其第一个任期内通过的大规模减税政策，还计划大幅削减针对低收入人群的医疗保险计划和食品援助计划。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">白宫新闻秘书Karoline Leavitt周一表示，该法案“不会增加赤字”，呼应了特朗普政府其他官员的说法，即减税将加速经济增长。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">然而，据无党派组织Committee for a Responsible Federal Budget估计，该立法将使公共债务到2034年底增加至少3.3万亿美元。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">该组织表示，<strong>这还将使债务占GDP比率从当前的100%增至创纪录的125%，远超现行法律下预测的同期117%的水平；年度赤字将从2024年约6.4%的GDP比例升至6.9%。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">在众议院预算委员会推进该立法以及穆迪下调美国评级之后，30年期美债收益率周一飙升至5.04%的峰值，创下2023年以来的最高水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Garda Capital Partners首席投资官Tim Magnusson表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">“我们正处于国债市场的一个转折点，为了让国债维持在当前水平，我们需要尽快获得有关赤字的好消息。如果需要有人来约束，那将是债券市场。”</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">Yardeni Research总裁Edward Yardeni指出：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>“债市义警已经准备就绪，他们准备采取行动了。”</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">全球资本开始对美国失去信心</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>财政担忧和关税政策的不确定性使投资者更加关注他们对美元资产的敞口。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">DoubleLine投资集团的投资组合经理Bill Campbell指出，该公司对20年期和30年期美国国债“低配”，认为该国“看起来没有认真努力控制债务的迹象”。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">德意志银行的George Saravelos表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>“对美国资产的购买意愿下降以及美国财政程序难以控制高赤字，是造成市场高度紧张的原因。”</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">在达利欧看来，美国需要迅速通过某种组合方式将赤字削减至GDP的3%，包括减少支出、增加收入和降低实际借贷成本。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">随着美国国会继续推进特朗普的减税政策，美国公共财政的未来前景变得愈加黯淡，投资者可能很快就要为美国政府的“放纵”付出代价。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  继美国之后，欧洲也对小额包裹“加税” 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">据媒体报道，欧盟计划对进入该地区的数十亿件小包裹征收每件2欧元的统一费用（“flat fee”）。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">欧盟贸易事务专员塞夫乔维奇（Maros Sefcovic）于周二向欧盟提议征收这项费用，以抵消每年46亿件直接寄往居民家中的包裹产生的相关成本。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">欧盟委员会草案显示，<strong>2欧元费用将适用于寄给消费者的商品，而发往仓库的包裹将按每件0.5欧元征收费用。</strong>媒体数据显示，去年有超10亿件包裹通过欧盟主要物流枢纽荷兰和比利时入境。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据悉，这项提议旨在帮助欧盟应对大量廉价商品涌入所带来的挑战，被视为欧盟加强海关管理、保护本地产业与消费者安全的重要举措。塞夫乔维奇宣称，汹涌的包裹潮给欧盟带来了监管、安全等方面的新挑战。他表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">我不认为这是税收，这只是…对成本的补偿，应该由平台支付。</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">这一举措与美国采取的类似措施相呼应。据央视财经报道，从5月2日起，美国取消对中国小额包裹免税政策正式生效，所有价值不超过800美元的小额包裹都要被征收关税。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">当前，<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747489" target="_blank" rel="noopener">日本也考虑对进口小额包裹征税</a>。据媒体报道，日本财务部正在考虑对包括小额包裹的免税政策进行审查。按照日本税制改革计划，预计2026年将制定出详细的税收新政策，在此之前，进口免税政策将继续推行。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  为了跟AI搜索竞争，谷歌越来越像Perplexity？ 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">谷歌正式推出“AI模式”功能，彻底重塑搜索引擎，正面迎战Perplexity、ChatGPT等AI对手的威胁。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">5月21日，据报道，谷歌正在搜索页面上推出一项名为“AI模式”的功能，该功能以聊天机器人风格的对话方式回答搜索查询，而不再显示传统的蓝色链接。这一选项已作为搜索页面内的标签向美国用户开放。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">谷歌母公司Alphabet的首席执行官Sundar Pichai表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">&#34;这是对搜索的完全重新构想，具有更先进的推理能力。我们现在正进入AI平台转变的新阶段，数十年的研究正在成为现实。&#34;</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">这一变化标志着谷歌正在积极应对Perplexity、OpenAI等人工智能初创企业对其标志性的搜索引擎产品和最大收入来源的威胁。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">AI搜索颠覆传统模式，谷歌市场份额受威胁</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">人工智能聊天机器人正从根本上改变用户搜索信息的方式。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">在回应查询时，OpenAI的ChatGPT及其竞争对手会以对话形式聚合信息。用户不像使用谷歌搜索时那样频繁点击多个链接。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">谷歌曾执行全球高达90%的互联网搜索。如果用户转向AI驱动的替代方案，它可能会失去流量——以及由此带来的广告收入。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">值得注意的是，本月早些时候，在针对谷歌的联邦反垄断案中，苹果高管称，未来一年内可能会在Safari浏览器中提供ChatGPT或Perplexity等AI选项，这一消息导致Alphabet股价大幅下滑。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">谷歌的反击战略，全力押注AI</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">为了在AI竞赛中领先，谷歌一直在改进其自身AI模型和聊天机器人Gemini的能力，并将AI功能添加到许多产品中。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">去年，谷歌在搜索中引入了&#34;AI概览&#34;，该功能使用AI总结传统搜索结果，通常显示在结果页面的顶部。据谷歌表示，该功能现在拥有15亿月活跃用户。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">近几个月来，谷歌一直在试验&#34;AI模式&#34;。该功能提供类似于使用其他AI聊天机器人的搜索体验。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">在新的推出计划中，使用谷歌搜索的人可以点击标签开启&#34;AI模式&#34;，该功能将由Gemini提供支持。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">谷歌搜索产品副总裁Robby Stein表示，公司正在考虑如何在“AI模式”结果中加入广告。他说，&#34;我们将其视为人们实际想要的内容组合的一部分。&#34;</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  从投行到交易员，华尔街已准备好：10年美债收益率冲击5% 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">随着特朗普税改法案引发美国债务和赤字担忧升级，交易员正大举押注10年期美债收益率将飙至5%。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据彭博报道，交易员正大规模押注长期美债收益率将因美国政府不断膨胀的债务和赤字担忧而飙升，而特朗普的减税法案使这一局面变得更加危险。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">报道称，包括高盛和摩根大通在内的华尔街策略师正在上调他们的收益率预测。其中，押注10年期美债收益率将达到5%的头寸规模最大。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>CME的未平仓合约数据显示，市场出现了大规模押注十年期美债收益率在未来几周内攀升至5%的期权交易，金额规模高达1100万美元。</strong></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">评级下调引发恐慌，30年期美债收益率触及5%关口</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">周一，30年期美债收益率短暂突破5%，达到自2023年11月以来的最高水平，随后回落。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">这一抛售潮是由穆迪将美国信用评级从Aaa下调至Aa1引发的，这导致各期限美债收益率在周一早盘交易中全线走高，之后回落抹平涨幅。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">摩根大通的策略师Jay Barry和Jason Hunter在一份报告中写道：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">“考虑到贸易和货币政策的不确定性，以及需求格局的结构性转变，短期内风险偏向于熊市陡峭化。”</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">根据报告，<strong>对冲长期美债曲线末端可能出现的更大损失的期权金额目前已升至4月以来最高水平，</strong>当时市场正被特朗普激进贸易政策可能带来的经济影响所动摇。当前期权偏斜的走势意味着，交易员正推高看跌期权的价格，以对冲收益率飙升的风险。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">投资者快速转向空头阵营，期权市场异动频现</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">周二发布的摩根大通美债客户调查也强调了对更高债券收益率的预期。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告显示，<strong>美债看空头寸攀升至2月10日以来的最高水平。</strong>然而，由于投资者仓位比4月初更为中性，策略师预计“波动幅度将明显小于上个月”。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">最近几周，针对收益率上升进行对冲的期权流动趋势已经形成，这反映在所谓的“期权偏斜”中，即显示期权价格上升以反映债券市场的抛售。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>交易员正支付越来越多的费用来对冲曲线长端的抛售，</strong>与周一美国30年期国债收益率突破5%水平以及最近美国国债收益率曲线陡峭化的走势相符。长期债券合约中看跌期权的偏斜度现已达到约一个月来的最高水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">截至5月13日的一周，CFTC数据显示，<strong>资产管理公司清算了大量多头头寸，对冲基金则平仓了空头头寸。</strong></p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  期权市场对美元的看法，从来没有这么悲观 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">随着特朗普反复无常的关税政策和不断扩大的财政赤字引发市场担忧，期权交易员对美元未来前景的看空达到前所未有的水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">5月21日根据媒体报道，外汇期权市场的数据显示，交易员对美元未来一年走势的悲观情绪达到有记录以来的最高点。<strong>衡量期权市场买入与卖出某种货币成本差异的1年期风险逆转指标已跌至-27个基点，这意味着看跌期权较看涨期权明显更受青睐。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">报道指出，彭博美元即期指数2025年迄今已下跌超过6%，创下该指数二十年来的最差年度开局。<strong>数据显示，市场参与者目前持有约165亿美元押注美元下跌的头寸，几乎创下9月以来的最高水平</strong>。截至周三亚盘时段，美元指数再度跌至100整数关口下方，从年内高点已跌近10%。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/16f1c85c-9755-4b85-b6fd-1411b470f824.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="633" data-wscnw="913"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">美元信心崩塌的核心导火索在于美国政策的不确定性。特朗普反复无常的关税政策正在严重扰乱市场预期，让投资者质疑美国政策制定的可预测性以及经济增长前景。嘉信理财首席固定收益策略师Kathy Jones直言：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>结构性看跌美元观点仍在，因为关税形势的缓和只是暂时的。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>与此同时，<strong>美国财政状况日益恶化也加剧了市场对美元的担忧</strong>。</p>
<p>目前国会正在推进特朗普的大规模减税方案，这将进一步扩大已经高企的联邦赤字。穆迪评级机构上周五晚间更是剥夺了美国的AAA信用评级，理由是过去十年美国政府债务和利息支付大幅增加。</p>
<p>对于投资者而言，这种前所未有的美元悲观情绪意味着美国资产可能面临进一步资金外流压力，同时也提示全球投资组合配置可能需要增加对欧元、日元等替代货币的敞口。</p>
<p>然而，部分分析师也提醒，如此极端的看空情绪有时恰恰可能是美元即将反弹的信号，市场过度悲观可能为逆势交易创造机会。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title: Google is putting more AI in more places
Description: <p><a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/11/18/google-ai-gemini-user-data-training" target="_blank">Google</a> used this week's I/O developer conference to announce a slew of <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/google-ai-shopping-features-virtual-try-on-clothes" target="_blank">new AI features</a> and experiences, along with a new $250-a-month subscription service for those who want to access the company's latest tools. </p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> Google is aiming to prove that it can make its core products better <a href="https://www.axios.com/technology/automation-and-ai" target="_blank">through AI</a> without displacing its highly lucrative advertising and search businesses.</p><hr><p><strong>Key announcements</strong> Google made Tuesday:</p><ul><li>It debuted Flow, a new AI filmmaking tool that draws on the company's latest Veo 3 engine and adds audio capabilities. The company also announced Imagen 4, its latest image generator, which Google says is better at rendering text, among other improvements.</li><li>Google said it would soon make broadly available its latest Gemini 2.5 Flash and Pro models and add a new reasoning mode for the Pro model called Deep Think. </li><li>Google will make its AI Mode, a chat-like version of search, broadly available in the U.S. and it's updating the underlying model to use a custom version of Gemini 2.5.</li><li>It's also beginning to allow customers to give large language models access to their personal data — starting with the ability to generate personalized smart replies to Gmail messages that draw on a user's email history. That feature will be available for paying subscribers this summer, Google CEO Sundar Pichai said.</li><li>On the coding front, Google offered further details on Jules, its autonomous agent, which is now available in public beta. Microsoft and OpenAI have also announced new coding agents in recent days.</li></ul><p><strong>For those who want</strong> to make sure they can have the most access to Google's AI models, the company is introducing Google AI Ultra, a $250-a-month service.</p><ul><li>The high-end subscription — an alternative to the standard $20-a-month basic service — includes access to a number of its most powerful AI agents, models and services, as well as YouTube Premium and 30TB of cloud storage.</li></ul><p><strong>Also in Google's cavalcade of demos,</strong> the company showed an early prototype of its <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/08/google-ar-glasses-vr-headset-ted" target="_blank">Android XR glasses</a> searching, taking photos and performing live translation. </p><ul><li>The glasses have audio and camera features similar to <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/02/09/meta-ray-ban-smart-glasses-ai-review" target="_blank">Meta's Ray-Ban smart glasses</a>, but also offer an optional display. (Meta is also said to be working on a version of its glasses with a built-in display for later this year.)</li><li>Partners include Samsung and eyewear makers Warby Parker and Gentle Monster. </li></ul><p><strong>The big picture:</strong> Google's event comes a day after Microsoft made a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/microsoft-grok-elon-musk-cloud" target="_blank">slew of announcements</a> at its Build conference in Seattle. Anthropic, meanwhile, is holding its first-ever developer conference on Thursday in San Francisco.</p><p><em>Go deeper: </em><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/google-ai-shopping-features-virtual-try-on-clothes" target="_blank">Google upgrades AI tools for shopping</a></p>

href="https://link.axios.com/click/39715719.22/aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuY25iYy5jb20vMjAyNS8wNC8yNy9jb21wYW5pZXMtbGdidHEtcHJpZGUtZmVzdGl2YWxzLmh0bWw_dXRtX3NvdXJjZT1uZXdzbGV0dGVyJnV0bV9tZWRpdW09ZW1haWwmdXRtX2NhbXBhaWduPW5ld3NsZXR0ZXJfdGhvdWdodGJ1YmJsZV9jb21tdW5pY2F0b3JzX3BybyZzdHJlYW09dG9w/628251ac30c888840206c912B8cabe380" wishy-washy support of the LGBTQ+ community and its DEI rollbacks.</li></ul><p><strong>By the numbers: </strong>39% of corporations are scaling back external Pride Month engagements this year, Title: Johnson offers $40,000 SALT deduction cap with income limits
Description: <p>House Speaker Mike Johnson offered GOP holdouts a detailed proposal on Monday to set the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/14/mike-johnson-salt-deduction-cap-taxes" target="_blank">SALT deduction cap</a> at $40,000 for anyone who makes less than $751,600 a year.</p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> But Johnson (R-La.) also offered the SALT members an entirely different option: Figure out the math yourself, he said, according to a person familiar with the matter.</p><hr><ul><li>Johnson offered a crucial caveat: they still need to stay within the fiscal constraints of the Ways and Means framework, which has only has a set amount of money to spend on the SALT portion for the tax portions of the bill.</li><li>Johnson needs to resolve the SALT issue this week, but he doesn't have unlimited money to do it with.</li><li>"We continue to work on it," Johnson told reporters last night. "It's not a final resolution yet and I think we're getting very close."</li><li>Punchbowl News first reported, <a href="https://x.com/jakesherman/status/1924791698875466075?s=42" target="_blank">on X</a>, some of the details in Johnson's offer.</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news:</strong> Members of the SALT caucus appeared to be more interested in Johnson's second option.</p><ul><li>Rep. Andrew Garbarino (R-N.Y.) <a href="https://x.com/eleanor_mueller/status/1924666918981558651?s=46" target="_blank">told reporters last night</a> that "we have to follow up with Joint Committee on Tax and CBO on" on how much different proposals will cost. </li><li>"They hope to have some numbers back to us by the morning."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out:</strong> Johnson wants to signal flexibility to the half-a-dozen members who are threatening to vote against President Trump's <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/01/mike-johnson-republicans-medicaid-trump" target="_blank">one big, beautiful bill</a> if they don't get more relief for their constituents who are hit with high taxes in blue states.</p><ul><li>The SALT caucus had been eyeing an additional $200 billion in headspace based on the Ways and Means instructions to authorize a total of $4 trillion in spending.</li></ul><p><strong>By the numbers:</strong> There are firm income limits and phase-out in Johnson's proposal, according to the person familiar with the matter.</p><ul><li>For years 1-4: The deduction would be at $40,000 for anyone making less than $751,600. That includes individual and joint-filers.</li><li>For anyone making more than roughly $850,000, the deduction would be $10,000, with a $20,000 deduction at the $800,000 threshold.</li></ul><p><strong>Then starting in year five</strong>, both the deduction and the income levels drop.</p><ul><li>For anyone making less than $400,000 a year, the cap is at $30,000 in state and local taxes.</li><li>For anyone in the $400,000 to $450,000 range, the deduction would be $20,000. For $500,000 and up, the deduction is back at the $10,000 level.</li></ul>

Title: A Teacher Dragged a 6-Year-Old With Autism by His Ankle. Federal Civil Rights Officials Might Not Do Anything.
Description: 
                <p class="byline">
                by <a class="name" href="https://www.propublica.org/people/jennifer-smith-richards">Jennifer Smith Richards</a> and <a class="name" href="https://www.propublica.org/people/jodi-cohen">Jodi S. Cohen</a>                </p>
                                             

                                                                    
            
                <p>ProPublica is a nonprofit newsroom that investigates abuses of power. <a href="https://www.propublica.org/newsletters/dispatches?source=54G&amp;placement=top-note&amp;region=local">Sign up for Dispatches</a>, a newsletter that spotlights wrongdoing around the country, to receive our stories in your inbox every week.</p>

            

                

      
  



                    
<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.0">A short video taken inside an Illinois school captured troubling behavior: A teacher gripping a 6-year-old boy with autism by the ankle and dragging him down the hallway on his back.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.1">The early-April incident would’ve been upsetting in any school, but it happened at the Garrison School, part of a special education district where at one time students were arrested at the highest rate of any district in the country. The teacher was charged with battery weeks later after pressure from the student’s parents.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.2">It’s been about eight months since the U.S. Department of Education <a href="https://www.propublica.org/article/illinois-garrison-school-reform-student-discipline">directed Garrison to change the way it responded to the behavior of students with disabilities</a>. The department said it would monitor the Four Rivers Special Education District, which operates Garrison, following a ProPublica and Chicago Tribune investigation in 2022 that found the <a href="https://www.propublica.org/article/students-police-arrests-illinois-garrison-school">school frequently involved police and used controversial disciplinary methods</a>. </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.3">But the department’s Office for Civil Rights regional office in Chicago, which was responsible for Illinois and five other states, was one of seven abolished by President Donald Trump’s administration in March; the offices were closed and their entire staff was fired.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.4">The future of oversight at Four Rivers, in west-central Illinois, is now uncertain. There’s no record of any communication from the Education Department to the district since Trump took office, and his administration has terminated an antidiscrimination agreement with at least one school district, in South Dakota.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.5">In the April incident, Xander Reed, who has autism and does not speak, did not stop playing with blocks and go to P.E. when he was told to, according to a police report. Xander then “became agitated and fell to the ground,” the report said. When he refused to get up, a substitute teacher, Rhea Drake, dragged him to the gym.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="2.6">Another staff member took a photo and alerted school leadership. Principal Amy Haarmann told police that Drake’s actions “were not an acceptable practice at the school,” the police report said.</p>
        
    
                    
<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="4.0">Xander’s family asked to press charges. Drake, who had been working in Xander’s classroom for more than a month, was charged about three weeks later with misdemeanor battery, records show. She has pleaded not guilty. Her attorney told ProPublica that he and Drake did not want to comment for this story. </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="4.1">Tracey Fair, the district’s director, said school officials made sure students were safe following the incident and that Drake won’t be returning to the district. She declined to comment further about the incident, but said school officials take their “obligation to keep students and staff safe very seriously.” </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="4.2">Doug Thompson, chief of police in Jacksonville, where the school is located, said he could not discuss the case.</p>
        
    
                    

    
        

                        
                    
                

            A screenshot from a recording of a CCTV video shows Xander Reed being dragged down the hallway by a teacher at the Garrison School.
    
            (Obtained by ProPublica)
    
    
    

    

        
    
                    
<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="6.0">Xander’s mother, Amanda, said her son is fearful about going to Garrison, where she said he also has been punished by being put in a school “crisis room,” a small space where students are taken when staff feel they misbehave or need time alone. “He has not wanted to go to school,” she said. “We want him to get an education. We want him to be with other kids.”</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="6.1">Four Rivers serves an eight-county area, and students at Garrison range from kindergartners through high schoolers. About 70 students were enrolled at the start of the school year. Districts who feel they aren’t able to educate a student in neighborhood schools send them to Four Rivers; Xander travels 40 minutes each way to attend Garrison.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="6.2">The federal scrutiny of Garrison began after ProPublica and the Tribune revealed that during a five-year period, school employees called police to report student misbehavior every other school day, on average. Police made more than 100 arrests of students as young as 9 during that period. They were handcuffed and taken to the police station for being disruptive or disobedient; if they’d physically lashed out at staff, they often were charged with felony aggravated battery.</p>
        
    
                    

    
        

                        
                    
                

            Garrison School is part of a special education district that’s supposed to be under federal monitoring for violating the civil rights of its disabled students.
    
            (Bryan Birks for ProPublica)
    
    
    

    

        
    
                    
<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.0">The news organizations also found that Garrison employees frequently removed students from their classrooms and sent them to crisis rooms when the students were upset, disobedient or aggressive.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.1">The Office for Civil Rights’ <a href="https://ocrcas.ed.gov/sites/default/files/ocr-letters-and-agreements/05235001-a.pdf">findings echoed those of the news investigation</a>. It determined that Garrison routinely sent students to police for noncriminal conduct that could have been related to their disabilities — something prohibited by federal law. </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.2">The district was to report its progress in making changes to the OCR by last December, which it appears to have done, according to documents ProPublica obtained through a public records request.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.3">But the records show the OCR has not communicated with the district since then and it’s not clear what will come of the work at Four Rivers. The OCR has terminated at least one agreement it entered into last year — a deal with a South Dakota school district that had agreed to take steps to end discrimination against its Native American students. Spokespeople for the Education Department did not respond to questions from ProPublica.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.4">Scott Reed, 6-year-old Xander Reed’s father, said he and Xander’s mother were aware of the frequent use of police as disciplinarians at Four Rivers and of OCR’s involvement. But they reluctantly enrolled him this school year because they were told there were no other options.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.5">“You can say you’ve made all these changes, but you haven’t,” Scott Reed said. For example, he said, even after confirming that Drake had dragged the 50-pound boy down the hall, school leadership sent her home. “They did not call police until I arrived at school and demanded it” hours later, he said.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="8.6">“If that was a student” that acted that way, “they would have been in handcuffs.”</p>
        
    
                        

    
        

                            
                                                        
                                                        
                                

            Scott and Amanda Reed, Xander’s parents, enrolled their son in Garrison School after being told they had no other options.
    
            (Bryan Birks for ProPublica)
    
    
    

            
                    
    
                    
<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="10.0">New ProPublica reporting has found that since school began in August, police have been called to the school at least 30 times in response to student behavior. </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="10.1">Thompson, the police chief, told ProPublica that, in one instance, officers were summoned because a student was saying “inappropriate things.” They also were called last month after a report that a student punched and bit staff members. The officers “helped to calm the student,” according to the local newspaper’s police blotter. </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="10.2">And police have continued to arrest Garrison students. There have been six arrests of students for property damage or aggravated battery this school year, police data shows. A 15-year-old girl was arrested for spitting in a staff member’s face, and a 10-year-old boy was arrested after being accused of hitting an employee. There were at least nine student arrests last school year, according to police data.</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="10.3">Thompson said four students between the ages of 10 and 16 have been arrested this school year on the more serious aggravated battery charge; one of the students was arrested three times. He said he thinks police calls to Garrison are inevitable, but that school staff are now handling more student behavioral concerns without reaching out to police. </p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="10.4">“I feel like now the calls for service are more geared toward they have done what they can and they now need help,” Thompson said. “They have attempted to de-escalate themselves and the student is not cooperating still or it is out of their control and they need more assistance.”</p>

<p data-pp-blocktype="copy" data-pp-id="10.5">Police were called to the school last week to deal with “a disturbance involving a student,” according to the police blotter in Jacksonville’s local newspaper. It didn’t end in an arrest this time; a parent arrived and “made the student obey staff members.”</p>

Title: Comey Peddles Unbelievable Excuse For His '8647' Sea Shell Post...
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Comey Peddles Unbelievable Excuse For His '8647' Sea Shell Post...</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><a href="https://modernity.news/2025/05/20/comey-peddles-unbelievable-excuse-for-his-8647-sea-shell-post/"><em>Authored by Steve Watson via Modernity.news,</em></a></p>

<p><strong>Disgraced former FBI Director James Comey is playing dumb and innocent after essentially calling for President Trump to be assassinated last week, claiming he had no idea his post would be so controversial.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Comey.jpg?itok=s_WZxdPH" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Comey.jpg?itok=s_WZxdPH"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="e390f372-c780-435d-ac3b-cc0fd91dc4db" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Comey.jpg?itok=s_WZxdPH" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>After Comey posted an image of shells on a beach he arranged to read ‘8647’, meaning get rid of Trump, The Secret Service questioned him, but then let him go without any charges.</p>

<p><iframe class="wp-embedded-content" data-secret="hZLf6UtIS3" frameborder="0" height="500" marginheight="0" marginwidth="0" sandbox="allow-scripts" scrolling="no" security="restricted" src="https://modernity.news/2025/05/17/trump-supporters-rage-at-secret-service-for-not-arresting-comey/embed/#?secret=hZLf6UtIS3" title="“Trump Supporters Rage At Secret Service For Not Arresting Comey” — modernity" width="600"></iframe></p>

<p>Now, in an interview with MSNBC he claims he’s just a silly old fella who wears baggy jeans and sweaters and had no idea what he was doing.</p>

<p><em><strong>“I don’t know how we ended up here. Never occurred to me that it was any kind of controversial thing, but that’s the time we live in,” </strong></em>Comey told MSNBC’s Nicolle Wallace.</p>

<p>It’s got nothing to do with the time we live in, shit posting an image threatening to kill the President when you’re a deep state lackey is always going to cause outrage.</p>

<p>Comey then claimed that he wasn’t the one who arranged the shells, and they were put there by some other TDS addled leftist.</p>

<p><em><strong>“We were walking on the beach, we went to the beach to prepare for this week… and we were walking back towards the road and we saw in the sand someone had arranged shells with numbers. And Patrice, my wife, said, ‘why would someone put an address in the sand?’ and I said, ‘I don’t know’ and we stood over and I said, ‘I think it’s some kind of political message.'”</strong></em></p>

<p>Hurling his own wife under a bus, Comey then added, “She said you know, when I was a server – she did a lot of work in restaurants – 86 meant to remove an item from the menu when you ran out of ingredients. And I said, ‘well to me, as a kid it always meant to leave a place, to ditch a place.’ And she said well that’s very clever you should take a picture of that and I did and posted it on my Instagram and thought nothing more of it until I heard through her that people were saying that it was a call for some sort of assassination which is crazy!”</p>

<p>Pfffffft, SURE.</p>
