Title:  美债大跌，银行“接盘”？ 
Description:  <p>近期美债大跌，30年期美债收益率昨日午后一度突破5%，10年期美债收益率再次来到4.5%关口。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/0a99bd36-1b1a-41f2-9698-1153e5ac2437.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="607" data-wscnw="905" data-wscnsize="51231"/></p>
<p>美债大跌引发业内对政府出手救市的预期，然而，银行担心，最终接盘的还是自己。周二，前贝莱德基金经理、资深华尔街投资人Edward Dowd表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>“谁来买我们的国债？是我们自己……他们打算放松针对国债的SLR（补充杠杆率）监管，好让银行来接盘。”</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/288b8d14-75eb-4f0c-bf28-de0b923ac8b9.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="527" data-wscnw="599"/></p>
<p>据媒体此前报道，美国五名共和党议员致信美联储，呼吁调整监管，敦促美联储出手改善美债市场的流动性问题，并建议考虑“有针对性地”修改银行资本监管的规定，特别是涉及SLR的部分。</p>
<p>SLR是巴塞尔协议III的一部分，它的核心是银行必须为其全部资产（包括国债）预留一定比例的资本金，不能盲目扩张。如果银行囤太多国债，资本要求也会大幅上升，于是银行不愿意囤债、不积极买卖，影响了市场流动性。而对系统性重要的大型银行来说，还要遵守更严格的“增强版SLR”要求，使得问题更为突出。</p>
<p>美国国债市场规模庞大，目前已高达29万亿美元。最近几年，这个市场流动性有时会出问题，比如2020年疫情刚爆发那会儿，市场一度非常紧张，美联储不得不出手每天购买数十亿美元的美债来救场。</p>
<p>多位投资者和分析师认为，这类流动性紧张的背后，与SLR制度有关。美国部分国会议员呼吁美联储：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“我们建议美联储审慎评估是否可以进行有针对性的调整。”</p>
</blockquote>
<p>美联储官方暂时没有表态。不过鲍威尔上个月在国会听证会中曾表示支持降低SLR，还说：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“我确实预计我们会重新回到这个问题上来，跟其他机构的新同事们一起合作，把这事办成。”</p>
</blockquote><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  现金翻倍！哔哩哔哩Q1营收同比增24%，游戏业务同比大增76%，净利润3.62亿元 | 财报见闻 
Description:  <p>得益于月活用户、月均付费用户、日均使用时长均创历史新高，B站Q1营收同比增24%。同时，广告与游戏等高利润率业务营收大增，带动B站毛利率升至36.3%，Q1经调整后净利润较去年一季度扭亏为盈，经营现金流实现翻倍。</p>
<p>5月20日，哔哩哔哩发布未经审计的2025年第一季度财报。</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Q1营收同比增长24%至70.03亿元，市场预估为69.1亿元人民币。</p>
<p>Q1调整后每股收益0.86元人民币，去年同期亏损1.06元人民币。</p>
<p>Q1经调整净利润为3.62亿元，去年同期则为亏损4.56亿元。</p>
<p>Q1月活跃用户3.68亿，同比增长7.8%。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>哔哩哔哩美股盘前一度涨超4%，现涨幅收窄至逾2%。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/42ca331c-01db-4171-96dc-aedae28daf2b.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="439" data-wscnw="618" data-wscnsize="45278"/></p>
<h2>月均付费用户创新高，广告、游戏业务带动利润增长</h2>
<p>B站Q1营收同比增长24%至70.03亿元，经调整净利润为3.62亿元，去年同期则为亏损4.56亿元，实现扭亏为盈。</p>
<p>分业务看，B站四大收入来源呈现不同增长态势：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>增值服务：营收28.07亿元，同比增长11%，占总营收40%。</p>
<p>广告业务：营收19.98亿元，同比增长20%，占总营收28.5%。</p>
<p>手机游戏：营收17.31亿元，同比增长76%，占总营收24.7%。</p>
<p>IP衍生品及其他：营收4.67亿元，同比下降4%，占总营收6.8%。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>值得注意的是，游戏业务的突出表现主要来自独家授权游戏《三国：谋定天下》的强劲表现。游戏和广告业务毛利率通常高于增值服务，这一结构优化帮助B站整体毛利率提升。</p>
<p><strong>至于营收双位数增长的原因，CEO陈睿指出：</strong></p>
<blockquote>
<p>“B站用户基础及使用粘性继续增强。第一季度，日均活跃用户(DAU)达1.067亿，同比增长约4.2%；月活用户(MAU)创历史新高达3.68亿。<strong>更重要的是，月均付费用户达3200万，创下历史新高，表明用户付费意愿增强。</strong></p>
<p>日均使用时长达108分钟的新高，显示用户粘性增强。同时，用户群体渐趋成熟，2025年用户平均年龄达26岁，这一群体通常拥有更强的消费能力。</p>
<p>随着用户价值的提升和商业化效率的提升，我们第一季度的总净收入同比增长24%，达到人民币70亿元。</p>
<p>2025年我们以强劲的财务表现和健康的社区生态指标实现了开门红...我们将乘势而上，通过提供更高效、更优质的商业化解决方案持续释放社区潜力。&#34;</p>
</blockquote>
<p><strong>至于净利润扭亏为盈的原因，CFO樊欣指出：</strong></p>
<blockquote>
<p>“第一季度，我们加速了收入增长并提升了利润率。<strong>这得益于我们高利润率的广告和游戏业务的出色表现，这两个业务营收分别同比增长20%和76%。</strong>毛利润同比增长58%，毛利率从去年同期的28.3%上升至36.3%。</p>
<p>在强劲的收入和利润率增长的支撑下，我们实现了调整后净利润3.615亿元人民币。我们良性的运营周期继续推动强劲的经营现金流，本季度创造了13亿元人民币的现金流。</p>
<p>展望未来，我们将继续专注于盈利增长，通过高效、可持续的运营扩大业务规模和社区规模，并为股东创造长期价值。”</p>
</blockquote>
<p>成本管控方面，虽然总营收增长24%，但营业成本仅增长10%，远低于营收增速。其中，研发开支同比下降13%，体现了运营效率的提升。销售及营销开支同比增加26%，主要是由于春节联欢晚会独家弹幕直播的一次性营销开支以及《三国：谋定天下》的推广开支。</p>
<p><strong>公司经营现金流达13.02亿元，较去年同期的6.38亿元翻了一倍多</strong>，显示业务运营逐渐步入良性循环。截至2025年3月底，B站持有现金、现金等价物、定期存款及短期投资总计173.97亿元(23.97亿美元)，财务状况稳健。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  玻尿酸被资本抹黑？昔日千亿医美巨头回应“炮轰券商”事件 
Description:  <p>玻尿酸巨头华熙生物近期向券商“开炮”，揭开了医美行业“热点轮动”的一角！</p>
<p>针对突然向券商“开炮”，周二华熙生物对每经作出最新回应，华熙生物表示，透明质酸产业一直希望其作为行业龙头带头发声，纠正对透明质酸的罔顾科学的踩踏和抹黑。此次发声是基于多重考虑，且已和两大行业协会沟通并获得支持。</p>
<p>这一回应针对华熙生物5月17日在微信公众号发布的长文，其在文中驳斥了“玻尿酸过时”的观点，并点名了多家券商炒作“重组胶原蛋白”，与玻尿酸进行恶意对比。</p>
<p>“炮轰”的背后隐藏着华熙生物的困境，随着玻尿酸产能过剩价格不断下降，行业竞争也在不断加剧，华熙生物的业绩已经开始失速，2024年扣非净利缩水78.13%，市值也较巅峰缩水超1000亿。</p>
<p>反观，重组胶原蛋白成为市场的“新宠”，行业中巨子生物司股价一路走高，其业绩上完成了对华熙生物的反超，2024年归母净利润仅为巨子生物净利润的十二分之一左右。</p>
<h2>华熙生物发长文“<strong>开撕”券商</strong></h2>
<p>5月17日晚间，华熙生物在其官方微信号发布《概念总在重演，科技永远向前》的文章，点名批评多家券商的研究报告，认为这些报告通过“对比研究”的方式，试图抹黑透明质酸（即玻尿酸），从而抬高重组胶原蛋白的市场地位。</p>
<p>华熙生物直接在文章中点名几家券商机构称：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>2022年开始，随着资本市场不断追求新的公司题材，重组胶原蛋白概念被看似幸运地选中了。为了营造比透明质酸产业更大的预期，围绕某重组胶原企业的研报中，出现了大量直接针对中国透明质酸产业的所谓“对比研究”。这些误导性“结论”伴随着随后兴起的“玻尿酸过时论”被媒体和自媒体红人广泛传播，形成了资本市场与消费市场的舆论共振。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/254cd688-67b3-48e1-81a6-e4423dc2cba4.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="663" data-wscnw="697" data-wscnsize="91755"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p>华熙生物认为，透明质酸“过时论”的兴起，本质上是一场由“浮躁资本”构建的题材幻象，试图用“神话过时”绕开中国产业发展必然面临的进阶过程，引导资本和市场资源聚焦于资本新题材，用“新贵登场”塑造沙土高楼。</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements">
<h2 id="ab479bc4">“炮轰”背后：华熙生物的困境与反击</h2>
</div>
<p>然而，这背后也隐藏着华熙生物的困境。</p>
<p>随着玻尿酸量产技术的成熟，产能早已过剩，价格也在不断下降。据媒体报道，玻尿酸原料价格平均每年下降约5%。越来越多的玩家涌入玻尿酸市场，行业竞争日益加剧。</p>
<p>这种背景下，华熙生物曾经辉煌的玻尿酸业务面临严峻挑战，这已经体现在了业绩上。</p>
<p>2024年，华熙生物营业收入同比下降11.61%，归母净利润暴跌70.59%，仅为1.74亿元，创下上市以来最差纪录。 2025年一季度，营收再次下降20.77%，归母净利润下降58.15%，延续了颓势。</p>
<p>在资本市场上，玻尿酸概念股的表现也不尽如人意。昊海生科、华熙生物和爱美客在2021年7月之后，股价均出现大幅下跌。2021年巅峰时的华熙生物市值曾超1400亿，但截至5月20日收盘，股价为53.08元/股，市值为255.67亿。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/fcfce13a-bc3b-4fd0-b728-d4a7b6db08bd.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="474" data-wscnw="589" data-wscnsize="46584"/></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements">
<h2 id="580eeac1">资本市场的“新宠”：重组胶原蛋白的崛起</h2>
<p>同处医美赛道，玻尿酸和重组胶原蛋白均为具有填充、修复功能的生物材料。过去几年，玻尿酸行业竞争加剧，利润空间被压缩。而重组胶原蛋白凭借其独特的优势，成为资本市场的新宠。</p>
<p>A股“重组蛋白”概念股巨子生物和锦波生物表现强势，股价持续上涨。截至5月20日收盘，巨子生物的股价收于84.85港元/股，较其发行价上涨超200%，总市值为908亿港元。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/d34504f2-4e83-425b-a4ab-044f2421c018.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="471" data-wscnw="596" data-wscnsize="47083"/></p>
</div>
<p>两家公司的业绩也保持高速增长势头。2022年至2024年期间，巨子生物的营业收入分别为26.59亿元、38.91亿元、59.81亿元；净利润分别为11.22亿元、16.02亿元、22.27亿元。</p>
<p>事实上，“热点轮动”是市场常态， 与其“炮轰券商”，实力、技术才是打动资本的核心。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  小马智行Q1营收同比增12%，Robotaxi收入暴增200%，乘客车费增长800% | 财报见闻 
Description:  <p>自动驾驶企业小马智行2025年Q1营收同比增12%，Robotaxi业务收入达1230万元（173万美元），同比增长200%，是一季度营收保持同比增长的主要原因。一季度乘客车费收入增幅明显，同比增长800%。</p>
<p>5月20日，小马智行发布未经审计的2025年第一季度财报。</p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>小马智行第一季度总营收为1.02亿元（1398万美元），同比增长12%；其中，Robotaxi 服务收入 170 万美元，同比增长 200%，其中收费收入增长约 800%。</li>
<li>毛利230万美元，同比减12%，毛利率从去年同期的21%下降至16.6%；</li>
<li>运营亏损达到5600万美元，净亏损3740万美元，高于去年同期的 2080 万美元。亏损扩大主要是由于对Gen 7的大规模生产投入。</li>
<li>现金及现金等价物为7.385亿美元，环比下降，主要用于研发和生产准备。</li>
</ul>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/d7c27f92-7cd8-4b8a-b85f-2765bee9cd68.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="176" data-wscnw="724"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p>小马智行联合创始人、CEO彭军表示，2025年是小马智行的Robotaxi量产之年，<strong>随着第七代Robotaxi的自动驾驶系统成本下降，再加上生产提速，2025年底Robotaxi车队规模将扩大到千台。</strong></p>
<p>美股盘前，小马智行涨超17%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/dc3a8759-eb8c-49a9-b49d-830be8f8d1cc.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="660" data-wscnw="844"/></p>
<h2>Robotaxi同比增长200%，车队规模年底达千台</h2>
<p>第一季度，Robotaxi业务收入达1230万元（173万美元），同比增长200%，是一季度营收保持同比增长的主要原因。<strong>Robotaxi业务收入主要来源两类：乘客车费收入和技术解决方案项目收入。一季度乘客车费收入增幅明显，同比增长800%。</strong>车规级硬件等的加持，小马智行显著降低了第七代平台的硬件成本，再加上自动驾驶车队运营目前已高度自动化，提升了运营效率，也降低了运营成本。</p>
<p>第七代Robotaxi是小马智行迈向量产的里程碑。目前，小马智行正携手丰田、北汽、广汽三家车企，建立了密切的战略合作关系，七代Robotaxi带来了多方面的优势，包括：</p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>安全性和可靠性提升。</li>
<li>采用 100% 车规级自动驾驶套件。</li>
<li>相比上一代系统，BOM 成本降低 70%。</li>
<li>预计从 2025 年年中开始量产。</li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
<p>长远来看，第七代Robotaxi量产能为小马智行带来更大收益，但在短期内研发费用有所增加。</p>
<p>2025年第一季度，小马智行经调整研发费用为2.95亿元（4058万美元），同比增长38%。小马智行CFO王皓俊表示，2025年是Robotaxi扩大规模的关键一年，小马智行将在加大核心业务投入的同时进一步提升资金使用效率，以推动未来增长，并构建长期可持续的盈利模式。</p>
<h2>未来展望：扩大商业化区域，加强战略合作</h2>
<p>展望未来，小马智行正在积极推进其商业化战略：</p>
<blockquote>
<ul>
<li>扩大商业化区域，目前已覆盖北京、广州、深圳和上海，总面积超过 2000 平方公里。</li>
<li>获得深圳首个全无人驾驶 Robotaxi 牌照，具有里程碑意义。</li>
<li>与 Uber 合作，计划在中东地区推出 Robotaxi 服务，并拓展至其他国际市场。</li>
<li>与 ComfortDelGro 合作，在新加坡进行 Robotaxi 试点项目。</li>
</ul>
</blockquote><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  央行撤退，大行观望，日本国债无人接盘！ 
Description:  <p>在日本国债拍卖需求创下十多年来的新低之际，瑞穗金融集团（Mizuho Financial Group）<strong>正在采取“非常保守”的证券投资策略，大幅削减债券持仓，</strong>等待日本央行加息政策进一步明朗。</p>
<p>瑞穗首席执行官 Masahiro Kihara 在周二的新闻发布会上表示，<strong>在确信日本央行不会进一步加息之前，该行不会建立大规模的投资头寸。</strong></p>
<p>投资者报告显示，瑞穗已经削减了其在日本和外国政府债券中的头寸。<strong>截至今年3月，其持有的日本国债从三年前的25.1万亿日元锐减至8.3万亿日元（约合570亿美元）。</strong></p>
<p>虽然同期其外国债券持仓从8.9万亿日元增加到11.8万亿日元，但由于该行已经意识到损失，其外国债券持仓较去年有所下降。</p>
<p>目前，日本央行正在努力微调其量化紧缩进程，市场参与者内部对何时加快或减缓购债节奏众说纷纣。而瑞穗的谨慎策略或预示着未来一段时间内市场将维持谨慎情绪。</p>
<h2>瑞穗谨慎布局：债券持仓大瘦身，静待日央行政策明朗</h2>
<p>Kihara 的言论发布之际，<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747438" target="_blank" rel="noopener">日本20年期国债迎来自2012年以来最差拍卖</a>，投标倍数跌至2.5倍，尾差飙升至1987年以来最高水平。截至上个月底，日本央行持有的长期政府债务为576.6万亿日元，仅比2024年7月底（即开始放缓债券购买速度之前）下降了2.2%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/03582fbb-1932-499b-9bce-887002f8111b.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="467" data-wscnw="844"/></p>
<p>消息导致日本国债周二进一步下跌。其中，日本20年期国债收益率飙升约15个基点，达到2000年以来最高，而30年期债券收益率则升至1999年首次发行该品种债券以来最高。</p>
<p><img src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/13837aba-f174-4c81-84b5-120c24a96bc9.png"/></p>
<p>然而，这些市场波动对瑞穗和其他商业银行的影响可能不大，因为他们倾向于购买期限短于10年的债券。<strong>瑞穗在简报中表示，其持有的日本国债的平均剩余期限为一年，外国债券的平均剩余期限为两年。</strong></p>
<p>除了债券市场，瑞穗还宣布计划在截至2028年3月的三年内出售至少价值3500亿日元的“战略”持股，即为巩固与企业客户关系的股票。</p>
<p>Kihara表示，<strong>瑞穗不太可能在美国进行投资银行业务交易。</strong>该行于2023年收购了纽约精品咨询公司 Greenhill &amp; Co.，Kihara 认为该行已经在此领域建立了足够的产品。特别值得注意的是，穆迪上周五下调美国信用评级，从Aaa降至Aa1，进一步放大了全球债券市场的不确定性。</p>
<p>此外，据 Kihara 称，瑞穗也不太热衷于亚洲的传统零售银行业务。</p>
<h2>日本债券市场动荡，长期债券承压</h2>
<p>目前，<strong>日本央行正在努力微调其量化紧缩进程，市场参与者内部对何时加快或减缓购债节奏众说纷纣。</strong></p>
<p>一些人认为央行应加快削减购债，理由是过一半的日本国债由日本央行持有，以及由此对收益率曲线造成的扭曲。而另一些则强调应放慢节奏，担忧快速收紧可能会加剧市场流动性紧张。</p>
<p>关于最终的购债规模，市场也存在广泛的看法。一些人认为央行最终应完全停止购买债券，而另一些人则认为每月应购买1万亿日元（约合69亿美元）至2万亿日元，还有人建议维持在3万亿日元左右。</p>
<p>日本央行正在与来自银行、证券公司和人寿保险公司等的代表举行听证会，就缩减购债的步伐征询意见。<strong>预计央行将在6月17日结束的董事会会议上更新其在市场中减少影响力的计划。</strong></p>
<p>Norinchukin Zenkyoren Asset Management的高级基金经理Ryoma Nagatomo表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“我不想碰超长期债券，原因包括财政风险和供应过剩问题日益严重。”</p>
</blockquote><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  今年前四月财政收入降0.4%，财政支出增4.6%，交易印花税收入增57.8% 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">5月20日周二，财政部公布数据显示，<strong>1—4月，全国一般公共预算收入80616亿元，同比下降0.4%；全国一般公共预算支出93581亿元，同比增长4.6%。</strong></p>

<p>据证券时报，5月20日，国家发改委召开5月份新闻发布会。发改委新闻发言人李超表示，在加快落实既定政策基础上，发改委已会同有关部门加快推出稳就业稳经济推动高质量发展的若干举措。目前有关部门正在抓紧落实，大部分政策举措计划将在6月底前落地。</p>
<p><strong>港股：</strong>截至收盘，恒指涨1.49%，恒科指涨1.15%。宁德时代在港交所上市首日收涨超16%，成为今年全球最大IPO。医药、科技板块均走强，石药集团涨超6%，三生制药涨超32%，小米集团涨超4%。</p>

<h2>生物医药股大涨</h2>
<p>受到利好消息，今天A股和港股的生物医药股大涨。截至A股收盘，生物科技指数收涨2.36%，板块内三生国健20CM涨停，荣昌生物、益方生物、科兴制药等涨幅超过10%，回盛生物、赛升药业、科前生物等股纷纷走高。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/b03f8555-4d86-42ad-bedc-4e14b35206a6.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="539" data-wscnw="479"/></p>
<p>截止收盘，港股恒生生物科技指数涨超3%，板块内三生制药超32%，荣昌生物涨16%，瀚森制药、石药集团等纷纷走高。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/52ad5d3b-2a56-480e-ab83-3ad425af1576.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="403" data-wscnw="798"/></p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/d1d0318c-87e1-475e-b499-08a4fee59e9b.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="543" data-wscnw="530"/></p>
<p>消息面，<span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747423" target="_blank" rel="noopener">华尔街见闻此前提及</a></span>，全球医药市场的目光再次聚焦于中国创新。5月20日，三生制药公告称，其与辉瑞公司就前者自主研发的PD-1/VEGF双特异性抗体SSGJ-707签订了独家许可协议 。</p>
<p>根据协议，辉瑞将获得SSGJ-707在全球（不包括中国内地）开发、生产和商业化的独家权利 。三生制药将获得12.5亿美元的首付款，以及最高可达48亿美元的开发、注册及销售里程碑付款，外加基于产品在许可地区净销售额的梯度双位数百分比提成 。同时拥有中国区商业化选择权。</p>
<p>国信证券认为生命科学上游处于景气反转初期，海外需求回暖、国内企业加大研发与全球布局，有望重回高增速。</p>
<p>招银国际称，受益于创新药出海交易、国内集采政策优化、创新药丙类医保目录落地、医疗设备招标复苏、内需复苏等积极因素推动，医药行业有望在2025年继续迎来估值修复。</p>
<h2>“宁王”登录港股成今年最大IPO</h2>
<p>宁德时代港股上市首日涨16.43%，报306.2港元/股，成交82.984亿港元。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/c91ec4a0-38db-429e-9f04-4dc741e03d6a.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="406" data-wscnw="811"/></p>
<p>消息面，宁德时代此次港股上市，全球发售股份总数为1.35亿股，发行价格为263.00港元/股，募集资金357亿港元（46亿美元），成为今年最大IPO。Jefferies驻香港中国工业研究主管Johnson Wan表示，宁德时代在香港的股票估值为17倍市盈率定价，目前来看仍有50%的上涨空间，这得益于强劲的盈利和有吸引力的估值。</p>
<p>据宁德时代财报数据显示，2024年，宁德时代实现营业收入3620.13亿元，同比下降9.70%；实现归属于母公司股东的净利润507.45亿元，同比增长15.01%；2025年第一季度，公司实现营业收入847.05亿元，同比增长6.18%；实现归母净利润139.63亿元，同比增长32.85%。</p>
<p>另外，小米集团收涨4.68%，报54.8港元/股，小米3nmSoC官宣后市值上涨900亿港元。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/0ade6984-63af-4f2e-ab76-2cfc5925ab43.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="403" data-wscnw="795"/></p>
<p>消息面，5月20日上午，小米集团股价盘中最高涨超4%，一度涨至54.6港元/股。5月19日，小米宣布自研SoC芯片玄戒O1将采用3nm制程。5月20日，小米集团创始人、董事长兼CEO雷军又宣布，玄戒O1已大规模量产，搭载这款芯片的小米15S Pro将于5月22日发布。两天来，小米集团股价最高涨幅累计达8%，市值增加近900亿港元。</p>
<h2>微盘股指数再创新高</h2>
<p>万得微盘股指数以上交所、深交所上市的所有上市公司为样本空间，剔除ST、*ST及退市警示标的，选取市值最小的400只股票为成份股。</p>
<p>从成份股表现看，截至收盘，360只成份股实现上涨，占比90%；其中金利华电20cm涨停，莱绅通灵、浪莎股份、天安新材、祖名股份、滨海能源等个股涨停。从近期表现看，金利华电、浪莎股份、滨海能源已经实现两连板。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/84a08d0e-2515-4ad5-b231-24209cee13da.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="545" data-wscnw="483"/></p>
<p>中邮证券认为， 5月16日，证监会发布了修改后的《上市公司重大资产重组管理办法》（以下简称《重组办法》），包括推动重组股份对价分期支付落地、明确跨界并购的规范运作要求、完善锁定期规则支持上市公司之间吸收合并以及鼓励私募基金参与上市公司并购重组。《重组办法》修改发布后，将允许跨界并购，这对于微盘股而言构成利好。</p>
<p>中信建投证券认为，对行业而言，新设简易审核程序和提高监管包容度，简化了重组流程，降低了交易门槛，有助于提高市场活跃度，促进上市公司通过并购重组实现资源整合与转型升级，推动行业整体发展。</p>
<h2>新消费概念集体爆发</h2>
<p>新消费概念集体爆发，成为今天全市场最大的热点之一。宠物经济概念集体爆发，源飞宠物、依依股份等涨停。IP经济概念走强，实丰文化、高乐股份等封板。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/1128e348-67fa-4654-9f5e-f42bac2d60fc.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="453" data-wscnw="628"/></p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/467af2de-62e8-45a2-9311-bc537296da8d.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="478" data-wscnw="630"/></p>
<p>消息面上，根据派读宠物《2025年中国宠物行业白皮书》，2015年至2024年，国内宠物市场整体呈稳步增长趋势，年均复合增长率为13.3%。预计到2027年，城镇宠物（犬猫）消费市场规模将突破4000亿元大关，达到4042亿元。</p>
<p>中信证券认为，2025年宠物板块业绩有望持续增长。宠物经济是稀缺赛道，需求韧性强，国内市场目前仍处“大行业、小龙头”阶段，龙头集中程度进一步提升，看好龙头通过产品创新、品牌和渠道建设不断提升市场份额。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  美国生物医药“三座大山”压顶：关税、药价、专利悬崖 
Description:  <p>近期，美国大型生物制药板块经历了一场显著的“倒春寒”。自2025年4月2日一项关键的关税声明发布以来，该板块表现大幅跑输标普500指数约15个百分点，市场情绪趋于谨慎。</p>
<p>行业似乎正笼罩在关税壁垒高筑、药价谈判压力以及迫在眉睫的专利悬崖等多重阴霾之下，前景显得扑朔迷离。</p>
<h2><strong>阴霾笼罩——压制板块表现的“三座大山”</strong></h2>
<p>生物医药，这个曾经群星璀璨的板块，如今正面临前所未有的挑战。摩根大通的分析师们将这些挑战归纳为几个核心“悬顶因素”（overhangs）。</p>
<p>而早在2023年5月，美国外交关系协会高级研究员Brad W. Setser在美国参议院财政委员会的证词中，就已深刻揭示了美国制药公司通过复杂的税务结构和生产布局来规避本土高额税负的现象，这些深层结构性问题与当前板块面临的压力不无关联。</p>
<p><strong>第一座山：关税阴云与供应链挑战</strong></p>
<p>行业特定的关税政策无疑是近期板块下行的直接导火索。</p>
<p>这些政策细节尚未完全披露，给市场带来了巨大的不确定性。然而，摩根大通认为，关税的冲击在很大程度上是“可控的”。</p>
<p>短期内，企业可以通过积极的库存管理、加速产品运往美国等方式来应对。从中长期来看，通过制造业回流，包括利用内部产能和拓展第三方合作关系，能够有效管理关税带来的风险敞口。</p>
<p>尽管摩根大通预计企业在2026至2027年的损益表可能会因此受到一定影响，例如目前约16-17%的税率可能向吉利德科学（GILD）那样主要依赖美国本土生产和知识产权的19-20%税率靠拢，但这并不构成投资者需要完全规避该行业的根本理由。</p>
<p>值得注意的是，Setser在其证词中指出，美国税法（尤其在2017年《减税与就业法案》(TCJA)之后）的结构性缺陷，客观上鼓励了美国公司将利润和生产转移至海外低税率地区。</p>
<p>例如，GILTI（全球无形低税收入）税制中对海外有形资产的“推定回报”予以豁免，进一步刺激了企业在海外配置生产设施以降低全球税负。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/8ce72317-9908-4162-a0e8-e425b7317270.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="847" data-wscnw="1213"/></p>
<p>这导致美国从爱尔兰、瑞士、新加坡等以低税率吸引制药企业的热点地区大量进口药品，而这些策略本质上是为了税收优化。这种长期的离岸生产布局，也使得板块在面临新的关税政策时显得更为脆弱。</p>
<p><strong>第二座山：药价谈判——MFN与IRA的双重压力</strong></p>
<p>药价问题始终是悬在生物医药板块头上的达摩克利斯之剑。其中，“最惠国”（MFN）参考定价的幽灵不时搅动市场情绪。</p>
<p>但摩根大通对此持谨慎乐观态度，认为MFN政策若想广泛推行，不仅需要获得国会的明确批准（而共和党对此支持寥寥），还可能面临诸多法律层面的挑战。</p>
<p>即便政府试图通过现有IRA（通胀削减法案）的框架小规模引入MFN原则，其影响也可能被IRA中针对所谓“药丸罚款”（Pill Penalty，指对某些口服药物的惩罚性定价条款）的潜在取消所抵消，并且当前估值已在一定程度上反映了这些担忧。</p>
<p>至于IRA法案本身带来的药品价格谈判，摩根大通认为其对市场预期的冲击更多是“增量”而非“颠覆性”的。</p>
<p>市场对于2027年谈判药品（预计2025年11月30日前公布最高公平价格MFPs）将面临比2026年清单（当时实现了约20-25%的净价削减）更大折扣已有预期，部分分析甚至已计入了35-50%的价格下调。</p>
<p>而美国医保和医助服务中心（CMS）近期关于2028年谈判可能将某些皮下注射产品（如Keytruda、Opdivo的皮下剂型）与其静脉注射剂型捆绑的指导意见，在摩根大通看来，市场早已预料到这些产品无论如何都将面临生物类似药的激烈价格竞争，因此IRA的纳入并不会带来额外的大幅震动。</p>
<p>Setser的证词为理解药价压力提供了更深层的视角。</p>
<p>他强调，尽管美国药品价格全球最高，但许多美国大型制药公司通过利润转移，仅在美国报告极少的利润，而在海外（通常是低税率国家）报告巨额利润。</p>
<p>例如，2022年，Setser援引数据显示，（剔除吉利德和礼来后）几家主要美国上市药企在美国本土的2140亿美元营收中仅录得约100亿美元利润，而在海外1710亿美元营收中却斩获超900亿美元利润。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/cbcaae70-aa0f-4ce8-b194-e57707bdf01f.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="1454" data-wscnw="1070"/></p>
<p>这种利润与销售地点的显著错位，正是通过复杂的知识产权转移和离岸生产实现的，其核心目的之一便是规避美国本土相对较高的税率和药价体系的全面冲击。</p>
<p><strong>第三座山：专利悬崖——无法回避的周期性阵痛</strong></p>
<p>对于投资者而言，2028年至2030年间一批重磅药物（如Keytruda、Opdivo、Eliquis等）的专利到期，无疑是长期压制板块估值的重要因素。</p>
<p>然而，这更像是一场可预见的“盈利重置”（rebase），而非板块性的“断崖式危机”。</p>
<p>预计即使是受影响最直接的公司，如百时美施贵宝（BMY）和默沙东（MRK），其每股收益（EPS）的调整幅度也可能在15-20%或更低的水平。</p>
<p>与此同时，礼来（LLY）、吉利德科学（GILD）、强生（JNJ）、艾伯维（ABBV）等一批公司，其下一轮主要的专利到期潮（LOEs）要到2030年代中期甚至更晚才会到来。</p>
<p>回顾历史，大型专利到期事件通常是行业可以消化和管理的，LOE后一年平均EPS的侵蚀幅度约为15%，随后往往能迅速反弹，并伴随着市盈率的扩张。<strong> </strong></p>
<h2><strong>估值探底——历史性低谷中寻觅“黄金坑”？</strong></h2>
<p>在多重压力的交织下，美国大型生物制药板块的估值已悄然滑落至历史性的洼地。摩根大通指出，经历了近期的回调后，该板块（剔除礼来）目前相对标普500指数的估值折价已达到惊人的45-50%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/3ea36022-af75-441f-9064-a0d870959af2.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="466" data-wscnw="854"/></p>
<p><em>图表说明：该图表展示了过去十余年间，美国大型生物制药板块（剔除礼来）的远期12个月市盈率（P/E）与标普500指数P/E的对比，以及两者之间的折价百分比。当前折价已触及历史低点。</em></p>
<p>摩根大通的分析师们认为，如此之深的折价，意味着市场当前的股价已计入了相当程度的政策风险，甚至可能是对关税、MFN以及IRA等不利因素的“近乎最坏情况”的定价。这种过度悲观的情绪，反而可能为板块的价值修复创造了空间。</p>
<p>从板块表现来看，自2025年4月2日关税消息落地后，生物制药板块整体下跌约8%，而同期标普500指数上涨约5%，其他防御性板块如消费必需品和公用事业也分别录得约2%和4%的正增长。</p>
<p><strong><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/a778e211-75ec-4dbd-ad6c-4841b853cab4.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="298" data-wscnw="502"/></strong></p>
<p><em>图表说明：该图表展示了自2025年4月3日关税声明以来，美国大型生物制药板块与标普500指数、科技股、公用事业、消费必需品等其他板块的表现对比。生物制药板块显著落后。</em></p>
<p><strong><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/0af27abf-7693-4b34-a86e-afed2f44abd8.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="300" data-wscnw="414"/></strong></p>
<p><em>图表说明：该图表展示了2025年年初以来，各大板块的表现情况，进一步印证生物制药板块的相对弱势。</em><strong> </strong></p>
<h2><strong>重振之路——哪些催化剂能让板块“王者归来”？</strong></h2>
<p>在估值触底、悲观情绪弥漫之际，市场也在苦苦寻觅能够引领板块走出泥潭的催化剂。摩根大通认为，以下几个方面的积极变化，有望为板块注入新的活力：</p>
<p><strong>政策清晰化是关键</strong>：当前，无论是关税、MFN还是IRA的后续执行，许多政策仍停留在方向性指导层面，缺乏具体的实施细节，这使得投资者在“信息真空”中犹豫不前。</p>
<p>一旦这些政策的细节（如关税的确切税率、MFN的适用范围、IRA谈判的具体药品清单和降价幅度）得以明朗，将有助于投资者更准确地评估其实际影响。而这种影响，很可能没有市场当前所担心的那般可怕。</p>
<p>例如，近期可能宣布的针对制药业特定关税的232调查结果，若最终税率如市场基线预期的25%左右，摩根大通认为这将是行业高度可控的，反而能有效缓解投资者的焦虑情绪。</p>
<p>此外，对预算和解法案中关于MFN政策（如确认国会无进一步扩大行动）和IRA“药丸罚款”（如能取消，对板块是重大利好）的关注也至关重要。</p>
<p>从更宏观的政策层面看，Setser在其证词中提出了一系列旨在修正美国税法，以减少利润和生产外流的改革建议。</p>
<p>这些建议包括提高美国公司全球无形收入的税率至至少15%（与OECD全球最低税负协议对接），按国别计算GILTI税，以及强化原有的Subpart F条款，对海外特许权使用费收入按美国税率征税，取消对“成本分摊协议”的特殊税收待遇等。</p>
<p>虽然这些是更长期的结构性改革，但任何朝向这个方向的政策调整，都可能从根本上改变药企的生产和利润布局，对板块产生深远影响。</p>
<h2><strong>结论：于迷雾中寻找航向</strong></h2>
<p>综上所述，美国大型生物制药板块当前无疑正经历一段艰难时期。关税威胁、药价压力以及专利到期等“悬顶之剑”共同构成了压制市场情绪和板块估值的主要因素。</p>
<p>然而，这些挑战在很大程度上或是可以被行业主动管理和消化的（如通过生产回流应对关税，或凭借管线创新平滑专利到期影响），或是其负面冲击已在股价中得到了较为充分甚至过度的反映。</p>
<p>Setser的证词则从更深层次揭示了美国税收政策如何长期塑造了制药行业的全球生产和利润布局模式，这些模式在面临新的政策冲击时，既是脆弱点，也可能是企业战略调整的考量点。他甚至不无尖锐地指出2017年的《减税与就业法案》在某种程度上可以被称为“制药业减税与爱尔兰就业法案”，突显了税收政策对产业外移的深远影响。</p>
<p>未来，政策的逐步明朗化、IRA中不利条款（如“药丸罚款”）的潜在移除，以及市场风险偏好的转变，都有可能成为驱动板块反弹的强力催化剂。</p>
<p>在这样的背景下，投资者或许不应被短期的悲观情绪所裹挟，而更应聚焦于那些拥有强大研发实力、稳健财务状况、清晰增长路径的低估公司。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  资金涌入关税避风港，这个新兴国家股市今年飙涨28%！ 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">波兰领跑新兴市场下一轮大牛市？</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">数据显示，<strong>波兰主要股指WIG今年已上涨28.6%，远超标普500仅1%的累计涨幅，成为今年全球表现最强劲的市场之一。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/7418d459-24a2-4cb8-a2b8-673f3192942e.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="397" data-wscnw="865"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">分析指出，<strong>波兰股市的强劲表现部分归功于该国相对独立于全球贸易战的地位，以及预期从德国巨额财政刺激计划中获益。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Warsaw研究所的首席执行官Tomasz Bardziłowski表示，这波涨势由“大量外资流入”推动，受益于波兰健康的经济以及股市不断上升的股息和相对较低的估值。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Bardziłowski指出，当前波兰股票的市盈率比MSCI新兴市场指数低15%。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">美国贸易战推升“和平交易”、经济增长仍具韧性</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">4月以来，<strong>特朗普发动的贸易战实际上转移了资本流向，从美国转向波兰和拉丁美洲部分国家等受关税影响较小的新兴市场。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">波兰VeloBank首席经济学家Piotr Arak指出：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">“市场规模足够小，外国资本流动能产生明显影响。”</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">其次，波兰本国的经济增长也显现出强劲韧性。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">欧盟统计局的数据显示，波兰经济在2025年第一季度同比增长3.8%，是欧盟增长第二快的国家（仅次于爱尔兰），远高于欧盟1.4%的平均水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">分析师预计，2025年华沙证交所上市公司的每股收益平均将增长约10%。其中，占WIG指数40%权重的金融服务公司，本季度在创纪录盈利后正在提高股息。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">欧洲复兴开发银行(EBRD)首席经济学家Beata Javorcik表示，波兰在这些动荡时期保持韧性，“<strong>要归功于其多元化经济、庞大的国内市场以及有限的对美直接贸易敞口”。</strong></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;"><strong>欧盟资金释放提供额外推力，关注6月总统决选</strong></h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">此外，波兰总理图斯克（Donald Tusk）及其亲欧盟联盟回归后，解锁了之前冻结的数十亿欧元欧盟资金。这些资金主要用于基础设施和能源转型项目，政府正在部署这些资金，寻求摆脱对煤炭的依赖。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">受到这些举措的推动，<strong>波兰国有能源集团股价飙升，石油公司Orlen上涨53%，公用事业公司PGE今年以来上涨56%。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>投资者目前正密切关注将于6月1日开展的总统决选。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">目前，执政党候选人Rafał Trzaskowski正与反对派法律与公正党（PiS）的Karol Nawrocki之间展开出人意料的激烈竞争。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">波兰最大的银行PKO BP的首席经济学家Piotr Bujak表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>“如果图斯克所属党派的候选人获胜，将有利于投资者对波兰资产的信心，而失败则可能引发人们对波兰是否会继续走改革道路的新担忧。”</strong></p>
</blockquote>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">新兴市场投资机会显现，波兰或仅是开始</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">波兰的案例可能只是新兴市场崛起的开端。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">随着美元走弱预期增强、美国债券收益率可能已触顶以及市场对中国经济复苏的期待，新兴市场正重新成为全球投资者关注的焦点。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">根据<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747364">美银策略师Michael Hartnett的观察</a>，2025年迄今，不仅波兰股市成为表现最佳的股票市场，而且：</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p style="text-align: left;">年内表现最差资产：石油(-12%)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p style="text-align: left;">年内表现最佳资产：黄金(21%)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p style="text-align: left;">年内表现最佳货币：俄罗斯卢布(41%)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p style="text-align: left;">特拉维夫和德黑兰证券交易所都创下历史新高</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align: left;">Hartnett据此得出结论，今年地缘政治将驱动市场，而“和平交易”将在2025年跑赢“战争交易”。而在这样的环境下，<strong>“没有什么会比新兴市场股票表现得更好”。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/b89d9f81-224f-46bd-84f0-ac0c5aacfcb8.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="330" data-wscnw="500"/></strong></p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  被降级后，美国面临二选一：要么减税缩水，要么加重关税？ 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">穆迪美国信用降级敲响警钟，美国面临要么减税缩水，要么加重关税的两难局面。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据追风交易台消息，美国银行在最新的报告中表示，市场对美债的担忧已持续一段时间，穆迪的此次降级的时机也并非巧合，意在提醒美国政府关税收入将无法完全抵消拟减税成本。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">尽管如此，但美银表示，美国或可能执意而行：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">从我们的观点看，更可能的情况是我们仍将获得一个扩张性的税收方案，长期美债收益率应该会继续反映对财政前景的担忧。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">风险在于：当华盛顿认真对待美国财政问题时，关税可能是唯一能有效减少赤字的手段，而另一轮大规模关税上调可能比不那么扩张的财政方案对经济造成更大伤害。</p>
</blockquote>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">降级时机绝非巧合</h2>
<p>美银表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>近期，许多客户询问债券市场是否即将到达投资者对债务可持续性担忧爆发的临界点。穆迪在周五晚间将美国评级从Aaa下调至Aa1后，这个问题变得尤为突出。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">从我们的角度来看，此次降级的时机并非巧合。在减税和关税政策悬而未决之际，穆迪似乎在传递一个信息：它认为这些政策变化将使美国的财政轨迹进一步恶化。具体而言，关税收入将无法完全抵消拟议中税法案的成本。我们对此表示认同。</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">由于这并非新鲜事，截止目前市场反应较为温和。美银策略师预计，由于评级下调不会导致美债被排除在任何主要固定收益指数之外，因此不会引发被动抛售美国国债。然而，由于财政状况持续恶化，他们对长期美债持负面看法。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">更负责任的财政措施 or 扩张性税收政策+关税</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">现在的问题是，这次降级是否会促使国会共和党人转向更具财政责任感的方案，包括减少或推迟减税规模，和/或增加支出削减。这对短期增长不利，但对美国长期财政健康有益。债券市场的动荡将增加这种结果的可能性。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">美银表示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">但从我们的观点看，更可能的情况是我们仍将获得一个扩张性的税收方案。长期美债收益率应该会继续反映对财政前景的担忧。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">但除非出现突然变动，否则风险在于：当华盛顿认真对待美国财政问题时，关税可能是唯一能有效减少赤字的手段。另一轮大规模关税上调可能比不那么扩张的财政方案对经济造成更大伤害。</p>
</blockquote>

Title:  医药股全线爆发！辉瑞60亿美元押注中国抗癌药 
Description:  <p>辉瑞斥资60亿美元押注中国抗癌药研发，带动中国医药股持续飙升。</p>
<p>20日周二，生物医药股爆发，港股恒生生物科技指数大涨超4%，板块内三生制药（3SBio）涨超35%，荣昌生物涨14%，瀚森制药、石药集团等纷纷走高。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/21f21486-24fb-4bdd-980b-882c68ba6a24.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="419" data-wscnw="867"/></p>
<p><a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747423" target="_blank" rel="noopener">华尔街见闻此前提及，</a><strong>辉瑞与中国沈阳的三生制药达成协议，就PD-1/VEGF双特异性抗体SSGJ-707达成首付12.5亿美元，总额60.5亿美元的全球开发与商业化协议（除中国内地外），并对三生制药进行1亿美元股权投资和中国商业化选择权。</strong></p>
<p>这一交易在中国药企许可交易中创下新纪录，同时三生制药未来最多可获得4.8亿美元的里程碑式后续费用。<strong>也预示着全球PD-1/VEGF双抗这一炙手可热的赛道竞争将进一步升级，更多中国优质产品将迎来BD可能。</strong></p>
<p>伯恩斯坦的医药和生物技术高级分析师Rebecca Liang表示，辉瑞与三生制药的合作是迄今为止中国生物科技公司最大的一笔对外授权交易。她认为，市场反应表明投资者将此视为对整个行业创新质量日益提升的认可。</p>
<h2>辉瑞押注中国，药物创新成市场新亮点</h2>
<p><strong>值得注意的是，辉瑞还将向三生制药进行1亿美元的股权投资。</strong>三生制药在中国销售一系列用于癌症、自身免疫性疾病、肾脏疾病、皮肤病等疾病的药物。</p>
<p>SSGJ-707是三生制药旗下三生国健基于其专有CLF2平台自主研发的创新双抗药物 。从临床数据看，SSGJ-707潜力不俗。根据三生制药公告，SSGJ-707已在中国开展多项临床研究 。</p>
<p>在针对PD-L1阳性、局部晚期或转移性非小细胞肺癌（NSCLC）的一线治疗方面，该药物的III期临床研究已获国家药监局药品审评中心（CDE）批准启动，并获得了突破性疗法认定 。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/8b80d687-9a1b-4083-9a37-72e3340a2ebf.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="459" data-wscnw="867"/></p>
<p>这次辉瑞的入场，不仅仅是一次资金投入，更是全球资本对中国创新药的高度认可。过去一年，许多辉瑞的同行都押注中国本土研发的药物来补充其产品线。</p>
<p>据GlobalData统计，<strong>2024年中国药企的授权交易规模创历史新高，占到全球创新药授权的28%。</strong>今年，诺和诺德和默沙东也分别投资了2亿美元，用于引进癌症和心血管药物。</p>
<h2>3SBio药物对标Keytruda，竞争格局引人注目</h2>
<p>辉瑞此次合作<strong>，也可以视为在“抗癌药战局”中的一场关键布局，有望与默克（Merck）Keytruda（全球最畅销药物）抗衡。</strong>三生制药的药物靶点与 Akeso Inc.一款表现优异的药物类似，后者在一次试验中的表现优于Keytruda。值得注意的是，Merck也从中国生物科技公司LaNova Medicines收购了一种类似的药物。</p>
<p>此前，辉瑞曾与Akeso的美国合作伙伴Summit Therapeutics合作，测试Akeso和Summit的药物与辉瑞自身疗法的组合。Daiwa Capital Markets的分析师Wilfred Yuen表示，这项研究协议不会受到新交易的影响。</p>
<p>随着辉瑞、诺和诺德、默沙东等巨头加大投入，中国药企的“出海”步伐逐步加快。Citigroup分析师将3SBio目标价从13港元提升至21港元，预示着市场对中国创新药的信心。</p>
<h2>三生制药计划年内启动后期研究，辉瑞将在美国生产药物</h2>
<p>三生制药计划今年在中国启动该药物的首次后期研究。虽然辉瑞没有概述其自身的临床计划，但该公司在一份声明中表示，它将在美国生产该药物。</p>
<p>花旗分析师在一份报告中写道，这笔新交易应该可以缓解投资者对可能影响授权趋势的地缘政治风险的担忧，而这一趋势已经提振了中国生物科技公司的发展。</p>
<p>花旗分析师写道：“全球扩张是创新制药/生物科技公司的关键投资主题。”花旗在达成协议后，<strong>将三生制药的目标价从13.00港元上调至21.00港元（2.7美元）。</strong></p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>

Description: <p>The House GOP's blue state holdouts are close to a deal on the "big, beautiful bill" that would raise the state and local tax (SALT) deduction cap to $40k a year for people making up to $500,000 a year, sources familiar told Axios. </p><p><strong>Why it matters</strong>: Getting the blue state holdouts on board is a must-do for House Speaker <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/mike-johnson-salt-deduction-income-limits" target="_blank">Mike Johnson</a>, who wants a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/mike-johnson-thune-republican-senators" target="_blank">House floor vote Wednesday</a> on the full bill. </p><hr><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>Johnson offered the holdouts on Monday an increase for the state and local tax (SALT) deduction cap from $10,000 to $40,000 a year, within income limits. </p><ul><li>The speaker then got an assist from <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/trump-house-republicans-medicaid-salt" target="_blank">President Trump</a>, who told the holdouts to cut a deal and warned them to stop pushing so hard.</li><li>The agreement that's in final negotiations is a $40k a year cap for people making up to $500,000 a year. The income phaseout would grow 1% a year for 10 years, and then the deduction would become permanent. </li><li>Not all the details have final agreement, but sources said they're making progress and they expect most SALT members to agree to the terms before passage. </li></ul><p><strong>The bottom line:</strong> That number would keep the GOP within the $350 billion window that it has left for cuts, according to the reconciliation bill instructions. </p>

Axios in an emailed statement Tuesday evening that the former president's last known prostate-specific antigen (PSA) test was in 2014. </p><ul><li>"Prior to Friday, President Biden had never been diagnosed with prostate cancer," the spokesperson said.</li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>The U.S. Preventive Services Task Force <a href="https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jama/fullarticle/2680553" target="_blank">recommendation</a> on screening for prostate cancer holds that it's an individual choice for men age 55-69 and that it offers a small potential benefit of reducing the chances of death.</p><ul><li>They worry about potential harms of screening, including additional testing, prostate biopsy, over-treatment and complications.</li><li>For those 70 and older, like Biden, they advise against it, saying with moderate certainty that potential benefits don't outweigh expected harms.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines:</strong> Biden was 70 or 71 years old when he had his last PSA, before he had symptoms that led to last Friday's exam. That's within standard guidelines and is not unusual.</p><ul><li>It is noteworthy, however, that he apparently was not tested for it even while he was president.</li></ul><p><strong>Context: </strong>Biden's personal office <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/18/biden-prostate-cancer-diagnosed" target="_blank">announced his diagnosis</a> on Sunday.</p><ul><li>"On Friday, he was diagnosed with prostate cancer, characterized by a Gleason score of 9 (Grade Group 5) with metastasis to the bone," they said.</li><li>Even at that advanced stage, physicians say the condition can be managed, thought not cured.</li><li>He <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/13/biden-nodule-prostate-physical-health" target="_self">was evaluated</a> last week after doctors found a "small nodule" in his prostate during a routine physical exam.</li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper:</strong> <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/biden-cancer-sympathy-suspicion" target="_blank">Biden's cancer diagnosis draws sympathy — and suspicion</a></p>

countries they're not citizens of would <strong>"</strong>clearly violate" an earlier order against sending people to third countries.</p><hr><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>The lawyers said the security threats" that include crime, kidnapping, and armed conflict.</p><ul><li>"N.M. has limited English proficiency," said a San Francisco-based attorney in a Tuesday <a href="https://storage.courtlistener.com/recap/gov.uscourts.mad.282404/gov.uscourts.mad.282404.112.1.pdf%20" target="_blank">filing</a> that said she was told after the fact that her client had been "removed" from Texas' Port Isabel Detention Center to South Sudan. </li><li>The emergency filing in the Massachusetts District Court said T.T.P., a national of Vietnam, "appears to have suffered the same fate as N.M." and the lawyers had "information that there were likely at least 10 other" immigrants on the deportation plane to South Sudan. </li><li>The lawyers said this "blatantly defies" the court order prohibiting sending immigrants to third countries and requested the judge block any further such deportations.</li><li>Representatives for the Trump administration did not immediately respond to Axios' request for comment in the evening.</li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/self-deportation-flights-1000-dollars" target="_blank">First Title: Schumer blasts Thune for choosing "nuclear option"
Description: <p>Senate Majority Leader <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/11/john-thune-trump-budget-taxes-medicaid-energy" target="_blank">John Thune</a> is blazing forward with a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/13/senate-california-emissions-standards" target="_blank">controversial move</a> to repeal California's EV mandate — and Democratic Leader Chuck Schumer is warning it will come back to bite him.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>Schumer (D-N.Y.) all but threatened to deploy similar strategies to get around opinions by key, <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/01/senate-gop-parliamentarian-ev-mandate-california" target="_blank">nonpartisan rule makers</a> if and when he grabs back control of the chamber.</p><hr><ul><li>"What goes around comes around," <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/schumer-legislation-qatar-trump-air-force-one" target="_blank">Schumer</a> said on Tuesday. He and other Democratic leaders have described the GOP move as a "nuclear option."</li><li>Thune (R-S.D.) accused Democrats of "throwing a tantrum."</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news:</strong> The Senate will vote as soon as Wednesday on a Congressional Review Act (CRA) resolution that would overturn California's Clean Air Act waiver, leading to an eventual ban on gas-powered vehicles.</p><ul><li>The Government Accountability Office issued an opinion saying that the waiver is not a rule that cannot be repealed by the CRA. The Senate parliamentarian then agreed with GAO.</li><li>That isn't stopping Republicans.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>Key Senate Republican leaders have been discussing the best way to move forward with repealing California's EV policy — and assuring senators with concerns about ignoring the parliamentarian.</p><ul><li>For weeks, GOP Whip John Barrasso (R-Wyo.) assured reporters the Senate would move forward with the CRA, making the case for it on the Senate floor and in an op-ed.</li><li>Senate Rules Chair Mitch McConnell (R-Ky.), a staunch defender of Senate procedure, spoke in favor of using the CRA during a closed-door lunch last week. His voice was particularly influential for some senators on the fence, according to sources familiar.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines:</strong> Republicans argue the California waiver is a unique case, the GAO does not get to decide what rules can be undone and that their action does not count as overruling the parliamentarian.</p><ul><li>"We are not talking about doing anything to erode the institutional character of the Senate," Thune argued on the Senate floor on Tuesday.</li><li>Democrats say Republicans are leaving the door wide open for how the CRA can be interpreted and used in the future — and point to past examples of Republicans asking the GAO to weigh in on the CRA.</li><li>"To go nuclear on something as significant as this, and to do the bidding of the fossil fuel industry, is outrageous," Schumer said on the Senate floor on Tuesday evening.</li></ul>

Title: Biden's deterioration unnerved House Democrats as early as 2023, new book reveals
Description: <p>Some of the first <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/07/06/list-house-democrats-biden-withdraw-2024-campaign" target="_blank">House Democrats</a> to call for <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/13/biden-book-wheelchair-2024-campaign-original-sin" target="_blank">former President Biden</a> to drop his reelection bid in 2024 saw firsthand signs of his deterioration as early as 2023, according to a new book by CNN's Jake Tapper and Axios' Alex Thompson.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>Many top Democrats, including White House officials, donors and lawmakers, ignored what they were seeing for months or even years. Others, the book says, noticed <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/16/biden-hur-tape-special-counsel-audio" target="_blank">Biden's shortcomings</a> but kept quiet.</p><hr><ul><li>In the end, it was self-preservation that spurred many Democrats to finally drop the charade and urge Biden to get out of the race after his disastrous presidential debate.</li><li>The book "Original Sin" is based on interviews with more than 200 people, mostly Democratic insiders, with knowledge of the events that unfolded during the final two years of Biden's presidency. Almost all of the interviews took place after the 2024 election.</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>Thompson and Tapper write that a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2023/11/27/white-house-christmas-decorations-2023" target="_blank">White House Christmas party</a> in 2023 was a watershed moment for several Democratic lawmakers.</p><ul><li>Rep. Adam Smith (D-Wash.), the ranking member of the House Armed Services Committee, was "stunned" to see Biden "completely out of it" while interacting with guests at the photo line.</li><li>Upon leaving the party, Rep. Seth Moulton (D-Mass.) and his wife, Liz, "remarked on how frail the president looked and how lethargic he seemed compared with the previous December."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>For Rep. Mike Quigley (D-Ill.), the book says, the epiphany came even earlier.</p><ul><li>During a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2023/04/13/president-biden-vists-ireland" target="_blank">trip to Ireland</a> in April 2023, Quigley saw Biden rapidly go from energetic to drained. "This was how his father, Bill, had been before he died," the authors write.</li><li>"Biden, Quigley thought, needed to go to bed for the rest of the day and night. He wasn't merely physically frail; he had lost almost all of his energy. His speech was breathless, soft, weak."</li></ul><p><strong>The other side: </strong>"There is nothing in this book that shows Joe Biden failed to do his job, as the authors have alleged, nor did they prove their allegation that there was a cover-up or conspiracy," a Biden spokesperson told Axios.</p><ul><li>"Nowhere do they show that our national security was threatened or where the President wasn't otherwise engaged in the important matters of the Presidency. In fact, Joe Biden was an effective President who led our country with empathy and skill."</li><li>Some Democrats have leapt to Biden's defense, with Rep. Jim Clyburn (D-S.C.) saying in a <a href="https://x.com/BulwarkOnline/status/1924096459814613093" target="_blank">CNN interview</a> that he "never saw anything that allowed me to think that Joe Biden was not able to do the job."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>Smith, Moulton and Quigley were among the first House Democrats to call on Biden to withdraw his bid for reelection after his debate with Trump in June 2024.</p><ul><li>But they and other House Democratic colleagues had largely kept quiet up until that point.</li><li>Former Rep. <a href="https://www.axios.com/2023/10/01/dean-phillips-steps-down-dem-leadership-biden" target="_blank">Dean Phillips</a> (D-Minn.), who challenged Biden in the Democratic primary, had "tried to get other Democrats to talk about the president's decline, but no one was willing to say anything publicly," the book says.</li><li>The former congressman is quoted as saying later: "The whale who spouts gets harpooned."</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>At a debate watch party, one House Democrat who watched the calamity unfold exclaimed to House Democratic caucus chair Pete Aguilar (D-Calif.): "I just lost my job."</p><ul><li>Former House Speaker Nancy Pelosi (D-Calif.) heard from swing-district House Democrats who "were getting polling back that indicated Biden's campaign was going to drag dozens of them down with it," the book says.</li><li>Rep. Bill Foster (D-Ill.) said at a closed-door Democratic caucus meeting: "I lived through the 2010 bloodbath — we lost sixty-three seats. That could happen again."</li></ul><p><em>This story is adapted from the <a href="https://sites.prh.com/originalsin?ref=PRH1147C5509975&amp;aid=8075&amp;linkid=PRH1147C5509975" target="_blank">book</a>, "Original Sin: President Biden's Decline, Its Cover-Up, and His Disastrous Choice to Run Again," by CNN's Jake Tapper and Axios' Alex Thompson.</em></p>

Title: Trump and Hegseth unveil $175 billion plans for Golden Dome missile shield
Description: <p>President <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">Trump</a> on Tuesday touted $25 billion in initial funding for the "<a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/19/trump-iron-dome-technology-costs" target="_blank">Golden Dome</a>" and put Space Force Gen. Michael Guetlein in charge of realizing the hemispheric missile shield.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>Golden Dome — previously dubbed Iron Dome, but separate from Israel's missile defense program — is a mammoth undertaking with enthusiastic backing from the president but many doubters in the national security community.</p><hr><ul><li>Trump said the project will cost around $175 billion and be built over the next three years, though those are both just estimates. The initial $25 billion will be included in the "<a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/trump-mike-johnson-freedom-caucus-tax-bill" target="_blank">big beautiful bill</a>" working its way through Congress, Trump said.</li><li>Planning, building, operating and maintaining the Golden Dome, as well as paying for it, will require intense coordination between <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/26/pentagon-hegseth-doge-musk-layoffs" target="_blank">the Pentagon</a>, Congress, current and future presidents, defense contractors and troops. Trump said Canada also expressed interest in being covered by the shield but would have to "pay their fair share."</li><li>Analysts have expressed doubts about the plausibility — and immense costs — of replicating Israel's air defense capabilities at a continental scale. Trump, however, remains bullish.</li></ul><p><strong>The latest: </strong>Trump and Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth discussed the envisioned countermeasures during a televised Oval Office meeting.</p><ul><li>They said the missile shield will be designed to block hypersonic missiles, ICBMs and other projectiles, including nuclear weapons, whether they are launched from the earth's surface or from space.</li><li>Trump said President Reagan had wanted to build something similar during the Cold War "but they didn't have the technology." Now, he said, the U.S. has "super technology."</li><li>"This is very important for the success and even survival of our country. It's a pretty evil world out there," Trump said.</li></ul><p><strong>How it works: </strong>At the heart of Golden Dome is a mesh of sensors and spotters and space-based interceptors.</p><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>Defense companies have been jockeying for position since Trump signed an executive order in January to pursue it.</p><ul><li>Lockheed Martin pitched its <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/15/f35-f55-trump-qatar-lockheed" target="_blank">F-35 stealth fighter</a>, Sentinel A4 radars, command-and-control networks and more as components. Chief operating officer Frank St. John told Axios the project will "require the best of every technology company."</li><li>Booz Allen Hamilton unveiled Brilliant Swarms, a nod to the Reagan-era Brilliant Pebbles. It envisions masses of satellites capable of detecting and smashing into missiles. "The longer you wait to kill an enemy ballistic missile, the harder your problem gets," executive vice president Chris Bogdan <a href="https://www.axios.com/newsletters/axios-future-of-defense-588ffe40-0fbe-11f0-a03c-4d6b66c34260" target="_blank">told Axios</a>.</li><li>Meanwhile, Anduril Industries, <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/12/palantir-anduril-titan-army-california" target="_blank">Palantir Technologies</a> and SpaceX were collaborating on dome-related plans, according to Reuters.</li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/14/nuke-spending-cbo-report-criticism" target="_blank">U.S. to spend $1 trillion on nuclear weapons over next decade</a></p>

Title: Biden agreed to $4 million campaign salary for top aide: new book
Description: <p><em>This story is adapted from the <a href="https://sites.prh.com/originalsin?ref=PRH1147C5509975&amp;aid=8075&amp;linkid=PRH1147C5509975" target="_blank">new book</a> "Original Sin: President Biden's Decline, Its Cover-Up, and His Disastrous Choice to Run Again," by CNN's Jake Tapper and Axios' Alex Thompson.</em></p><p>Mike Donilon, a top adviser to former <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/13/biden-book-wheelchair-2024-campaign-original-sin" target="_blank">President Biden</a>, was paid about $4 million to work on the 2024 Biden campaign at the president's insistence, CNN's Jake Tapper and Axios' Alex Thompson write in their new book, "<a href="https://sites.prh.com/originalsin?ref=PRH1147C5509975&amp;aid=8075&amp;linkid=PRH1147C5509975" target="_blank">Original Sin</a>."</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The sum was orders of magnitude higher than the pay for other top aides — campaign chair Jen O'Malley Dillon made $300,000 — and illustrates the standing held by Biden's inner-most circle of advisers.</p><hr><ul><li>Many former Biden officials remain bitter at Donilon for making so much money and, in their view, guiding the campaign into disaster. </li></ul><p><strong>Behind the scenes: </strong>In early 2024,<strong> </strong>Donilon agreed to shift from the White House to the campaign, but wouldn't budge on his asking price.</p><ul><li>"The president told the campaign: Pay Mike what he wants," the authors report. Title: Government contractors are lining up to work with DOGE
Description: <p>Security contractors are adapting to the <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/doge-department-of-government-efficiency" target="_blank">Department of Government Efficiency's</a> brutal cost-cutting regime — by pitching their tech as essential to its mission.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>As federal workforce cuts deepen, DOGE is expected to lean more heavily on third-party security vendors to help dismantle longstanding information silos — despite <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/09/elon-musk-doge-federal-it-national-security" target="_blank">the national security risks</a> that could come from its quest.</p><hr><p><strong>Driving the news:</strong> In recent weeks, DOGE has quietly begun laying the groundwork for what privacy advocates long feared was its endgame: building a <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2025/05/07/doge-government-data-immigration-social-security/" target="_blank">centralized database</a> containing the personal information of millions of U.S. citizens and residents.</p><ul><li>Some <a href="https://www.wired.com/story/doge-recruiter-ai-agents-palantir-clown-emoji/" target="_blank">reports</a> also suggest DOGE is exploring ways to deploy AI agents to replace federal workers across agencies, fueling further alarm about the national security and privacy implications.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines:</strong> Several companies are now marketing their tools directly to agencies as a way to survive DOGE's cost-cutting demands.</p><ul><li>ServiceNow CEO Bill McDermott <a href="https://www.marketwatch.com/story/servicenows-stock-pops-as-earnings-beat-quiets-doge-fears-e936cde7" target="_blank">said in an earnings call</a> last month that his company is benefiting from the shift. "In this moment, we're one of the rare companies that will grow 30% year over year in the public sector," he said.</li><li>Wired <a href="https://www.wired.com/story/openai-fda-doge-ai-drug-evaluation/" target="_blank">reported</a> this month that OpenAI has met with the Food and Drug Administration about a tool to evaluate new drugs. Two DOGE associates were also in attendance, according to the report.</li><li>A source familiar with the matter confirmed the meetings to Axios, noting that OpenAI has shown clear interest in working specifically with the FDA in some capacity. However, no contracts have been signed yet.</li></ul><p><strong>The intrigue:</strong> Many of these vendors have ramped up their lobbying power in recent months — particularly with Trump-aligned lobbying firms.</p><ul><li>So far in 2025, at least nine security and consulting firms, including Zscaler, Accenture, and Booz Allen Hamilton, have registered with <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/11/brian-ballard-trump-west-wing" target="_blank">Ballard Partners</a>, according to congressional lobbying disclosures.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>Axonius, an Israeli cybersecurity startup with growing federal ambitions, told Axios it's started pitching itself to agencies as a tool that can help them dodge the most severe DOGE audits.</p><ul><li>The company's platform gives administrators full visibility into devices, software and users, aligning closely with DOGE's stated mission to <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/25/trump-executive-order-musk-doge-data" target="_blank">streamline IT environments</a>.</li><li>Tom Kennedy, vice president of Axonius Federal Systems, told Axios that the company's tools can be "part of a great efficiency story" and that its technology usually gets through relevant DOGE audits.</li><li>But Brian Meyer, field CTO at Axonius Federal Systems, added that the company's pitch doesn't endorse job cuts.</li><li>"Even before the DOGE, there was a problem in the cybersecurity industry for full-time employees — they're already trying to do more with less," he said. "We've been telling that story for years: Based on what we have, you can do more with the resources that you have."</li></ul><p><strong>The big picture:</strong> The federal cybersecurity ecosystem has been on edge during the early months of the second Trump administration, amid <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/04/cisa-workforce-layoffs-trump-administration" target="_blank">staff cuts</a> in the federal cyber workforce and a pending Department of Justice investigation into former CISA director <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/09/chris-krebs-miles-taylor-doj-investigation-trump" target="_blank">Chris Krebs</a>.</p><ul><li>Several administration officials met with companies on the sidelines of the RSA Conference last month in the hopes of <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/02/trump-administration-cybersecurity-talks-rsa-conference" target="_blank">mending some of these relationships</a>.</li><li>Still, some executives say federal work has remained consistent. "We have been really privileged to have a strong relationship with every White House administration," Cloudflare CEO Matthew Prince told Axios in an interview.</li><li>"It feels like everything today is a partisan issue — but cybersecurity is on the less partisan side of that equation," he added.</li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but:</strong> That hasn't spared vendors from fallout.</p><ul><li>Security research government contractor Mitre is <a href="https://www.ffxnow.com/2025/04/04/report-federal-contractors-in-tysons-reston-to-lay-off-workers/" target="_blank">laying off</a> 442 employees, or nearly 5% of its workforce, in June due in part to contract cancellations.</li><li>Deloitte has also shared <a href="https://www.hr-brew.com/stories/2025/04/11/what-layoffs-at-consultancies-like-deloitte-mean-for-recruiters" target="_blank">plans</a> to lay off staff, and other consulting firms have <a href="https://www.reuters.com/technology/accenture-raises-lower-end-full-year-revenue-forecast-2025-03-20/" target="_blank">warned</a> of declining U.S. federal revenues this year.</li><li>"It's disruptive, there's no other way to put it," Kennedy said of DOGE's cuts to the federal cybersecurity workforce. "We were hoping that cybersecurity would be sheltered, and it has not been from a human side."</li></ul><p><strong>What to watch:</strong> Courts have continued to stonewall some of DOGE's most ambitious efforts, including accessing <a href="https://www.cnbc.com/2025/04/21/court-blocks-doge-access-to-sensitive-personal-social-security-data.html" target="_blank">personal information</a> at <a href="https://www.scotusblog.com/2025/05/trump-asks-high-court-to-allow-doge-access-to-social-security-records/" target="_blank">the Social Security Administration</a>.</p><ul><li>Lawmakers have <a href="https://cyberscoop.com/doge-dismantles-cisa-cybersecurity-trump-elon-musk-eric-swallwell-op-ed/" target="_blank">raised serious concerns</a> about the scope of the contractor and workforce cuts at CISA.</li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper</strong>: <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/25/elon-musk-doge-legacy" target="_blank">Elon Musk leaves legacy of self-destruction at DOGE</a></p>
