Title: Trump tells House GOP not to "f**k around" with Medicaid
Description: <p>President Trump warned congressional Republicans on Tuesday not to "f**k around" with <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/obamacare-aca-repeal-fight-again" target="_blank">Medicaid</a>, a stark pushback to conservative lawmakers demanding steeper cuts to the program in "<a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/house-budget-reconciliation-vote" target="_blank">one big, beautiful bill</a>." </p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>Trump is already floating political retribution for Republican holdouts who don't get in line.</p><hr><ul><li>He also tore into Rep. Thomas Massie (R-Ky.), who has been a firm "no" on the bill throughout the process, blasting him publicly and privately as a "grandstander" and saying he should be "voted out of office."</li><li>Trump also warned the GOP's blue state holdouts not to push too hard on the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/mike-johnson-salt-deduction-income-limits" target="_blank">SALT deduction cap</a>. </li></ul><p><strong>The big picture</strong>: Millions of people could lose health coverage if the current reconciliation bill's Medicaid cuts become law.  </p><ul><li>"President Trump and Republicans are protecting and preserving Medicaid for the Americans who the program was intended to be a lifeline for: pregnant women, children, disabled individuals, and seniors," White House spokesperson Kush Desai told Axios' Emily Peck. </li><li>That White House list of people who need Medicaid doesn't include the poorer working-age adults without kids who gained coverage under the Affordable Care Act's expansion of Medicaid.</li></ul><p><em>This is a breaking news story and will be updated.</em></p>

Title: Musk says he'll do "a lot less" political spending moving forward
Description: <p>MAGA ally <a href="https://www.axios.com/business/elon-musk" target="_blank">Elon Musk</a> said on Tuesday that he plans to spend "a lot less" on political donations moving forward after <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/10/16/musk-trump-donation-america-pac-republican-mega-donor" target="_blank">funneling millions</a> into Donald Trump's 2024 presidential campaign.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>The comment from the richest man in the world could come as a disappointment for Republicans in 2026.</p><hr><ul><li>Musk spent more than <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/12/06/elon-musk-trump-donations-pac-rbg-abortion" target="_blank">$250 million</a> in a push to return <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">Trump</a> to the White House.</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>When asked at the Qatar Economic Forum if he would continue spending at such high levels in future elections, he said he thinks that "in terms of political spending, I'm going to do a lot less in the future."</p><ul><li>Pressed on why, Musk replied, "I think I've done enough." </li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but: </strong>The Tesla CEO, who appeared virtually for the conversation, said if he sees "a reason" to spend, he will. However, he added, "I do not currently see a reason."</p><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>Musk <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/07/13/donald-trump-shots-fired-rally-elon-musk" target="_blank">endorsed Trump</a> last year after the Butler, Pennsylvania, assassination attempt and later became a key — yet highly controversial — <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/10/16/musk-trump-donation-america-pac-republican-mega-donor" target="_blank">GOP megadonor</a>.</p><ul><li><a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/10/24/elon-musk-million-dollar-giveaway-doj-warning" target="_blank">Musk's lottery</a> offering $1 million prizes to registered voters in swing states was scrutinized as legally questionable during the 2024 race, and the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/31/musk-wisconsin-state-supreme-court" target="_blank">eyebrow-raising giveaways</a> made a comeback during the closely watched Wisconsin Supreme Court race earlier this year.</li><li>Musk poured millions into the election, only to see the conservative-backed candidate defeated in the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/01/wisconsin-supreme-court-election-expensive-donations" target="_blank">most expensive</a> judicial race in U.S. history.</li></ul><p><strong>Catch up quick: </strong>Musk has led a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/03/usaid-musk-trump-what-to-know" target="_blank">DOGE-driven crusade</a> against so-called government "waste," directing a massive upheaval of the federal government during Trump's second term that's seen thousands of workers ousted from their jobs and carved out massive spending cuts.</p><ul><li>The chaos has left him with a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/25/elon-musk-doge-legacy" target="_blank">wounded reputation</a> and prompted brand blowback, Axios' Zachary Basu reports. </li><li>That's triggered protests and, in some cases, vandalism involving Tesla cars and showrooms. Musk on Tuesday <a href="https://x.com/elonmusk/status/1924837701917782464" target="_blank">said</a>, "[w]e are coming for those who organized the violence &amp; death threats against Tesla."</li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/axios-harris-poll-tesla-spacex-elon-musk" target="_blank">Tesla, SpaceX reputations crater in new Axios Harris Poll 100</a></p><p><em>Editor's note: This is a breaking news story and will be updated. </em></p>

Title: Rising costs rip into business reputation
Description: <p>Business reputation is eroding due to consumer concerns about <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/15/walmart-store-prices-trump-tariffs" target="_blank">rising costs</a>, according to this year's <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/axios-harris-poll-company-reputation-ranking" target="_blank">Axios Harris Poll 100</a>, which assigns reputation scores based on seven categories like trust, products and services, vision and culture.</p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> Companies that have kept costs low while standing firm on their corporate values rank highest on this year's list. </p><hr><p><strong>State of play:</strong> Trader Joe's, the low-cost grocer known for being <a href="https://www.supermarketnews.com/company-news/retailer-dei-backlash-where-do-we-go-from-here-" target="_blank">values-focused</a>, ranks No. 1 on the list and saw a 3.5-point increase in its reputation score since last year. </p><ul><li><a href="http://axios.com/2025/01/23/costco-dei-shareholders-reject-anti-diversity-proposal" target="_blank">Costco</a> ranks in the top 5, and Arizona Beverage Co., known for its <a href="https://www.cnbc.com/2024/06/27/why-arizona-iced-tea-ceo-says-he-wont-raise-iconic-99-cent-price-tag.html" target="_blank">99-cent iced tea</a>, joined the list for the first time, coming in at No. 7.</li></ul><p><strong>The big picture:</strong> Consumer sentiment is in free fall,<strong> </strong>according to a new University of Michigan <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/tariffs-consumer-economy-sentiment" target="_blank">report</a>.</p><ul><li>Inflation expectations are higher than those reported in 2022, with respondents pointing to <a href="https://www.axios.com/economy/tariffs" target="_blank">tariffs</a> as potentially inflationary and economically damaging.</li><li>This comes amid Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent's <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/18/trump-tariffs-bessent-walmart-prices" target="_blank">acknowledgement</a> on Sunday that some consumer prices will likely rise due to tariffs.</li></ul><p><strong>By the numbers: </strong>Spiraling consumer sentiment is likely to impact business reputation and favorability, according to the Harris Poll survey.</p><ul><li>78% of Americans have noticed the increasing costs of groceries.</li><li>Meanwhile, 4 in 10 Americans say their overall opinion of companies is declining, with most pointing to inflation as the top reason. </li><li>However, those surveyed also say that companies with strong values are better protected from reputational damage.</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying: </strong>The companies ranking highest on the list are "delivering value through their values," says John Gerzema, CEO of the Harris Poll.</p><ul><li>"Americans have shifted their attention almost singularly toward inflation and high prices. And so now, corporate reputation is make or break on allyship: Are they looking out for my bottom line or theirs? The companies that are thriving [this] year are intentional, empathic and most of all, dependable."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>Clear and consistent corporate values can serve as a safety net, according to the survey.</p><ul><li>Costco (No. 5) <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/01/23/costco-dei-shareholders-reject-anti-diversity-proposal" target="_blank">made headlines</a> for upholding its commitments to diversity, equity and inclusion, while <a href="https://www.axios.com/2023/05/25/patagonia-harris-poll-reputation" target="_blank">Patagonia</a> (No. 2) is known for its pledge to fight climate change.</li><li>Meanwhile, companies that are viewed by consumers as leaning toward one political ideology — like <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/14/ben-jerrys-co-founder-arrested-kennedy-hearing-protests" target="_blank">Ben &amp; Jerry's</a> (No. 24) or <a href="https://www.axios.com/2023/05/31/anti-woke-movement-spac-investment-publicsq-target" target="_blank">Chick-fil-A</a> (No. 26) — rank highly.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>Potential price increases threaten the reputation of budget-friendly companies like Dollar Tree (No. 75), Dollar General (No. 85) and Spirit Airlines (No. 100), per the rankings.</p><ul><li>Both dollar stores anticipate <a href="https://www.barrons.com/articles/dollar-general-stock-upgrade-tariffs-2ea78197" target="_blank">disruptions</a> or added costs brought on by President Trump's tariff policies, while Spirit Airlines has <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/07/30/spirit-airlines-premium-fares" target="_blank">introduced </a>premium fares.</li><li>Meanwhile, Chinese e-commerce companies like Temu (No. 90) and Shein (No. 94) are <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/14/china-trade-deal-shein-temu-tariffs" target="_blank">particularly exposed</a> to tariffs, dropping in score to sit in the ranking's bottom 10%.</li></ul><p><strong>What to watch: </strong>While corporate leaders are signaling potential price increases due to Trump's trade policies, few have publicly opposed the tariffs.   </p><ul><li>According to the Harris Poll survey, more than half of Americans say their opinion of companies would improve if they spoke out against tariffs.</li></ul><p><strong>More on Axios:</strong><em> </em></p><ul><li><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/axios-harris-poll-company-reputation-ranking" target="_blank">Full results and poll methodology</a></li></ul>

Title: Trump frustrated by Gaza war, wants Netanyahu to "wrap it up": White House officials
Description: <p>President <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">Trump</a> has been frustrated by the ongoing <a href="https://www.axios.com/world/israel" target="_blank">war in Gaza</a> and upset by images of suffering of Palestinian children, and has told his aides to tell Israeli Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu he wants him to wrap it up, two White House officials tell Axios.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>U.S. and Israeli officials deny that Trump is prepared to "abandon" Israel, or that he is applying intense pressure on Netanyahu. But they admit there are growing policy differences between a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/18/gaza-ceasefire-hamas-trump" target="_blank">president who wants to end the war</a> and a prime minister who is massively expanding it.</p><hr><ul><li>"The president is frustrated about what is happening in Gaza. He wants the war to end, he wants the hostages to come home, he wants aid to go in and he wants to start rebuilding Gaza," one White House official said.</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news:</strong> In the days since Trump's trip to the region, the U.S. has been <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/18/gaza-ceasefire-hamas-trump" target="_blank">pressing</a> both Israel and Hamas to accept a new proposal presented by White House envoy Steve Witkoff for a hostage and ceasefire deal. </p><ul><li>Witkoff has been speaking directly with Netanyahu and his top adviser Ron Dermer, and to Hamas leadership through a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/13/edan-alexander-release-secret-talks-bahbah" target="_self">backchannel</a> facilitated by Palestinian-American businessman Bishara Bahbah.</li><li>The negotiations have shown little progress. Meanwhile, the Israel Defense Forces are proceeding with an operation to displace all 2 million Palestinians in Gaza to a "humanitarian zone" and flatten most of the enclave.</li><li>The logjam in the talks and the situation on the ground convinced Vice President Vance to <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/vance-skip-israel-visit-gaza-operation" target="_blank">scrap plans</a> for a visit to Israel this week. His decision sheds light on how the U.S. feels about the current Israeli policy in Gaza.</li></ul><p><strong>The other side: </strong>An Israeli official told Axios that at the moment, Netanyahu doesn't feel strong pressure from Trump. "If the president wants a hostage and ceasefire deal in Gaza he needs to put much more pressure on both sides," the official said.  </p><ul><li>Other leaders are attempting to apply pressure. The leaders of the U.K., France and Canada <a href="https://www.gov.uk/government/news/joint-statement-from-the-leaders-of-the-united-kingdom-france-and-canada-on-the-situation-in-gaza-and-the-west-bank" target="_blank">issued a statement</a> on Monday threatening to take steps against Israel over the war in Gaza.</li><li>"We will not stand by while the Netanyahu Government pursues these egregious actions. If Israel does not cease the renewed military offensive and lift its restrictions on humanitarian aid, we will take further concrete actions in response" they said.</li><li>Netanyahu <a href="https://x.com/netanyahu/status/1924569469281550689" target="_blank">rejected</a> their call and accused "the leaders in London, Ottawa and Paris" of "offering a huge prize for the genocidal attack on Israel on October 7 while inviting more such atrocities."</li></ul><p><strong>The latest:</strong> The British government announced on Monday that it is suspending free trade deal negotiations with Israel, imposed new sanctions on Israeli settlers involved in attacks on Palestinians in the West Bank and summoned the Israeli ambassador to the Foreign Office in London.</p><p><strong>State of play:</strong> One area where Trump has put pressure on Netanyahu over the last two weeks is Israel's total freeze on humanitarian aid deliveries to Gaza. </p><ul><li>A White House official told Axios the president was upset by pictures of suffering children and babies in Gaza and pressed the Israelis to reopen the gates. </li><li>On Sunday, the Israeli cabinet <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/18/gaza-humanitarian-aid-israel" target="_blank">approved</a> the resumption of aid deliveries to Gaza and on Monday a dozen trucks with baby food and other supplies entered the enclave. The White House official said more needs to be done.    </li><li>The UN has warned that thousands of children are at risk of starvation if aid does not significantly increase. More than 55,000 Palestinians have been killed during the war, according to the health ministry in Hamas-run Gaza.</li></ul><p><strong>Behind the scenes:</strong> While Trump felt his Middle East trip was a success, he believes the war in Gaza is holding back his plans for the region, a senior White House official said.</p><ul><li>"The President sees a real chance for peace and prosperity in the region, but the war in Gaza is the last hot spot and he wants it to end," the White House official said. </li><li>The second White House official described the war as a distraction from other things Trump wants to do. "There is a lot of frustration by this crisis getting dragged on."</li><li>The official said Trump's decision to move unilaterally to secure the release of American-Israeli hostage Edan Alexander, rather than waiting for Israel to agree to a broader dael, was a result of this frustration.   </li></ul><p><strong>What they are saying:</strong> "The President may be saying, 'Hey, listen, let's try to end the war,' he might speak strongly… But his support is ironclad," Trump hostage response envoy Adan Boehler <a href="https://www.foxnews.com/world/trump-hostage-envoy-dismisses-report-israel-abandonment-threat-fake-news" target="_blank">told Fox News</a> on Monday. He stressed that a Washington Post report claiming the administration threatened to "abandon" Israel was "fake."</p><ul><li>White House press secretary Karoline Leavitt told reporters Monday that Trump had "made it very clear to Hamas that he wanted to see all hostages released" and "made it very clear he wants to see this conflict in the region end."</li></ul><p> </p>

Title: The lose-lose calculus of the White House trade war
Description: <p>Usually, there's at least one big group that stands to benefit from White House economic policy: businesses, workers or consumers.</p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> In this moment, it's not exactly clear who wins from the current administration's triple play of raising tariffs, cutting workplace regulations, and cracking down on immigration.</p><hr><p><strong>State of play: </strong>President Trump <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/17/trump-walmart-tariffs" target="_blank">lashed out</a> at Walmart last weekend, after the company said it would be forced to raise prices to handle higher tariff costs.</p><ul><li>The retailer is the latest company to run into the buzzsaw of the White House trade agenda.</li></ul><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>The White House says its agenda spurs investments that benefit consumers and workers, but shifting trade policy, combined with other fast-paced changes, is creating uncertainty that's roiling almost all corners of <a href="https://www.axios.com/economy" target="_blank">the economy</a>.</p><p><strong>Zoom in:</strong> "We've been rocked very hard by the tariffs," says Jonathan Silva, co-owner of WS Game Company, an upscale board-game business that his father started 25 years ago.</p><ul><li>Since "Liberation Day" in April, Silva's raised prices for games, halted all shipments from China, taken a pay cut, and paused retirement benefit contributions for the Massachusetts-based company's 22 employees.</li><li>Now that the most onerous China tariffs have been lifted, the race is on to ship inventory in the next 90 days before the holiday season. He's worried about shipping companies jacking up costs as demand spikes.</li><li>"No matter what happens, the writing's on the wall that with an executive order, things can change on, you know, on just a random Monday."</li></ul><p><strong>Workers, meanwhile, </strong>haven't caught much of a break either. Small business employees, such as those working for Silva, are in a bad spot. Many more are <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/07/labor-market-recession-glassdoor" target="_blank">concerned</a> about holding on to their jobs.</p><ul><li>It's not just them. Tens of thousands of federal workers have been fired, with many more on deck. Those in unions are fighting to keep their right to collective bargaining.</li><li>The harsher situation for public workers is also trickling down to the private sector, where management is newly emboldened to crack the whip, as <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/07/trump-musk-management-labor-rights" target="_blank">Axios</a> and the <a href="https://www.wsj.com/lifestyle/workplace/corporate-bosses-workers-culture-changing-cbd19c2c" target="_blank">Wall Street Journal</a> have reported.</li><li>Other changes have hurt, too, like weakening agencies critical to worker protections and reducing the minimum wage for federal contractors.</li></ul><p> <strong>As for consumers? </strong>Tariffs typically mean higher prices. The duties raise input costs for companies, making it more expensive to produce and sell goods, which means higher prices for working people.</p><ul><li>Nobody seems to benefit, former Treasury Secretary Larry Summers tells Axios, who says the likelihood is that the tariffs "are going to create<em> </em>fewer good-paying jobs."</li></ul><h2>Looking for winners</h2><p><strong>Reality check: </strong>For all the dire recession warnings, the overall hard data show the economy in good shape.</p><ul><li>The unemployment rate is still low, and inflation is easing.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>The White House seeks to position itself as both pro-business and pro-worker.</p><ul><li>The coming "big beautiful" tax bill is getting positioned as a big win for businesses and working people, who may wind up with some nice new  breaks, including no taxes on tips and a higher standard deduction.</li><li>And those easier regulations are often a win for businesses. The share of executives who say they're concerned about labor regulations fell to 56% this year, down from 73%, per a recent survey from Littler Mendelson, the employment law firm.</li><li>In a recent press release, the White House pointed to a <a href="https://www.wsj.com/economy/trade/trumps-tariffs-are-lifting-some-u-s-manufacturers-06b4c6e1" target="_blank">Wall Street Journal</a> story that reports some small and midsize U.S. manufacturers are actually seeing increased<em> </em>business due to tariffs.</li></ul><p><strong>For the record: </strong>"The Trump administration is slashing costly regulations, lowering energy prices, cutting Joe Biden's runaway spending that sparked inflation, negotiating better trade deals, and spurring trillions in historic investment commitments, including in sectors critical to our national and economic security," White House spokesman Kush Desai says.</p><ul><li>"Any 'economist' who can't understand how this agenda is benefitting American workers and industries, as the data proves is already happening, should find a new profession."</li></ul><p><strong>The bottom line: </strong>Critics argue the small pockets of victory don't seem to outweigh the downsides.</p><ul><li>Some pockets of businesses want certain tariffs in place, acknowledges Heidi Shierholz, the president of the liberal Economic Policy Institute.</li><li>But there isn't a big constituency out there who wanted them to this scale. </li></ul>

Title: Exclusive: Opioid use disorder costs almost $700K per case
Description: <div>Data: Avalere Health; Map: Axios Visuals</div><p><a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/09/24/opioid-abuse-treatments-barriers" target="_blank">Opioid abuse</a> is as much an economic problem as a public health one, according to a comprehensive analysis provided first to Axios that concludes the total average annual cost associated with each case is nearly $700,000. </p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> The cost burden falls <a href="https://www.axios.com/2023/09/28/charted-medical-claims-related-to-opioid-dependence" target="_blank">unevenly</a>, with states in a belt stretching through Appalachia to New England typically having bigger caseloads<strong> </strong>and a higher cost per case.</p><hr><ul><li>Opioid use disorder cost the U.S. an estimated $4 trillion last year, per the <a href="https://advisory.avalerehealth.com/insights/white-paper-the-cost-of-opioid-use-disorder" target="_blank">analysis from Avalere</a>, which used 2017 figures to project 2024 net costs. </li><li>"While this is a cost to government, it's also a cost to private businesses, and the huge cost, of course, is to the individuals who have OUD," said Margaret Scott, a principal at Avalere and author of the report.</li></ul><p><strong>By the numbers:</strong> The projected cost of opioid use disorder in 2024 ranged from $419,527 per case in Idaho to more than $2.4 million in D.C. That covers lost productivity, health insurance costs, property lost to crime and other variables. </p><ul><li>The cost per case totaled more than $1 million in West Virginia, Rhode Island, Ohio and Maryland.  </li><li>Some of the regional variation in costs is from lost tax revenue, which varies by state. The local availability of treatment for opioid use disorder may also drive the cost, Scott said. </li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>Opioid use disorder — defined as frequent opioid use and unsuccessful efforts to quit — is estimated to affect <a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/data/sites/default/files/reports/rpt42731/2022-nsduh-nnr.pdf" target="_blank">more than 6 million people</a> in the United States. </p><ul><li>The cumulative economic burden on patients, including years of life lost and reduced quality of life, exceeded $3 trillion in 2024, Avalere estimated.  </li><li>Private businesses absorbed more than $467 billion in costs from lost productivity and health insurance costs while the federal government bore about $118 billion in Medicare and other federal insurance costs, lost taxes and criminal justice expenses. </li><li>It cost state and local governments more than $94 billion, with about $42 billion of that going toward criminal justice costs. </li><li>The Trump administration in March released its <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/articles/2025/03/the-staggering-cost-of-the-illicit-opioid-epidemic-in-the-united-states/#:~:text=Our%20cost%20estimates%20are%20based,2024%20dollars%2C%20is%20as%20follows:" target="_blank">own analysis</a> that estimated illicit opioids cost the U.S. about $2.7 trillion in 2023.</li></ul><p><strong>Where it stands:</strong> Treatment can defray the costs by more than 40% in some instances, the analysis found. </p><ul><li>Behavioral therapy alongside long-acting injectable buprenorphine —<strong> </strong>a treatment that reduces the risk of future overdoses — generated an estimated $295,000 savings per case, the biggest cost-saver of the options Avalere analyzed. </li><li>Therapy plus methadone and therapy plus buprenorphine administered through mucous membranes like the mouth each save about $271,000. Behavioral therapy alone saves a project $144,000 per case.</li><li>The treatment savings estimates assume that patients fully adhere to the regimen for a year.</li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but: </strong>Federal data from 2022 showed that only <a href="https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/73/wr/mm7325a1.htm#:~:text=In%202022%2C%203.7%25%20of%20U.S.,medications%20for%20OUD%20(30.0%25)." target="_blank">one-quarter</a> of adults who needed medication treatment for OUD actually got it. </p><ul><li>Less than half of adults who received any OUD care that year got medication treatment. </li><li>However, buprenorphine distribution <a href="https://www.kff.org/mental-health/issue-brief/addressing-the-opioid-crisis-a-look-at-the-evolving-landscape-of-federal-oud-treatment-policies/" target="_blank">increased significantly</a> between 2019 and 2022 as policy changes during the COVID-19 pandemic allowed people to start treatment via telehealth. </li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>Overdose deaths in the U.S. <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/14/opioid-overdose-deaths-fall-trump-budget-cuts-2026" target="_blank">fell to the lowest level</a> since 2019 last year, partly due to expanded availability of the overdose reversal drug naloxone. An estimated 80,391 people died from drug overdoses in 2024, down nearly 27% from the previous year, per Centers for Disease Control and Prevention data.</p><ul><li>But some addiction experts say cuts to federal grant funding and other program changes led by Health and Human Services Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. could hurt addiction recovery programs.</li></ul><p><strong>The fine print:</strong> Indivior, a pharmaceutical company specializing in treatments for opioid use disorder, funded the Avalere analysis. </p><p><em>Editor's note: The story has been corrected to reflect that the total average annual costs associated with each case reflects the full economic burden (not just the cost of treatment).</em></p>

Title: "Fire weather" is happening more often amid climate change
Description: <div>Data: <a href="https://www.climatecentral.org/climate-matters/more-frequent-fire-weather" target="_blank">Climate Central</a>; Map: Kavya Beheraj/Axios</div><p>Hot, dry and windy weather that helps <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/08/14/climate-change-extreme-wildfire-season" target="_blank">wildfires</a> spread is becoming more common across much of the U.S. amid climate change, a new analysis finds.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>What used to be several months of <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/05/15/us-wildfire-outlook-2024-climate-change" target="_blank">"fire season"</a> is stretching in some places into a yearlong phenomenon, straining fire departments and others tasked with controlling or containing wild blazes.</p><hr><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>The number of "fire weather" days rose by 37 in the Southwest and 21 in the West on average between 1973 and 2024, per an <a href="https://www.climatecentral.org/climate-matters/more-frequent-fire-weather" target="_blank">analysis</a> from Climate Central, a climate research group.</p><ul><li>Some areas, including parts of Texas, California and New Mexico, now experience "around two more months of fire weather per year compared to a half century ago," the group says.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>Fire weather is also getting more frequent in some eastern and northeastern parts of the country, like New Jersey and New York's Long Island.</p><ul><li>Both areas experienced <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/23/nj-wildfire-evacuation-new-jersey-highway-closed" target="_blank">notable</a> <a href="https://abcnews.go.com/US/long-island-new-york-wildfires-suspected-cause/story?id=119629135" target="_blank">wildfires</a> in recent months.</li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but:</strong> Fire weather days decreased in a handful of areas, such as central North Dakota (-12) and northern Maine (-8).</p><p><strong>How it works: </strong>Climate Central's analysis is based on data from 476 nationwide weather stations and is broken down by 245 climate divisions across the continental U.S.</p><ul><li>The group defined a "fire weather day" as one with temperatures of at least 45°-55°F (depending on the season), relative humidity within 5% of regional thresholds, and sustained wind speeds of 15mph or more — all happening together during at least two hourly measurements on a given day.</li></ul><p><strong>Stunning stat: </strong>Human activities (unattended campfires, sparks from power lines, etc.) start a whopping 87% of wildfires, Climate Central says, citing the National Interagency Fire Center.</p><ul><li>Regardless of how a fire starts, "fire weather" can give them the push they need to spread and grow.</li></ul><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>Extreme wildfire events more than doubled in frequency and magnitude globally over the past two decades, a recent <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/06/25/extreme-wildfires-doubled-climate-change" target="_blank">study</a> found.</p><p><strong>What's next: </strong>States like <a href="https://www.gov.ca.gov/2025/04/07/with-peak-fire-season-on-horizon-california-launches-statewide-wildfire-preparedness-campaign/" target="_blank">California</a> and <a href="https://idahonews.com/news/local/idaho-officials-prepare-for-extended-fire-season-emphasizing-year-round-fire-readiness" target="_blank">Idaho</a> are preparing for what could be a challenging fire season as higher temperatures and faster winds risk turning even the smallest sparks into massive conflagrations.</p>

Title: Trump's deference to Putin stunned European leaders on call
Description: <p>Ukrainian President Zelensky and five other European leaders joined a conference call with President <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">Trump</a> immediately after his <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/trump-putin-call-ceasefire-agreement" target="_blank">call with Vladimir Putin </a>on Monday hoping to hear that Putin had agreed to a ceasefire — or the U.S. would impose penalties on him for refusing to do so.</p><ul><li>Instead, Trump said Putin had agreed to negotiate, stressed the U.S. wouldn't be involved in those negotiations, and pushed back against the idea of imposing sanctions on Putin at the current time, two sources who were on the call and a third source briefed on the call told Axios.</li></ul><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>Trump gave the impression he was getting closer to withdrawing from the issue altogether.<strong> </strong>Some leaders on the call seemed "surprised" or "shocked," the sources said.</p><hr><ul><li>"I think something's going to happen. And if it doesn't, I just back away and they're going to have to keep going. Again, this was a European situation, and should have remained a European situation," Trump told reporters in the Oval Office several hours after his calls. </li></ul><p><strong>How it happened:</strong> Trump and Zelensky had a brief call Monday morning, and Trump asked his Ukrainian counterpart what he should tell Putin, the sources said. </p><ul><li>Zelensky was happy Trump called him to consult. He requested that Trump demand an immediate ceasefire, threaten new sanctions against Russia, and offer no concessions to Putin without consulting Ukraine, the sources say.</li></ul><p><strong>Behind the scenes: </strong>When the call with Putin ended, Trump called Zelensky again. This time the leaders of Germany, France, Italy, Finland and the European Commission were also on the line. </p><ul><li>"The second call was longer and of a different character than the first one," Zelensky said later.</li><li>While a European source on the call told Axios it was "constructive," another source said Zelensky felt it was "bad."</li></ul><p><strong>Trump told the leaders</strong> that Putin agreed to start direct negotiations on a ceasefire immediately. A source on the call said there were a few seconds of puzzled silence.</p><ul><li>Zelensky then pointed out that Putin had previously agreed to negotiate, and the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/16/russia-ukraine-ceasefire-talks-turkey" target="_blank">first round of ceasefire talks took place</a> on Friday in Istanbul. Trump didn't directly respond, the sources said. </li><li>The sources said Zelensky and several other leaders on the call told Trump it had been his idea to start the peace talks with an immediate 30-day ceasefire. </li><li>A White House official told Axios Trump "never agreed" that a ceasefire should be a prerequisite for negotiations and never said Zelensky can decide what the conditions for negotiations will be.   </li></ul><p><strong>Friction point: </strong>Other European leaders on the call asked about the possibility of U.S. sanctions against Russia, but Trump said he didn't think was a good idea and stressed that he thought Putin wanted a deal. </p><ul><li>Italian Prime Minister Giorgia Meloni jumped in to ask why there couldn't be a ceasefire for at least two weeks heading into the talks, while German Chancellor Friedrich Merz asked what concessions Russia was willing to make, the sources said. </li><li>Trump told the group Putin would present a "peace memo" with his terms for a ceasefire and for ending the war. A source on the call said Trump told Zelensky and the European leaders he asked Putin to present "something people can agree to" and not a proposal that will be rejected immediately.</li><li>Zelensky said previous rounds of negotiations with Putin, including last week, didn't produce anything and stressed that if Trump doesn't push, Putin won't move, the sources said.</li><li>The White House official said that for months Russia had refused to present a document with its vision of how to end the war and the fact Putin agreed to do it was a significant step forward.  </li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines:</strong> Leaders on the call seemed surprised that Trump seemed relatively content with what he heard from Putin, and presented it as a new development, even though the Russian leader did not seem to have changed his position at all, the sources said.</p><p><strong>What to watch:</strong> Trump told the group that Russia and Ukraine should conduct bilateral direct negotiations without any third party mediators because the parties best understand all the details of the conflict. </p><ul><li>Meloni and Merz said the U.S. and European countries need to be involved in the negotiations. "Someone needs to be a judge," Meloni said. Merz proposed holding a meeting with all the parties present.  </li><li>Trump <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/pope-leo-host-russia-ukraine-peace-talks-trump" target="_blank">later suggested the Vatican</a> as a venue for the talks.</li></ul><p><strong>Where it stands:</strong> On the call, Finland President Alexander Stubb asked Trump what the next steps were. "I don't know. Someone has to come out and say whether the negotiations are going well or badly, and then we'll decide what to do," Trump said. </p><p><em>This story was updated with comments from a White House official. </em></p>

Title: Biden's cancer diagnosis draws sympathy — and suspicion
Description: <p>Former <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/joe-biden" target="_blank">President Biden</a>'s disclosure that he had Stage 4 <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/biden-prostate-cancer-diagnosis" target="_blank">prostate cancer</a> was quickly met with <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/18/biden-cancer-prostate-tributes-congress-leaders-react" target="_blank">sympathy</a> late Sunday. By Monday morning, the questions — from Democrats and Republicans alike — had begun.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The timing of Biden's announcement, coupled with the way his handlers tried to <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/14/book-biden-cabinet-crisis-access" target="_blank">cover up his health issues</a> in the past, fueled speculation about how long he'd known about the cancer.</p><hr><p>People in both parties, whether they love Joe Biden or despise him, wondered whether the announcement was timed to change the subject after a week of reports about his physical and mental deterioration when he was president.</p><ul><li>Those reports included <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/16/biden-hur-tape-special-counsel-audio" target="_blank">recordings</a>, first posted Friday by Axios, of Biden being interviewed by prosecutors in 2023 about his handling of classified documents. Biden had such difficulty recalling events that prosecutor Robert Hur later described him as a "well-meaning, elderly man with a poor memory."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in:</strong> On Monday, medical experts didn't exactly calm the suspicions about Biden's cancer diagnosis — even as they said it was treatable and that he could live several years with the disease.</p><ul><li>"He's had this for many years, maybe even a decade, growing there and spreading," Ezekiel Emanuel, an oncologist who was a Biden White House COVID adviser, told the <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/news/morning-joe-stunned-oncologist-says-131633655.html" target="_blank">stunned hosts</a> of MSNBC's "Morning Joe."</li><li>Emanuel later told CNN that the prostate-specific antigen (PSA) blood test used to detect prostate cancer isn't always reliable. Emanuel and other doctors noted that Biden, 82, is well beyond the 55-70 recommended age range for prostate cancer screening.</li><li>But given how thoroughly presidents' health is scrutinized, it would be surprising if Biden hadn't been tested before his recent symptoms appeared, Emanuel said on "Morning Joe": "It's a little strange."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out:</strong> Several former Biden White House aides acknowledged they were perplexed.</p><ul><li>"I love Joe Biden," a former campaign and White House aide told Axios. "But I don't feel the same about some of the people around him. So I feel terrible saying this: I just don't know what to believe."</li></ul><p><strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">President Trump</a></strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank"></a> and the White House initially offered sympathy for Biden and did not engage in speculation on Sunday.</p><ul><li>But on Monday, Trump told reporters: "I'm surprised the public wasn't notified a long time ago ... I think if you take a look, it's the same doctor who said Joe was cognitively fine."</li></ul><p><strong>Some of Trump's MAGA loyalists</strong> struck a similar chord on social media, sending a mix of prayers and I-told-you-so messages about Biden's health — an issue they'd been harping on for years.</p><ul><li>Vice President Vance <a href="https://x.com/ericldaugh/status/1924472174225633681?s=46" target="_blank">questioned</a> the care Biden received and whether his advisers were honest, telling reporters: "We can pray for good health — but also recognize that if you're not in good enough health to do the job, you shouldn't be doing the job."</li><li>Donald Trump Jr. asked on <a href="https://x.com/DonaldJTrumpJr/status/1924250965965709808" target="_blank">X</a> whether former First Lady Jill Biden was part of "another coverup."</li></ul><p><strong>Flashback: </strong>The Bidens have been silent about cancer in the family before, according to "<a href="https://www.amazon.com/Original-Sin-President-Cover-Up-Disastrous-ebook/dp/B0DXCMSHVL" target="_blank">Original Sin</a>," a book by Axios' Alex Thompson and CNN's Jake Tapper that's being released today.</p><ul><li>When the Bidens' son Beau was attorney general of Delaware in 2013, he had brain surgery to remove a tumor and was diagnosed with Stage 4 glioblastoma — one of the deadliest forms of brain cancer.</li><li>Beau and then-Vice President Biden's teams deliberated whether to explain his situation publicly, but decided to say nothing for months, according to "Original Sin."</li></ul><p><strong>In February 2014</strong>, Dr. Wai-Kwan Alfred Yung released a statement that Beau had a "clean bill of health."</p><ul><li>Beau Biden died 15 months later, soon after he left office.</li><li>The book says that for the last year of his life, as he had difficulties with speech and other everyday tasks, Beau Biden was quietly flown around the country for experimental treatments and usually admitted into hospitals under an alias: George Lincoln.</li></ul><p><strong>Even some members </strong>of the Biden family didn't understand the lack of transparency.</p><ul><li>According to "Original Sin," Beau's wife, Hallie, expressed frustration about concealing the disease rather than telling people. The public would rally around Beau, she argued to friends. But Joe and Beau Biden opposed going public.</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying:</strong> A Biden spokesperson declined to comment on Monday. </p><ul><li>But on Tuesday the former president's team shed some light on Biden's diagnosis, saying that his "last known PSA [test] was in 2014," meaning he stopped getting tested when he was 70 or 71, about the age at which the test no longer is recommended.</li><li>The spokesperson added: "Prior to Friday, President Biden had never been diagnosed with prostate cancer."</li></ul><p><em>This story has been updated to reflect the Biden spokesperson's comment on Tuesday. </em></p>

Title: Gen Z's new side hustle: selling data
Description: <p>Many young people are more willing than their parents to share personal data, giving companies deeper insight into their lives.</p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> Selling data is becoming the new selling plasma.</p><hr><p><strong>Case in point: </strong>Generation Lab, a youth polling company, is launching a new product, <a href="https://verbai.generationlab.org/" target="_blank">Verb.AI</a>, today — betting that buying this data is the future of polling.</p><ul><li>"We think corporations have extracted user data without fairly compensating people for their own data," says Cyrus Beschloss, CEO of Generation Lab. "We think users should know exactly what data they're giving us and should feel good about what they're receiving in return."</li></ul><p><strong>How it works: </strong>Generation Lab offers people cash — $50 or more per month, depending on use and other factors — to download a tracker onto their phones.</p><ul><li>The product takes about 90 seconds to download, and once it’s on your phone, it tracks things like what you browse, what you buy, which streaming apps you use — all anonymously. There are also things it doesn't track, like activity on your bank account.</li><li>Verb then uses that data to create a digital twin of you that lives in a central database and knows your preferences.</li></ul><p><strong>Say a political advocacy group </strong>wants to know where women under 30 get their news, they can use Verb to query one or all the twins who fit that demographic in an interface that feels like ChatGPT.</p><ul><li>If a venture capital firm wants to figure out which apps are trending among young people, they can ask.</li></ul><img src="https://images.axios.com/vhEEOOcWyVdnkTnXqI6LcZ63-kA=/2025/05/20/1747707133286.jpg"> <div>Screenshot via Verb.AI</div><p><strong>The intrigue: </strong>Generation Lab says this method of polling will give companies, nonprofits, and news organizations more accurate information about how young people really think by tracking their behavior instead of asking them about it.</p><ul><li>"For decades, market research has been the equivalent of a doctor asking a patient to describe their symptoms. VERB is an MRI machine," Generation Lab's pitch deck says.</li><li>The polling company is aiming to get to 5,000 users of the tracker by the end of September.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>Many younger Americans consider sharing data the tradeoff for being online. They're already giving away their data for free, and are even more willing to share it for cash.</p><ul><li>88% of Gen Z is open to sharing personal information with social media companies, 20 points higher than older generations, <a href="https://www.emarketer.com/content/privacy-concerns-dont-get-in-way-of-gen-z-enthusiasm-about-ai-enabled-banking" target="_blank">eMarketer notes</a>.</li><li>33% of Gen Z agrees or strongly agrees with the statement “I don’t mind being tracked by websites or apps,” compared with 22% of older adults, according to <a href="https://www.malwarebytes.com/blog/personal/2023/11/what-gen-z-really-cares-about-when-it-comes-to-privacy" target="_blank">a 2023 survey</a> from the cybersecurity company Malwarebytes.</li><li>Gen Z-ers and millennials are also more likely to expect incentives or rewards for sharing data — whether that's money or a personalized social media algorithm, a 2022 Euromonitor International <a href="https://www.euromonitor.com/article/generational-attitudes-and-actions-around-data-privacy" target="_blank">study</a> found.</li></ul><p><strong>Reality check: </strong>Despite their relative comfort with sharing data, Gen Z-ers and millennials are also likelier to pay for increased security or delete data after they're done using a service, <a href="https://www.mckinsey.com/~/media/mckinsey/email/genz/2022/09/27/2022-09-27b.html" target="_blank">McKinsey notes</a>.</p>

Title: AI agents will do programmers' grunt work
Description: <p>AI makers are flooding the market with a new wave of coding <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/02/26/generative-ai-next-act-autonomous-agents" target="_blank">agents</a> promising to relieve human programmers of busy work.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>Automating the routine aspects of technical labor will almost certainly transform and downsize the tech industry workforce — but there's no guarantee it will alleviate software development's biggest headaches.</p><hr><p><strong>Driving the news:</strong> Microsoft Monday <a href="https://github.blog/news-insights/product-news/github-copilot-meet-the-new-coding-agent/" target="_blank">announced</a> a new AI coding agent for Github Copilot that's good for "time-consuming but boring tasks."</p><ul><li>"The agent excels at low-to-medium complexity tasks in well-tested codebases, from adding features and fixing bugs to extending tests, refactoring code, and improving documentation," Microsoft's post says.</li><li>Github's move follows Friday's <a href="https://openai.com/index/introducing-codex/" target="_blank">announcement</a> by OpenAI of Codex, a "research preview" of a new coding agent that can "work on many tasks in parallel."</li><li>Notably, the Github Copilot agent is powered not by Codex or any other tool from Microsoft partner OpenAI, but instead by Anthropic Claude 3.7 Sonnet, per Microsoft.</li></ul><p><strong>The intrigue:</strong> Tech leaders have sent mixed messages on just how much work they see ahead for programmers. </p><ul><li>Amazon Web Services' then-boss Matt Garman caused a stir last year when he suggested the need for human coding <a href="https://developers.slashdot.org/story/24/08/23/1736253/aws-ceo-says-most-developers-could-stop-coding-soon-as-ai-takes-over" target="_blank">could disappear within two years</a>, However, he later told Axios that his comments were taken out of context.</li><li>"I think it's incredibly exciting time for developers," he told us last year. "There's a whole bunch of work that developers do today that's not fun."</li><li>"If you think about documenting your code, if you think about upgrading Java versions, if you think about looking for bugs,  that's that's not what developers love doing. They love thinking about, 'How do I go solve problems?' "</li></ul><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> Business transformations that start in Silicon Valley usually make their way into the wider economy.</p><ul><li>Silicon Valley's "dogfooding" tradition ensures that it will avidly apply new technologies to its own business first.</li><li>Both Microsoft and Google are now <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2025/04/29/microsoft-ceo-says-up-to-30-of-the-companys-code-was-written-by-ai/" target="_blank">claiming</a> that roughly 30% of the code they produce is AI-written.</li></ul><p><strong>Coding agents,</strong> like other generative AI tools, continue to "hallucinate," or make stuff up.</p><ul><li>But programs, unlike other kinds of language products, have a built-in pass-fail test: Either they run or they don't.</li><li>That gives programmers one early checkpoint to guard against bad code.</li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but:</strong> AI-generated code likely also contains tons of other errors that don't show up today. </p><ul><li>That will cause nightmares in the future as programs age, get used more widely, or face unexpected tests from unpredictable users.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>The software industry's assumption that what works inside tech will work everywhere else could be sorely tested when these techniques get pushed out beyond Silicon Valley. </p><ul><li>AI's usefulness in writing code may not easily transfer to other kinds of work that are less abstract and more rooted in physical reality — witness the many setbacks and challenges the autonomous vehicle industry has faced. </li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines:</strong> Nobody doubts that AI means tech firms will write more code using fewer employees. But no one yet knows exactly where these companies will continue to find competitive advantage.</p><ul><li>AI models are much more likely to be interchangeable than human organizations and cultures.</li></ul><p><strong>What's next:  </strong>As coding agents shoulder routine labor, product designers and creative engineers will use "vibe coding" — improvisational rough drafting via "throw it at the wall and see what works" AI prompting — to do fast prototyping of new ideas.</p><p><strong>The bottom line:</strong> The biggest challenges in creating software tend to arise from poorly conceived specifications and misinterpretations of data, both of which are often rooted in confusion over human needs.</p><ul><li>Today's large language models are ill-equipped to tackle those problems. </li><li>But software developers who excel at navigating the boundaries between human desire and machine capability should continue to find themselves in demand.</li></ul>

Title: Gemma 3 Supports Vision-Language Understanding, Long Context Handling, and Improved Multilinguality
Description: <img src="https://res.infoq.com/news/2025/05/gemma3-new-features/en/headerimage/gemma-new-features-header-1747653430294.jpg"/><p>Google’s generative artificial intelligence (AI) model Gemma 3 supports vision-language understanding, long context handling, and improved multi-linguality. In a recent blog post, Google DeepMind and AI Studio teams discussed the new features in Gemma 3. The model also highlights KV-cache memory reduction, a new tokenizer and offers better performance and higher resolution vision encoders.</p> <i>By Srini Penchikala</i>

Title: 成都为何成了中国“最有幸福感城市”
Description: 在经济高速成长期，年轻人离开成都和其他内陆城市前往沿海地区寻找机会。而在经济充满不确定性的当下，许多年轻人开始逃离北上广，选择在成都过上更放松的生活。<p><img src='https://static01.nyt.com/images/2025/05/19/multimedia/00Biz-China-Econ-01-ptwf/00Biz-China-Econ-01-ptwf-articleLarge.jpg' alt='成都动物园，这座城市被誉为“中国最具幸福感城市”。 The New York Times'/></p>                    <p style='text-align: right; color: gray; font-size: 11px!important; line-height: 10px;'>The New York Times</p>                    <p style='text-align: left; color: gray; font-size: 11px!important; line-height: 10px;'>成都动物园，这座城市被誉为“中国最具幸福感城市”。</p>                    

Title: 特朗普贸易战逆风中，G7财长会议谈什么
Description: 今年的G7财长会议气氛可能比往年紧张。特朗普的贸易策略将是美国财长贝森特与各国官员讨论的核心内容，许多经济学家认为这是对全球经济稳定的最大威胁。<p><img src='https://static01.nyt.com/images/2025/05/20/multimedia/20dc-g7-wvpj/20dc-g7-wvpj-articleLarge.jpg' alt='对于财政部长斯科特·贝森特来说，向外国官员解释特朗普政府的关税政策可能是一项挑战。 Pete Marovich for The New York Times'/></p>                    <p style='text-align: right; color: gray; font-size: 11px!important; line-height: 10px;'>Pete Marovich for The New York Times</p>                    <p style='text-align: left; color: gray; font-size: 11px!important; line-height: 10px;'>对于财政部长斯科特·贝森特来说，向外国官员解释特朗普政府的关税政策可能是一项挑战。</p>                    

Title:  大摩中期策略：下半年美元继续跌，但超配美国股债，择时是关键 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">尽管经济增长放缓，且政策不确定性较高，但是摩根士丹利看好美国股债，并预期美元将走弱。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">5月21日，据追风交易台消息，摩根士丹利在最新中期策略展望报告中称，预计下半年美元将继续贬值，但美国股债等资产仍然将是全球资金“避无可避”的选择。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告指出，尽管面临经济增长放缓，叠加前所未有的政策不确定性，但预计至2026年中，美国资产整体表现将优于全球其他市场，理由是关税威胁缓和，降低经济衰退可能性，同时伴随着实质性的货币宽松和监管放松。摩根士丹利称：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">对美国股票持超配立场，预期到明年二季度标普500指数将达到6500点，较当前水平上涨约9%。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/9f684d2a-58b8-425f-9b2f-f4a0b84f05ae.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="352" data-wscnw="1053"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">预计10年期美国国债收益率将降至3.45%，将为固定收益投资者创造约13%的总回报。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">美元指数是大摩唯一预计表现较弱的美国资产，预计美元指数到2026年中将贬值9%至91，欧元兑美元汇率升至1.25，日元兑美元走强至130。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/da3e4d2b-ee73-4849-bdb7-ffb3a4f11e05.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="419" data-wscnw="578"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">大摩还在报告中强调，在政策不确定性加剧的环境中，把握投资时机至关重要。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">美元贬值在所难免，对冲至关重要</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">摩根士丹利认为，美元强势时代或已终结，背后有两大核心驱动力正在消失：<strong>美国相对其他G10经济体的增长优势和收益率优势将大幅减弱</strong>。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告特别指出，更令投资者忧心的是，美国货币政策独立性的疑虑一旦出现，很难被消除。</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">这可能导致外国投资者减少对美资产的配置，转向非美资产，尤其在分配新资金时，同时外国投资者增加对美国资产敞口的货币对冲比例，两者都将给美元带来持续压力。</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">这也是大摩预计欧元、日元、瑞郎等避险货币将受益的一个原因。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">大摩表示，货币对冲将对预期回报和回报分布的波动性产生重要影响，对于以欧元为基础货币的投资者而言，标普500指数的预期回报从未对冲时的0%变为对冲时的7%。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/17f25b26-df5c-4d6f-a9e8-d514d2a4cfe6.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="311" data-wscnw="1171"/></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">美国股债仍是资金“避无可避”的选择</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告称，美元持续走弱无疑会助长&#34;美元资产失去避险吸引力&#34;的叙事，而且在市场上已有异常现象，即4月美国资产遭抛售期间，美元与标普500指数之间的相关性飙升至极端正值。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">这不符合避险货币在股市下跌时应当走强的常规表现。同时，今年以来欧洲股市的资金流入明显更强，也表明美股需求似乎正在减弱。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">但大摩认为，对美元资产需求消失的担忧被过度夸大。数据显示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">全球股票基金对美国的配置变化并未超过过去一季度指数权重的变化。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/69ef74ec-294e-453b-915a-e3ca36185f43.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="565" data-wscnw="699"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">外国持有的美元债券数量达到历史最高，表明非美投资者仍在购买美元资产，尤其是高质量美元资产。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/c99519dc-6f89-42ec-bcfd-05d9bdeffa76.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="523" data-wscnw="695"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告称，美元资产的市场体量仍是无可替代的优势。美国约50万亿美元的可投资股票市值几乎是第二大市场欧洲的五倍，超过一半的高质量流动性固定收益资产以美元计价。<strong>即使资金大规模流出美国资产，可替代的投资市场也极为有限</strong>。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">不过，大摩同时也指出，这并不意味着未来不会出现美元资产的替代品。只是市场规模的转变需要时间，这意味着<strong>当前&#34;别无选择&#34;(TINA)的市场主题仍将持续</strong>。</p>
<p>对于<strong>股票市场</strong>，大摩的策略师认为，中美贸易紧张局势的缓和降低了经济衰退的可能性，并消除了最极端的下行风险。</p>
<p>这意味着，股市短期内不太可能跌破4月份的低点，尤其是考虑到今年迄今为止的大幅下跌主要是对关税冲击的反应。</p>
<p>大摩的股票策略师预计，未来的美国政策议程将更具宽松性。</p>
<p>对于<strong>国债市场</strong>，大摩认为经济放缓和美联储降息最为重要。美债收益率预测更侧重于低增长和宽松政策。</p>
<p>大摩预计美联储降息的次数将超过市场目前的预期，这将导致国债收益率下降，尤其是在2026年初。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">择时是关键</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告称，在2025年的展望中，大摩就提出了&#34;择时至关重要&#34;，认为地缘政治不确定性和高估值意味着投资者应保持灵活应变。在最新的报告中，大摩认为，这一观点仍然适用。下半年关注以下几个政策变化的时机：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>关税政策：</strong>预计市场聚焦的美国重点贸易伙伴的关税水平将持续，会有不断变化的截止日期和潜在临时升级</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>财政政策：</strong>预计第三季度末通过《减税与就业法案》(TCJA)延期</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>金融监管：</strong>巴塞尔协议III终局提案（预计于2025年第四季度）将对证券化产品和金融股产生重大影响。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>货币政策：</strong>美联储料将在2025年剩余时间保持利率不变，直到2026年第一季度才开始降息，全年共降息175个基点，而市场当前仅计价两次降息。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/6e616769-8a80-4dc9-b9ae-2ad878f84fd7.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="571" data-wscnw="714"/></p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">摩根士丹利建议，考虑到政策决定变得与市场一样难以预测，投资者应保持灵活，以把握政策变化带来的投资机会。</p>
<p> </p>

Title:  继续“无人问津”，日本国债的雷，依然没有任何缓解 
Description:  <p>在经历周二债市大幅波动后，日本超长期债券周三几乎没有得到任何喘息的机会。</p>
<p>日本债券市场连续第二天无人出价，30年期和 40 年期日本国债收益率均创下历史新高。20年期日本国债收益率一度上涨1.5个基点至2.57%，创下自2000年10月以来的最高水平。这一收益率在周二跃升了令人震惊的15个基点。同时，30年期收益率下跌1.5个基点至3.110%，较其创纪录的3.14%略有回落，而40年期收益率则在触及周二3.6%的历史峰值后保持在3.595%不变。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/d032bc9b-5bd6-4896-bc46-ca355a38340c.jpeg" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="1025" data-wscnw="1741" data-wscnsize="228135"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">Okasan Securities首席债券策略师Naoya Hasegawa警告：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">要使超长期债券的需求反弹，市场需要获得更大的保证，即将减少新债券的发行，这在本财年内在技术上是可能的。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>此前周二，日本财务省周20年期国债拍卖<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747438?keyword=%E6%9A%B4%E9%9B%B7" target="_blank" rel="noopener">录得灾难性结果</a>。投标倍数仅为2.5倍，远低于上月的2.96倍，创下自2012年以来的最低水平。尾差（Auction Tail，即平均价格与最低接受价格之间的差距）从4月份的0.34飙升至1.14，为1987年以来最高水平。<span data-start="420" data-end="446">市场需求极为低迷，买家基本不愿意接盘长期国债</span>。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/87931917-d93b-42dd-b9dc-a6a80593a87c.jpeg" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="656" data-wscnw="1280"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">日本债券市场今年一直承受着巨大压力，3月由海外德国国债滑坡引发的大规模抛售尤为剧烈。最近，多个政党呼吁减少消费税，这一提议目前被石破茂首相拒绝，但市场担忧最终可能出台财政刺激政策。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">通胀高于目标和财政刺激的可能性为收益率增加了上行压力。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">日本央行目前正尝试减少债券购买并实现货币政策正常化，但超长期收益率的飙升使这一进程面临严峻挑战。更为严重的是，长期借贷成本的上升对高度负债的日本政府来说是一个危险信号。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">日经资产管理公司首席全球策略师Naomi Fink认为，<strong>目前走势突显了日本政府需要注意其使日本恢复基本收支平衡承诺的必要性。</strong>通胀上升预示着日本央行将减少债券购买，使市场更容易受到对价格更敏感的买家需求的影响。</p>
<p>分析认为，<strong>市场情绪在未来几周内可能继续承压，因为30年期债券下周和40年期债券的拍卖即将来临。随着日本央行逐渐退出市场，债券价格将更多地受到对价格敏感的投资者行为影响。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">对于全球投资者而言，这一发展表明日本的超宽松货币政策时代可能即将结束，这将对全球利率市场产生深远影响。随着全球主要经济体债务水平普遍攀升，日本债市的动荡可能成为其他高负债国家的预警信号。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"> </p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  德银：大家都知道美债不可持续，但不知道何时会崩溃 
Description:  <p>当美国债务危机真正爆发时，后果将比我们想象的更为严重。</p>
<p>周三，德意志银行主题策略师Jim Reid在其最新的每日图表分析中指出:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>金融市场最广泛认同的事实之一就是美国国债处于不可持续的路径上，最大的未知数是何时会崩溃，关税可能加速了这一危机的到来。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Reid认为，无论是通过有意为之还是纯粹偶然，美国的&#34;过度特权&#34;——即以远低于公允价值的成本借款的能力——正在逐渐消退，美元的储备货币地位也在弱化。</p>
<p>根据报告，这种特权使美国的借贷成本降低约70个基点，使其在不增加利息负担的情况下能够承担额外25个百分点的债务与GDP比率，而债务与GDP比率或将在未来十年飙升至200%以上。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/9c1f5118-774b-4a16-a65c-c88f6c3403f9.jpeg" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="496" data-wscnw="1194" data-wscnsize="63688"/></p>
<p>在穆迪下调美国主权评级后的首个交易日，美股不仅没有下跌，反而收高。这与2011年8月标普首次下调美国评级后股市暴跌7%的情况形成鲜明对比。有分析认为，答案简单明了：“投资者已接受美国债务将以荒谬速度扩张的事实...直到灾难真正来临。”</p>
<h2>美国债务末日图：未来恐怖轨迹已定</h2>
<p>虽然穆迪取消美国最后一个AAA评级不应让任何人感到震惊，但这无疑是美国财政大厦上出现的另一道裂缝。穆迪的理由特别直接：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>他们假设2017年减税政策将被延续（与国会预算办公室最近的估计不同），这将推动债务和赤字大幅上升，其关键预测包括：</p>
<ol>
<li>利息支出加上强制性支出将从2024年占联邦支出的73%上升到2035年的78%；</li>
<li>财政赤字将从占GDP的6.4%上升到2035年约9%；</li>
<li>债务与GDP比率将从当前的98%上升到2035年的134%；</li>
</ol>
</blockquote>
<p>Jim Reid在他的分析中，将这些预测与美国债务和赤字的历史趋势以及国会预算办公室的半年度预测进行了对比。虽然国会预算办公室的基准预测不包括减税延期，但其替代方案之一（包含减税延期）显示，未来几十年债务与GDP比率将超过200%。对于好奇&#34;灾难将至&#34;在未来会是什么样子的人来说，它将沿着债务末日图表中的淡蓝线某处出现。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/1f5fa47c-a53d-45f1-b070-e36884219b2c.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="453" data-wscnw="1280" data-wscnsize="210067"/></p>
<p> </p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  泡泡玛特的无限游戏有危险了 
Description:  <p style="text-align: right;"><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/6baa4f4a-0dfb-49fd-8050-b28a547d65ae.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="454" data-wscnw="843" data-wscnsize="540156"/>作者 | 王小娟</p>
<p style="text-align: right;">编辑 | 黄昱</p>
<p>最近，泡泡玛特家的“顶流艺人”LABUBU又升咖了。</p>
<p>在不久前的巴黎时装周上，泰国公主思蕊梵娜瓦瑞被拍到在爱马仕包上挂了LABUBU。这让不少时尚圈的弄潮儿争相效仿，在爱马仕、LV等大牌包上，也挂上LABUBU。</p>
<p>去年以来，在全球不少门店，抢LABUBU的人排出数百米长队。体现在对泡泡玛特业绩的贡献上，2024年，LABUBU所在的THE MONSTERS系列营收高达30.4亿元，同比增长726.6%，占到了泡泡玛特总营收的23.3%。</p>
<p>LABUBU在全球大受欢迎，泡泡玛特也成为二级市场上最被追捧的股票之一。5月20日盘中，其股价一度来到212.2港元/股，再次刷新其最高股价记录，市值也短暂超过了2800亿港元。</p>
<p>但泡泡玛特的生意也是一门无限的游戏，需要持续打造被追捧的爆款IP。不然，当如今的“女明星”过气，用户的新鲜感消失之后，泡泡玛特可能又会像几年前一样陷入低迷。</p>
<p>能不能培养出下一个顶流，是市场当前对泡泡玛特的新期待。</p>
<h2 data-header="4" data-foldable="true" data-default-linespacing="100">爆款养成</h2>
<p>即使不怎么关注潮玩的人，这两年也在社交媒体上刷到过一个有着毛茸茸的身体、尖尖的耳朵、总是露出九颗牙坏笑的淘气精灵搪胶毛绒玩偶。</p>
<p>她就是LABUBU，是中国香港艺术家龙家升创作的“THE MONSTERS”（精灵天团）系列中一个，由泡泡玛特独家签约并进行运营。经过几年的养成，如今已经成长为泡泡玛特旗下当红的“女明星”。</p>
<p>LABUBU和她的伙伴们被泡泡玛特于2018年签约，过去几年也一直不温不火。其去年爆火，离不开名人们的“带货”，也离不开泰国市场的助推。</p>
<p>在过去的一年里，她被泰国出生的女团偶像Lisa疯狂扫货，被泰国公主思蕊梵娜瓦瑞挂在爱马仕上。甚至，泰国官方也在为这一IP的爆火添砖加瓦。去年，身穿泰国服饰的LABUBU人偶到达泰国机场，泰国旅游与体育部部长瑟姆萨·蓬帕尼的亲自前来接机，并为其授予“神奇泰国体验官”的称号。</p>
<p>最近，在社交媒体上，LABUBU则一跃成为爱马仕等一众大牌包的首选挂饰。甚至有网友表示：“因为LABUBU要买人生第一款高奢包了。”这意味着，LABUBU甚至可以反向带货爱马仕了。</p>
<p>这CP看似抽象，但其实两者有很多相似之处。一个是“配货界祖师爷”，一个是“潮玩界SSR”，两者都擅长通过饥饿营销来制造稀缺性。</p>
<p>众所周知，爱马仕有着一套非常严格的配货机制，不同的消费等级，对应着不同级别的包。而想买到泡泡玛特家的当家女明星，也是需要一系列复杂的流程，比如限时抢购、捆绑非热门商品销售等，而如果想要拿到隐藏款，则需要持续不断开盲盒。</p>
<p>如此来看，这俩一个靠配货制度拿捏贵妇，一个靠隐藏款套路“收割”年轻人，都是社交货币极度内卷之下的产物。以前贵妇们拼铂金包的鳄鱼皮纹路，和现在潮人们拼LABUBU的稀有度，本质上是同一个逻辑。</p>
<p>甚至在社交媒体上，有行业人士分析，买爱马仕和买LABUBU的都是同一批人，都愿意为情绪价值买单。</p>
<p>在二手的逻辑上，两者都有很多相似之处。爱马仕在包界一直有着相对不错的保值性，而二手市场上，LABUBU也因为足够稀缺，成为炒娃客的最新理财产品。</p>
<p>如今成为CP之后，爱马仕也焕发出更多年轻活力气质，而泡泡玛特也再次升咖。</p>
<p>LABUBU在东南亚爆火的同时，泡泡玛特也加码在海外点燃这一热情。</p>
<p>而在海外新店的选址上，泡泡玛特选择各大核心地标商圈，和一众奢侈品成为邻居。在法国，其将门店开在巴黎奥斯曼大道，靠近老佛爷百货；在英国，门店位于伦敦牛津街，毗邻John Lewis百货及伦敦艺术大学。</p>
<p>门店本身开在核心商圈，又辅以限量款、联名款等手段，泡泡玛特各地的门店成为了游客与本地潮人的社交打卡中心，天然具备高曝光度和流量转化优势。</p>
<p>前段时间，LABUBU在全球发售第三代搪胶毛绒产品“前方高能”系列，当晚美国门店现场大排长龙，次日，泡泡玛特APP登顶美国App Store购物榜，这也是该官方应用在购物榜的首次登顶，并一跃成为 App Store免费总榜的第四名。</p>
<p>可见，全世界都在为这一只丑萌兔子疯狂，也让其化身为泡泡玛特的印钞机。</p>
<p>根据泡泡玛特2024年的财报，LABUBU带着它的怪物家族狂揽30亿元，相当于每天睁眼就有830万元进账。</p>
<p>整体来看，THE MONSTERS也贡献了泡泡玛特130.38亿元营收的23.3%，而在2023年时，这一系列占营收的比重仅为5.8%，从各系列对业绩的贡献来看，THE MONSTERS是去年泡泡玛特业绩的关键变量。</p>
<h2 data-header="4" data-foldable="true" data-default-linespacing="100">无限游戏</h2>
<p>THE MONSTERS系列的爆火，也让泡泡玛特的股价走出前几年的阴霾期，去年以来持续冲高。到5月20日，泡泡玛特盘中最高股价达到212.2港元/股，市值也一度超过2800亿港元。</p>
<p>在这一轮上涨中，摩根士丹利的分析师指出由于LABUBU V3在全球的需求强劲，尤其是美国市场，将带动新店开业，成为2025至26年的关键增长因素。</p>
<p>但潮玩本身是一个无限的游戏，需要持续创造新品来吸引用户注意力。</p>
<p>LABUBU大火之后，要面对的是同质化的竞争和用户审美的疲劳，泡泡玛特也不是说就能依靠LABUBU而高枕无忧了。</p>
<p>尽管当前LABUBU已经能和爱马仕炒“CP”了，但是其和爱马仕还是有很多不同。爱马仕依旧在奢侈品界拥有统治性的地位，但在潮玩市场，LABUBU的爆火具有一定的偶然性。爱马仕能穿越一个个审美周期，但LABUBU很可能像此前的众多同行一样，有一天也沦为时代的眼泪。</p>
<p>毕竟，公主的爱马仕上，今天可能挂LABUBU，明天就有可能挂Jellycat。在爱马仕上，人们很少去讨论审美疲劳，而在潮玩上面，总是新品更令人期待。可以说，这对CP中，爱马仕的铁打的，而LABUBU们则是流动的。</p>
<p>潮玩本身就有自己的生命周期。比如，曾一年赚数十亿，亚洲吸金天团LINE FRIENDS也在2021年关闭了最后中国内地最后一家线下门店。而从大火时排队需要数小时到关店退场，仅过了5年。</p>
<p>值得一提的时，LINE FRIENDS关店前后的2021年4月，泡泡玛特发售了一款地球女儿400%限量款，引发排队“抢娃”，现场堪比春运。但几年过去，尽管Molly系列依旧贡献着泡泡玛特16%的营收，但一个明显的特点是，当年的Molly还是C位顶流，现在只能给LABUBU当陪衬。</p>
<p>可见，潮玩圈没有永远的神，只有永远的“新神替代旧神”。</p>
<p>而泡泡玛特也一直在抓紧培养一堆“练习生”，以期在LABUBU过气后，能顺利承接。但爆火除了运营之外，还有一定的运气成分，存在巨大的不确定性。当前，泡泡玛特依靠中国强大的供应链，在海外市场驰骋，但从IP来看，能打的IP主要还是LABUBU，IP迭代问题很有可能在未来一段时间困扰到泡泡玛特。</p>
<p>要知道，这样的过往经历并不是没有。在Molly热度褪去，且盲盒生意被更严格的监管约束之后，泡泡玛特在2022年前后经历过一段火热IP青黄不接的时期。那段时间，股价一度跌破10港元/股。这也说明，泡泡玛特股价波动与IP的受欢迎程度有很大的关系。</p>
<p>除了IP的承接这个最大的不确定性之外，疯狂的二手交易也在成为其风险。</p>
<p>当前，LABUBU新品不少在二手市场有着数十倍的溢价。而随着新品的上市，此前的款大打折扣，但黄牛囤货规模一直在膨胀。</p>
<p>二手市场会为爆火按下加速键，也会是爆冷的助推器。如若二手市场持续过热，很可能像此前盲盒过热一样，引发监管的下场；而如果随着市场热度退散，泡沫破裂，黄牛不再炒作，很可能会加速这一IP的衰落，泡泡玛特本身也会受到影响。</p>
<p>就资本市场而言，根据最新的股价，泡泡玛特的市盈率已经超过80倍，处于比较高的水平，当前股价存在一定的泡沫。</p>
<p>此前，已有一些资本开始撤出。蜂巧资本（BORCHID CAPITAL）发文称，由于蜂巧人民币一期基金即将到期，蜂巧资本于近一周内通过大宗交易分三次集中出清了所有在上市前买入的泡泡玛特股份。据港交所信息，蜂巧资本套现金额超过22亿港元。</p>
<p>除了蜂巧资本，2024年以来，包括黑蚁资本、王宁夫妇在内的多位股东已累计减持超20亿港元。一众资本的退出，也意味着泡泡玛特正在向成熟的潮玩IP公司转变，未来也更加考验公司自身的运营能力。</p>
<p>无限游戏在继续，尽管如今站在山巅，但泡泡玛特仍需持续洞察未来审美与情绪，找到接替LABUBU的新明星，才能保持当前的势头。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  如何看美债近期抛售？瑞银：主因“经济衰退”概率降低，并非外资抛售或债务失控等宏大叙事 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">近期美债市场经历剧烈波动，2年期美债收益率过去一个月飙升42个基点，10年、30年期美债收益率分别突破4.3%和4.5%心理关口。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据追风交易台消息，针对市场热议的“外资撤离美债”“美国债务危机”等结构性解释，瑞银全球利率策略团队在最新报告中指出，<strong>本轮美债抛售的核心驱动力实为周期性因素——美国“经济衰退”概率降低，而非市场担忧的长期结构性风险。</strong></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">“经济<strong>衰退</strong>”<strong>概率下降</strong>，2年期美债成市场风暴眼</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">瑞银研报指出，关于长期利率上行的结构性解释如外资撤离、赤字担忧等甚嚣尘上，但通过拆解收益率曲线发现，当前市场波动主要集中在反应周期性叙事的2年期美债收益率上。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">自4月30日以来，2年期美债收益率飙升42个基点，这主要是由于市场对2025年美联储降息幅度的预期减少50个基点。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">与此同时，美债2年期与5年期、5年期与10年期以及10年期与30年期收益率利差仅温和趋平，这些利差在过去一个月的波动幅度均未超过10个基点。<strong>这表明本轮美债波动主因为“经济衰退”概率的变化，而非持久的结构性转变。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/ac061e9b-9b04-44b5-846f-f08b1a18808d.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="455" data-wscnw="527"/></strong></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #948f8f;">图1：近期市场波动集中在2年期，显示周期性因素（衰退概率下降）主导抛售</span></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">债市结构性压力并不明显</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">针对市场热议的美债危机，瑞银指出，从更长期来看美债确实出现了结构性变化，但并非近期出现。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">瑞银报告显示，当前美债2年期与5年期利差与短端利率的关系已回归至2015年前水平，结束了过去十年相对于利率水平而言极为平坦的收益率曲线。但这一关系变化主要发生在2024年，而非近期。这表明曲线陡峭化是市场机制的自然调整，而非债务危机驱动。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/308b9725-79ee-4ad3-9a08-d070e6b1265a.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="445" data-wscnw="1061"/></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #b3b3b3;">图3：利率曲线形态回归至2015年前水平；图4：美债“期限溢价”攀升</span></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">瑞银认为，从目前水平看，利率不太可能大幅走高，30年期债券收益率接近5%时可能为长期投资者提供有吸引力的入场机会。短期风险主要来自未来几个月可能走高的CPI数据。</p>

Title:  昔日碳化硅巨头Wolfspeed准备申请破产，美股盘后跳水60% 
Description:  <p>半导体供应商Wolfspeed正准备申请破产保护，股价暴跌超60%，看空期权交易创纪录。</p>
<p>5月20日美股盘后，据媒体报道，<strong>美国芯片制造商Wolfspeed公司正准备在数周内申请破产保护，该公司正艰难应对其债务危机</strong>。在拒绝了债权人提出的多项庭外债务重组方案后，该公司计划申请第11章破产保护，这一申请将得到其大多数债权人的支持。</p>
<p>作为碳化硅芯片制造商，Wolfspeed本月早些时候已表达了对自身持续经营能力的担忧，并预测其年收入将低于预期。公司预计2026年收入将达到8.5亿美元，但这一数字远低于分析师预期的9.587亿美元。而<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3744178" target="_blank" rel="noopener">此前3月底</a>，Wolfspeed芯片法案拨款悬而未决以及可转债再融资遇阻曾暴跌50%。周二破产重组消息后，美股盘后，Wolfspeed跳水60%。<img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/de64a7b8-d833-4302-a1dd-d086e16917b0.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="505" data-wscnw="695"/></p>
<p>根据媒体报道，周二有交易者大幅增加了对Wolfspeed的看空押注。接近7万份7月到期的看跌期权合约（相当于700万股股票）交易活跃，大部分交易发生在市场收盘前的最后半小时。看跌期权交易总量创下363,000手的历史纪录，如果这一价格水平在周三保持，看跌期权买家可能会获得丰厚利润。</p>
<h2>昔日碳化硅巨头，如今破产在即</h2>
<p>作为拥有全球首家8英寸碳化硅晶圆厂的碳化硅巨头，Wolfspeed曾名噪一时。</p>
<p>Wolfspeed原为Cree主营第三代化合物半导体业务的部门，公司技术最初商业化应用于LED市场，致力于推动LED照明变革。</p>
<p>自2017年以来，Cree开始战略性转型，将发展重心转移至Wolfspeed部门，为其核心功率和射频业务提供发展基金。2021年10月Cree正式更名为Wolfspeed，专注于第三代化合物半导体领域的开发与创新。</p>
<p>在过去几年里，新能源汽车、光伏、储能、工业控制等领域对碳化硅半导体应用的需求，确实给Wolfspeed带来巨大的想象空间。尤其是这几年发展较为火热的新能源汽车行业对碳化硅大量的需求，更是促进了行业的发展。目前，超过60%的碳化硅需求来自新能源汽车。</p>
<p><strong>在全球碳化硅产业掀起的增资扩产热潮和美国《</strong><span data-pm-slice="1 1 [&#34;para&#34;,{&#34;tagName&#34;:&#34;p&#34;,&#34;attributes&#34;:{&#34;style&#34;:&#34;text-align: justify;&#34;},&#34;namespaceURI&#34;:&#34;http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml&#34;}]"><strong>芯片与科学法案》的推动下，Wolfspeed一马当先，在碳化硅领域投入了大量的资金</strong>。</span>奈尔·雷诺兹曾表示，2021—2024财年是最重要的投资时期，公司正在执行产能扩张计划，包括莫霍克谷8英寸碳化硅晶圆厂的产能建设、6英寸碳化硅晶圆厂达勒姆工厂的产能扩充等。另外，Wolfspeed还在建设新的材料工厂（JPSilerCity）。</p>
<p><strong>但好景不长，被认为是碳化硅最大市场的新能源汽车却没有带来想象中的大量订单</strong>。近期，欧美纯电动汽车市场需求放缓，更是让很多汽车制造商推迟了车规级半导体订单。市场调研机构Yole分析数据显示，<strong>从短中期来看，2024年电动汽车市场的需求放缓对SiC器件市场产生了重大影响</strong>。</p>
<p>在过去的一年里，Wolfspeed已经解雇CEO，关闭一家工厂，并裁员20%，以应对其股价自疫情期间达到峰值以来暴跌90%以上的情况。今年3月7日，Wolfspeed在向美国证券交易委员会提交的文件中透露，将再裁员180人，主要在北卡罗来纳州达勒姆和赛勒城的工厂。</p>
<p><strong>投资机构JanaPartners认为，Wolfspeed管理层在资本配置、执行和战略方面的失误导致公司经营出现巨大问题，股价持续崩盘</strong>。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  关税阴霾下，日本出口连续第二个月放缓 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">日本政府周三公布的数据显示，该国4月出口同比增长2%，为连续第二个月放缓。这是自去年10月以来的最低增速，也是自去年9月出口萎缩1.7%后的最差表现。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">同时，日本当月进口同比萎缩2.2%，降幅小于预期的4.5%。日本贸易逆差缩小至1158亿日元（约8.031亿美元），低于预期的2271亿日元，3月贸易逆差为5594亿日元。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">关税冲击下，日本4月GDP数据陷入萎缩。日本政府初步数据显示，今年第一季度实际国内生产总值按年率计算萎缩0.7%，主要受到私人消费停滞和出口增长放缓的拖累。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">关税高压政策：日本制造业承压</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">媒体报道指出，<strong>当前，日本对美国的汽车、钢铁和铝材出口正面临25%的高额关税。海关数据显示，汽车是日本对美最大的出口商品，2024年占所有对美出口的28.3%。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">作为美国的关键盟友，日本同时还受到特朗普对大多数贸易伙伴征收的10%基准关税的影响。此外，日本商品还面临24%的“对等关税”，不过这部分关税目前已被暂时搁置。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">特朗普政府于4月2日对包括日本在内的180多个国家征收“对等关税”，随后设置了“90天关税宽限期”，允许贸易伙伴与其进行贸易谈判。而关税的不确定性对依赖出口的日本经济构成了持续风险，日本出口导向型企业或面临的进一步盈利压力。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>

Title:  华硕CEO：AI PC仍需1-2年才能实现 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">在关税冲击与AI技术生态滞后的双重压力下，AI PC（人工智能电脑）行业正仍然面临挑战。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">根据彭博社报道，华硕CEO胡书宾（Samson Hu）在接受采访时坦言，AI PC还需一两年才能兑现承诺，新一代AI PC可能需要等到2026年或更晚才能推动市场发展。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">尽管各大厂商包括华硕和联想集团去年接连推出AI PC，但这并未能提振低迷的笔记本市场。更雪上加霜的是，美国新政府最近宣布的一系列关税政策，进一步降低了今年的市场预期。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>胡书宾表示，华硕可能考虑将美国售价上调多达10%以抵消关税成本。他直言：“PC行业市场增长率的最初估计约为5%，但由于关税政策的不确定性，现在大多数估计已经降至1%或2%，甚至可能持平。”</strong>这一悲观预测反映了整个科技行业对贸易摩擦升级的担忧。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">这位掌舵全球前五大PC厂商的CEO透露，消费者对电脑的支出受制于全球经济担忧和关税影响，同时，因为现有软件尚不成熟，人工智能未能如预期般吸引用户。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">胡书宾称，虽然支持AI任务的硬件已经上市销售，包括微软一年前在2024年Computex上推出的Copilot+ PC，但行业可能还需要一到两年时间，直到第三方应用开发者构建能够充分利用这些功能的软件。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>
